Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Torah Prophecy of Ishmael's Descendant
Sanusi interprets the prophecy about Hagar's son as referring to Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets a biblical prophecy about Ishmael's descendant as evidence of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
A prophecy from Genesis points uniquely to Muhammad's universal mission.

This lesson presents another scriptural testimony, this time from the Torah. Sanusi cites God's promise to Abraham about Hagar's son: 'his hand shall be above all,' and argues that this could only refer to Muhammad. The analysis shows how the description of universal dominance and submission applies to Islam's global spread.

Guided Path
1
Read the Torah prophecy
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key phrases: 'hand above all' and 'hand extended in humility'.
This is a direct quote from the first book of the Torah (Genesis).
2
Identify the interpretation
Sanusi explains that this prophecy refers to none other than Muhammad, because no other descendant of Hagar achieved such universal dominance.
He mentions the previous dominance of the Children of Israel.
3
Understand the evidence
The proof lies in the universal prophethood of Muhammad and the victory of Islam over all religions.
4
Contrast with previous situation
Sanusi notes that before, the hand (authority) belonged to the Israelites, but now it belongs to Muslims.
This shows the shift in prophethood to Ishmael's line.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: ما جاءَ في السفرِ الأَوَّلِ مِنَ التوراة: أنَّهُ تعالى قالَ لإبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( إنَّ هاجر تله، ويكونُ مِنْ ولدها مَنْ تكون يده فوق الجميع، ويد الجميع مبسوطة إليه بالخشوع )، ولا خفاءَ أنه لم يكنْ مِنْ ولد هاجرَ مَنْ يدُه فوق الجميع غير نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ؛ فإنَّهُ بُعِثَ إلى أهل الأرض كافةً، وأظهر الله تعالى دينَهُ على الأديان كلها، وأذعن له جميع أهل الأرض، وبسطوا أيديهم إليه بالذِّلَّةِ والخشوع بعدما كانَتِ اليد لولدِ إسرائيل الذي هو يعقوب بن إسحاق عليهما الصلاة والسلام؛ إذْ أكثرُ الأنبياءِ مِنْ وَلدِهِ.
And among them: what came in the first book of the Torah that He, the Exalted, said to Abraham (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Indeed Hagar will bear, and from her son will be one whose hand is above all, and the hand of all will be extended to him in humility.' And it is no secret that no one from Hagar's descendants had his hand above all except our prophet and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace); for he was sent to all the people of the earth, and Allah Exalted made his religion manifest over all religions, and all the people of the earth submitted to him, and they extended their hands to him in humiliation and humility, after the hand used to be for the children of Israel, who is Jacob son of Isaac (peace be upon them), for most prophets were from his descendants.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage presents a third scriptural proof, this time from Genesis. The author cites God's promise to Abraham regarding Hagar's son, that his hand would be above all and all would submit to him. The author asserts that this prophecy uniquely describes Muhammad, who was sent universally and whose religion triumphed over all others. The phrase 'hand above all' is explained as universal dominance of Islam, and the submission of people is seen in the widespread acceptance of the Prophet. The author contrasts this with the earlier dominance of the Israelites, noting that most previous prophets came from Jacob's line.

Key Terms
السفر الأول
هاجر
يده فوق الجميع
الخشوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prophecy refers to a worldly conqueror, not a spiritual leader.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that 'hand above all' signifies universal prophethood and religious dominance, not mere military conquest.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does 'his hand above all' signify about Ishmael's descendant?
A) Military conquest
B) Universal prophethood and dominance of his religion
C) Wealth
D) Long life

Key Takeaway
The prophecy in Genesis about Ishmael's descendant is fulfilled uniquely in Muhammad's universal prophethood and the global triumph of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Muhammad (PBUH) is the universal leader to whom all people owe submission? In what area of your life—your career, relationships, or habits—are you still holding back from extending your hands to him in humility? What would it cost you to surrender that area completely?
?
The Children of Israel once held the hand of prophethood, but now it has passed to the followers of Muhammad. Are you living as if you belong to that universal community, or do you treat Islam as just one option among many? How would your daily choices change if you really felt the weight of being part of the final and universal message?
?
This prophecy was preserved even in a corrupted Torah. If Allah ensured that a sign pointing to Muhammad survived centuries of distortion, how much more should you trust that He will preserve your faith? What doubts about Islam's truth do you still entertain, and what step will you take this week to replace that doubt with certainty based on such clear proofs?

Prophethood

The Paraclete in the Gospel as Muhammad
Sanusi cites Gospel passages about the Paraclete and interprets them as referring to Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses Gospel passages about the Paraclete to argue for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
Gospel promises of the Paraclete point to Muhammad, not the Holy Spirit.

Sanusi turns to the Gospel, specifically John, to find prophecies of Muhammad. He quotes two passages that speak of a 'Paraclete' who will come after Jesus, and then explains key phrases to reinterpret them as referring to the Prophet. This lesson follows his argumentative strategy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Gospel quotes
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two quotes from the 'fourteenth' and 'fifteenth' books (chapters of John). Both mention the Paraclete.
2
Identify the Paraclete description
In the first quote, the Paraclete is promised to be with believers forever. In the second, he is called 'Spirit of Truth' who will teach and remind. Sanusi identifies him as 'spirit of truth and certainty'.
3
Examine Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi explains that 'my Father' means 'my Lord and God', rejecting sonship. The phrase 'in my name' is partly given; think about how this redefines the Paraclete as a prophet sent by God.
The explanation of 'in my name' is truncated in our source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإنجيل: فمنها: ما ورد في المصحفِ الرابع عشر: ( أنا أطلب لكم إلى أبي حتى يمنحكم ويعطيكم بارقليط ليكون معكم إلى الأبدِ )، والبارقليط: روح الحق واليقين. وفي الخامس عشر: ( فأمَّا بارقليط روح القدس الذي يرسله أبي باسمي هو يُعلِّمُكم ويمنحكم جميعَ الأشياء، وهو يُذكِّرُكم ما قلتُ لكم )، ثم قال: ( وإني أخبرتكم بهذا قبل أن يكونَ؛ حتى إذا كانَ ذلكَ تؤمنونَ به ). قوله: ( أبي ) معناه: ربي وإلهي، وقوله: ( باسمي ) يعني: ...
And as for the Gospel: among them: what is reported in the fourteenth book: 'I ask for you from my Father that He may grant you and give you a Paraclete to be with you forever.' And the Paraclete is the spirit of truth and certainty. And in the fifteenth: 'But the Paraclete, the Holy Spirit, whom my Father will send in my name, will teach you and grant you all things, and will remind you of what I have said to you.' Then he said: 'And I have told you this before it happens, so that when it does happen, you may believe in it.' His statement: 'my Father' means: my Lord and God, and his statement: 'in my name' means: ...
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage provides evidence from the Gospel (John) regarding the coming of the Paraclete. The author quotes two passages: one from the fourteenth chapter where Jesus promises to send the Paraclete, and another from the fifteenth chapter describing the Paraclete as the spirit of truth who will teach and remind. The author identifies the Paraclete as 'the spirit of truth and certainty'. Then he begins to explain the words of Jesus, clarifying that 'my Father' means 'my Lord and God', thus rejecting any literal sonship. The explanation of 'in my name' is cut off, but the proof is clear: the Paraclete is interpreted as the promised prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms
الإنجيل
المصحف الرابع عشر
المصحف الخامس عشر
بارقليط
روح الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Paraclete in the Gospel is the Holy Spirit, a divine person.
Correction: Sanusi argues the Paraclete is a created being, specifically the Prophet Muhammad, sent by God.

Checkpoint
How does the author explain the Gospel phrase 'my Father'?
A) It means a literal divine father-son relationship
B) It means 'my Lord and God'
C) It refers to a human father
D) It is a metaphor for the church

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses Gospel passages to argue that the Paraclete, promised by Jesus, is a prophecy of Muhammad, reinterpreting Christian scripture to support Islamic prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Jesus promised a Paraclete who would be with the believers forever. If you truly believe that this Paraclete is Muhammad, how does this change the way you view the relationship between your faith and the previous scriptures? Will you now read the Bible with new eyes? What personal responsibility does this place on you to understand the previous prophets' messages?
?
The passage interprets 'in my name' as something that is cut off. But it challenges you to consider: Are you willing to follow the messenger sent after Jesus, even if it requires reinterpreting familiar texts? What is one specific claim of the Gospel that you now see differently because of this lesson?
?
The author uses these verses to affirm the prophethood of Muhammad. How does this knowledge impact your conviction in the message of Islam? Are there any doubts you have about the prophethood that this evidence addresses? What will you do with this certainty?

Torah Prophecy: The Hand Above All
Sanusi cites a Torah prophecy and interprets it as referring to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the Torah prophecy about Hagar's offspring as a proof for Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Torah foretold a universal leader from Hagar's line—fulfilled only by Muhammad.

In this passage, Sanusi begins his scriptural proofs by citing a Torah prophecy. He argues that the prophecy about one from Hagar's offspring having his hand above all can only refer to the Prophet Muhammad, given his universal mission and the submission of all people to him. This lesson walks through that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Torah prophecy
Read the Arabic and translation of the prophecy carefully. Note the key phrase: 'يده فوق الجميع' (his hand above all).
This is a direct quote from the Torah as understood by Sanusi.
2
Identify Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi interprets 'his hand above all' as universal dominance. Notice how he contrasts this with the earlier dominance of the Children of Israel.
He says the hand was with the Children of Israel before Muhammad.
3
Understand why it must be Muhammad
Sanusi argues that no other descendant of Hagar attained universal dominance. Muhammad was sent to all peoples, his religion prevailed, and all submitted to him.
This is a simple argument from uniqueness.
4
Reflect on the proof's strength
Consider why Sanusi uses this as a proof. It shows that previous scriptures contain clear references to Muhammad.
This is a common method in kalam: using earlier prophecies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : ما جاءَ في السفرِ الأَوَّلِ مِنَ التوراة : أنَّهُ تعالى قالَ لإبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام : إنَّ هاجر تله ، ويكونُ مِنْ ولدها مَنْ تكون يده فوق الجميع ، ويد الجميع مبسوطة إليه بالخشوع ، ولا خفاءَ أنه لم يكنْ مِنْ ولد هاجرَ مَنْ يدُه فوق الجميع غير نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ فإنَّهُ بُعِثَ إلى أهل الأرض كافةً ، وأظهر الله تعالى دينَهُ على الأديان كلها ، وأذعن له جميع أهل الأرض ، وبسطوا أيديهم إليه بالذِّلَّةِ والخشوع بعدما كانَتِ اليد لولدِ إسرائيل الذي هو يعقوب بن إسحاق عليهما الصلاة والسلام ؛ إذْ أكثرُ الأنبياءِ مِنْ وَلدِهِ .
وأما الإنجيل : فمنها : ما ورد في المصحفِ الرابع عشر : أنا أطلب لكم إلى أبي حتى يمنحكم ويعطيكم بارقليط ليكون معكم إلى الأبدِ ، والبارقليط : روح الحق واليقين وفي الخامس عشر : فأمَّا بارقليط روح القدس الذي يرسله أبي باسمي هو يُعلِّمُكم ويمنحكم جميعَ الأشياء ، وهو يُذكِّرُكم ما قلتُ لكم ، ثم قال : وإني أخبرتكم بهذا قبل أن يكونَ ؛ حتى إذا كانَ ذلكَ تؤمنونَ به
قوله : أبي معناه : ربي وإلهي ، وقوله : باسمي يعني : بالنبوَّةِ ، ومعنى البارقليط : النبيُّ كاشف الخفيَّاتِ
و معنى كونِهِ روحَ الحقِّ واليقين وروح القدس ؛ أي : العدل ؛ يعني : أنَّ هذهِ الأشياء التي هي الحقُّ واليقين والعدل كالميت لا حراك لها ، بل هي مدفونةٌ خفيَّةٌ لا يُعوّل عليها ، والبارقليط عليهِ الصلاة والسلام إذا بُعِثَ هو كالروح لها ، فترجع حيَّةٌ قائمةً في الأرضِ ولا شك أنَّ الذي أحيا الله تعالى به الحق واليقينَ والعدل ، ويبقى شرعُهُ معَ الخلْقِ إلى الأبد بعد عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلامُ ، وبعدما خمدَ الحَقُّ مِنَ الأرضِ ، وأُحيي الباطل وانتشر . . إنَّما هو خاتم النبيينَ ، ومَنْ هو رحمة لجميع العالمينَ ؛ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .
وفي المصحفِ السادس عشرَ مِنَ الإنجيل : أقولُ لكمُ الآنَ حقاً يقيناً : إِنَّ انطلاقي عنكم خير لكم ؛ فإن لم أنطلق عنكم إلى أبي لم يأتكم البارقليط ، وإن انطلقتُ أرسلتُ بهِ إليكم ، فإذا ما جاءَ هو يفيدُ أهلَ العالم ويُدينهم ويُوبِّخُهم ويوقفُهم على الخطيئة والبر ، ثم قال : إذا جاءَ روح الحقِّ واليقين يرشدكم ويُعلِّمُكم ويُدبِّرُكم بجميعِ الخلْقِ ؛ لأنَّهُ ليسَ يتكلَّمُ بدعةٌ مِنْ تلقاءِ نفسِهِ
ومعنى انطلاقِ عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى أبيه - أي : ربَّهِ تعالى جل وعزّ - : انطلاقه إلى محلّ كرامته ورفعتِهِ ، والاستراحةُ مِنَ الناس بتوجيه القلبِ إِلى الجَوَلانِ في جلالِ اللهِ تعالى وعظمته ، على
And among them: what came in the first book of the Torah: that He, exalted, said to Abraham (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Indeed, Hagar will give birth, and from her offspring will be one whose hand will be above all, and the hand of all will be stretched out to him in humility.' And there is no concealment that there was none from the offspring of Hagar whose hand was above all except our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace and blessings of God be upon him); for he was sent to all the people of the earth, and God manifested His religion over all religions, and all the people of the earth submitted to him, and stretched out their hands to him in abasement and humility after the hand had been for the Children of Israel, who is Jacob son of Isaac (peace and blessings be upon them both); for most of the prophets were from his offspring. As for the Gospel: among them is what is reported in the fourteenth chapter: 'I ask for you from my Father that He grant you and give you a Paraclete to be with you forever.' And the Paraclete is the spirit of truth and certainty. And in the fifteenth: 'As for the Paraclete, the Spirit of Holiness, whom my Father will send in my name, he will teach you and grant you all things, and he will remind you of what I said to you.' Then he said: 'And I have told you this before it happens; so that when it happens, you may believe in it.' His saying 'my Father' means 'my Lord and my God.' And his saying 'in my name' means 'by prophethood.' And the meaning of 'Paraclete' is the prophet who reveals hidden things. And the meaning of his being the spirit of truth and certainty and the Spirit of Holiness, i.e., justice; meaning that these things—truth, certainty, and justice—are like a dead thing without motion, rather they are buried, hidden, not relied upon. And the Paraclete (peace and blessings be upon him) when he is sent, he is like the soul for them, so they return alive, standing in the earth. And there is no doubt that the one by whom God revived truth, certainty, and justice, and whose law remains with creation forever after Jesus (peace and blessings be upon him), and after truth had died out from the earth and falsehood was revived and spread, is only the Seal of the Prophets, and he who is a mercy to all the worlds; our Master and Patron Muhammad (peace and blessings of God be upon him). And in the sixteenth chapter of the Gospel: 'I tell you now truly and certainly: my departure from you is better for you; for if I do not depart from you to my Father, the Paraclete will not come to you; and if I depart, I will send him to you. And when he comes, he will benefit the people of the world, and judge them, and rebuke them, and make them stand upon sin and righteousness.' Then he said: 'When the Spirit of truth and certainty comes, he will guide you and teach you and manage you over all creation; for he does not speak any innovation from himself.' And the meaning of Jesus' departure to his Father—i.e., his Lord, exalted and glorified—is his departure to the place of his honor and elevation, and rest from people by directing the heart to contemplation in the majesty of God and His greatness, upon
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a proof from earlier scriptures, specifically the Torah and Gospel, demonstrating that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is foretold in these texts. The author, Sanusi, begins with a prophecy from the first book of the Torah: God tells Abraham that from Hagar's offspring will come one whose hand is above all, and everyone's hand will be stretched to him in humility. Sanusi argues that this cannot refer to anyone other than Muhammad, because he was sent to all mankind, his religion prevailed, and all people submitted to him, whereas before, the hand (of authority) was with the Children of Israel (prophets from Isaac's line). He then moves to the Gospel, citing three chapters: the fourteenth chapter speaks of a Paraclete (بارقليط) to be sent after Jesus, described as spirit of truth and certainty. The fifteenth chapter says the Paraclete, the Spirit of Holiness, will teach and remind of Jesus' words. Sanusi interprets 'my Father' as 'my Lord' and 'in my name' as 'by prophethood,' and defines the Paraclete as 'the prophet who reveals hidden things.' He then explains the meaning of 'spirit of truth and certainty' and 'Spirit of Holiness' as justice. These qualities—truth, certainty, justice—are like a dead thing that comes alive with the Paraclete. He concludes that the one who revived these and whose law remains forever after Jesus is none other than Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets. Finally, he cites the sixteenth chapter, where Jesus says his departure is necessary for the Paraclete to come, and that the Paraclete will guide, teach, and manage. Sanusi interprets Jesus' departure to the Father as his ascension to honor and rest from people, focusing on divine contemplation. The passage is a clear argument for Muhammad's prophethood using biblical proof texts.

Key Terms
التوراة
هاجر
اليد فوق الجميع
الخشوع
بنو إسرائيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Torah prophecy refers to Ishmael or another historical figure.
Correction: Sanusi argues it must be Muhammad because no other descendant of Hagar had universal dominance over all people.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what was the hand of authority before Muhammad?
A) With the Romans
B) With the Children of Israel
C) With the Persians
D) With the Arabs

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses the Torah prophecy about Hagar's offspring to show that Muhammad's universal mission was foretold in earlier scripture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, is Muhammad's hand truly above all? Are there areas—your ambitions, relationships, or habits—where you resist submitting your hands in humility? What would it take for you to fully stretch out your hands to him?
?
Sanusi argues that the prophecy shifted authority from the Children of Israel to Muhammad's followers. Do you live as if you hold that authority? Or do you still look to other sources for guidance and honor?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment and being asked: 'Did you submit to My Prophet's hand above all?' If your heart trembles at the question, what will you change starting today?

Gospel Prophecy: The Paraclete
Sanusi cites Gospel chapters about the Paraclete and interprets them as referring to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the Gospel passages about the Paraclete as prophecies of Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Paraclete in the Gospel is a human prophet, not a spirit—and that prophet is Muhammad.

In this passage, Sanusi turns to the Gospel, citing three chapters (14, 15, 16) that speak of a Paraclete. He explains the meaning of key terms and argues that the Paraclete must be Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets. This lesson unpacks his interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Gospel citations
Read the Arabic and translation of the three Gospel passages (chapters 14, 15, 16). Notice the term 'بارقليط' (Paraclete).
The term is Greek-derived.
2
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi interprets 'my Father' as 'my Lord' and 'in my name' as 'by prophethood'. He defines the Paraclete as 'the prophet who reveals hidden things'.
This is a clear interpretive move.
3
Analyze the 'spirit' terminology
Sanusi explains that being called 'spirit of truth and certainty' means the Paraclete revives these dead virtues, like a soul gives life.
He says truth, certainty, and justice were dead until the Paraclete.
4
Identify the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that this Paraclete can only be Muhammad, because his law remains forever and he revived truth after Jesus.
He calls Muhammad 'خاتم النبيين' (Seal of the Prophets).
5
Reflect on Jesus' departure
Sanusi interprets Jesus' departure to the Father as his ascension to honor and spiritual rest, not a literal journey.
This is a non-literal interpretation to fit the prophecy.

Source Text

ومنها : ما جاءَ في السفرِ الأَوَّلِ مِنَ التوراة : أنَّهُ تعالى قالَ لإبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام : إنَّ هاجر تله ، ويكونُ مِنْ ولدها مَنْ تكون يده فوق الجميع ، ويد الجميع مبسوطة إليه بالخشوع ، ولا خفاءَ أنه لم يكنْ مِنْ ولد هاجرَ مَنْ يدُه فوق الجميع غير نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ فإنَّهُ بُعِثَ إلى أهل الأرض كافةً ، وأظهر الله تعالى دينَهُ على الأديان كلها ، وأذعن له جميع أهل الأرض ، وبسطوا أيديهم إليه بالذِّلَّةِ والخشوع بعدما كانَتِ اليد لولدِ إسرائيل الذي هو يعقوب بن إسحاق عليهما الصلاة والسلام ؛ إذْ أكثرُ الأنبياءِ مِنْ وَلدِهِ .
وأما الإنجيل : فمنها : ما ورد في المصحفِ الرابع عشر : أنا أطلب لكم إلى أبي حتى يمنحكم ويعطيكم بارقليط ليكون معكم إلى الأبدِ ، والبارقليط : روح الحق واليقين وفي الخامس عشر : فأمَّا بارقليط روح القدس الذي يرسله أبي باسمي هو يُعلِّمُكم ويمنحكم جميعَ الأشياء ، وهو يُذكِّرُكم ما قلتُ لكم ، ثم قال : وإني أخبرتكم بهذا قبل أن يكونَ ؛ حتى إذا كانَ ذلكَ تؤمنونَ به
قوله : أبي معناه : ربي وإلهي ، وقوله : باسمي يعني : بالنبوَّةِ ، ومعنى البارقليط : النبيُّ كاشف الخفيَّاتِ
و معنى كونِهِ روحَ الحقِّ واليقين وروح القدس ؛ أي : العدل ؛ يعني : أنَّ هذهِ الأشياء التي هي الحقُّ واليقين والعدل كالميت لا حراك لها ، بل هي مدفونةٌ خفيَّةٌ لا يُعوّل عليها ، والبارقليط عليهِ الصلاة والسلام إذا بُعِثَ هو كالروح لها ، فترجع حيَّةٌ قائمةً في الأرضِ ولا شك أنَّ الذي أحيا الله تعالى به الحق واليقينَ والعدل ، ويبقى شرعُهُ معَ الخلْقِ إلى الأبد بعد عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلامُ ، وبعدما خمدَ الحَقُّ مِنَ الأرضِ ، وأُحيي الباطل وانتشر . . إنَّما هو خاتم النبيينَ ، ومَنْ هو رحمة لجميع العالمينَ ؛ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .
وفي المصحفِ السادس عشرَ مِنَ الإنجيل : أقولُ لكمُ الآنَ حقاً يقيناً : إِنَّ انطلاقي عنكم خير لكم ؛ فإن لم أنطلق عنكم إلى أبي لم يأتكم البارقليط ، وإن انطلقتُ أرسلتُ بهِ إليكم ، فإذا ما جاءَ هو يفيدُ أهلَ العالم ويُدينهم ويُوبِّخُهم ويوقفُهم على الخطيئة والبر ، ثم قال : إذا جاءَ روح الحقِّ واليقين يرشدكم ويُعلِّمُكم ويُدبِّرُكم بجميعِ الخلْقِ ؛ لأنَّهُ ليسَ يتكلَّمُ بدعةٌ مِنْ تلقاءِ نفسِهِ
ومعنى انطلاقِ عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى أبيه - أي : ربَّهِ تعالى جل وعزّ - : انطلاقه إلى محلّ كرامته ورفعتِهِ ، والاستراحةُ مِنَ الناس بتوجيه القلبِ إِلى الجَوَلانِ في جلالِ اللهِ تعالى وعظمته ، على
And among them: what came in the first book of the Torah: that He, exalted, said to Abraham (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Indeed, Hagar will give birth, and from her offspring will be one whose hand will be above all, and the hand of all will be stretched out to him in humility.' And there is no concealment that there was none from the offspring of Hagar whose hand was above all except our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace and blessings of God be upon him); for he was sent to all the people of the earth, and God manifested His religion over all religions, and all the people of the earth submitted to him, and stretched out their hands to him in abasement and humility after the hand had been for the Children of Israel, who is Jacob son of Isaac (peace and blessings be upon them both); for most of the prophets were from his offspring. As for the Gospel: among them is what is reported in the fourteenth chapter: 'I ask for you from my Father that He grant you and give you a Paraclete to be with you forever.' And the Paraclete is the spirit of truth and certainty. And in the fifteenth: 'As for the Paraclete, the Spirit of Holiness, whom my Father will send in my name, he will teach you and grant you all things, and he will remind you of what I said to you.' Then he said: 'And I have told you this before it happens; so that when it happens, you may believe in it.' His saying 'my Father' means 'my Lord and my God.' And his saying 'in my name' means 'by prophethood.' And the meaning of 'Paraclete' is the prophet who reveals hidden things. And the meaning of his being the spirit of truth and certainty and the Spirit of Holiness, i.e., justice; meaning that these things—truth, certainty, and justice—are like a dead thing without motion, rather they are buried, hidden, not relied upon. And the Paraclete (peace and blessings be upon him) when he is sent, he is like the soul for them, so they return alive, standing in the earth. And there is no doubt that the one by whom God revived truth, certainty, and justice, and whose law remains with creation forever after Jesus (peace and blessings be upon him), and after truth had died out from the earth and falsehood was revived and spread, is only the Seal of the Prophets, and he who is a mercy to all the worlds; our Master and Patron Muhammad (peace and blessings of God be upon him). And in the sixteenth chapter of the Gospel: 'I tell you now truly and certainly: my departure from you is better for you; for if I do not depart from you to my Father, the Paraclete will not come to you; and if I depart, I will send him to you. And when he comes, he will benefit the people of the world, and judge them, and rebuke them, and make them stand upon sin and righteousness.' Then he said: 'When the Spirit of truth and certainty comes, he will guide you and teach you and manage you over all creation; for he does not speak any innovation from himself.' And the meaning of Jesus' departure to his Father—i.e., his Lord, exalted and glorified—is his departure to the place of his honor and elevation, and rest from people by directing the heart to contemplation in the majesty of God and His greatness, upon
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a proof from earlier scriptures, specifically the Torah and Gospel, demonstrating that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is foretold in these texts. The author, Sanusi, begins with a prophecy from the first book of the Torah: God tells Abraham that from Hagar's offspring will come one whose hand is above all, and everyone's hand will be stretched to him in humility. Sanusi argues that this cannot refer to anyone other than Muhammad, because he was sent to all mankind, his religion prevailed, and all people submitted to him, whereas before, the hand (of authority) was with the Children of Israel (prophets from Isaac's line). He then moves to the Gospel, citing three chapters: the fourteenth chapter speaks of a Paraclete (بارقليط) to be sent after Jesus, described as spirit of truth and certainty. The fifteenth chapter says the Paraclete, the Spirit of Holiness, will teach and remind of Jesus' words. Sanusi interprets 'my Father' as 'my Lord' and 'in my name' as 'by prophethood,' and defines the Paraclete as 'the prophet who reveals hidden things.' He then explains the meaning of 'spirit of truth and certainty' and 'Spirit of Holiness' as justice. These qualities—truth, certainty, justice—are like a dead thing that comes alive with the Paraclete. He concludes that the one who revived these and whose law remains forever after Jesus is none other than Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets. Finally, he cites the sixteenth chapter, where Jesus says his departure is necessary for the Paraclete to come, and that the Paraclete will guide, teach, and manage. Sanusi interprets Jesus' departure to the Father as his ascension to honor and rest from people, focusing on divine contemplation. The passage is a clear argument for Muhammad's prophethood using biblical proof texts.

البارقليط
روح الحق
روح القدس
النبوة
خاتم النبيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the Paraclete refers to the Holy Spirit or a non-human spirit.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the Paraclete is a human prophet (النبي كاشف الخفيَّات) who revives truth, certainty, and justice.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the term 'بسمي' (in my name) mean in the Gospel passage?
A) In my honor
B) By prophethood
C) In my spirit
D) By my authority

Key Takeaway
Sanusi interprets the Gospel's Paraclete as a prophecy of Muhammad, the final prophet who revives true religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Gospel truly foretold the coming of Muhammad, what does that mean for your own confidence in his prophethood? Have you ever felt uncertain about this truth, and what would it take for you to be as convinced as Sanusi?
?
Sanusi says the Paraclete revives truth, certainty, and justice. In your own life, have you allowed these virtues to become 'dead'? What is the one area where you need the Prophet's guidance to resurrect your faith?
?
The Paraclete's coming depended on Jesus' departure. How does this remind you that the final guidance for humanity came through Muhammad? Are you truly living as if his message is the final and sufficient guidance for every aspect of your life?

The Paraclete as a Foretelling of Muhammad in the Gospel
Sanusi interprets the Paraclete as Muhammad and cites Gospel evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the Gospel's mention of the Paraclete as a prophecy of Prophet Muhammad's mission.

Core Idea
The Paraclete is not the Holy Spirit but the Prophet Muhammad, who revives buried truth.

Sanusi begins by explaining the meaning of the Paraclete (al-Bāriqlīṭ) as the Prophet who unveils hidden things. He then quotes a passage from the Gospel of John where Jesus promises the coming of the Paraclete after his departure. This lesson unpacks that interpretation and its significance for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of Paraclete
Read Sanusi's definition of al-Bāriqlīṭ as the Prophet who discloses hidden things, and his metaphor of reviving dead truth.
Notice how he emphasizes truth, certainty, and justice as buried until the Paraclete comes.
2
Examine the Gospel quote
Read the quoted passage from John 16 where Jesus speaks of the Paraclete coming after his departure.
The quote includes the Paraclete's role: to guide, teach, and rebuke the world.
3
Analyze the interpretation
Understand Sanusi's explanation of Jesus' departure to the Father and how he attributes sending the Paraclete to himself.
Sanusi connects Jesus' raising to the sign of Muhammad's mission.

على حد قوله تعالى في القرآنِ لهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ﴿ إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرَافِعُكَ إِلَى ﴾ [آل عمران : ٥٥]
وكونه يرسل النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّه يتسبب في برغبة إلى الله تعالى ، أو لما علم عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ أنَّ بعثَ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إِنَّمَا يَكونُ بعدَ رفعِهِ وتغييبِهِ عن الناس .. كانَ رفعُهُ مِنْ أماراتِ بعثِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فأسندَ إرساله إلى نفسه بهذا المعنى
وأما في الزَّبورِ : ففيه قوله تعالى خطاباً لسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( تقلَّد أيُّها الجبَّارُ السيفَ ؛ فإنَّ ناموسَكَ وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتَكَ ) ، ومعنى ( يَخِرُّونَ تحتكَ ) أي : يذلُّون لك حتى يدخلوا في الإسلامِ طَوْعاً أو كَرْهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ . وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ الله تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولد لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى له أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ كي يُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ) وهذا الولد الذي وُلِدَ لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام بتلك الصفة المذكورة هو عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ ، ولم يبعث الله تعالى بعدَهُ جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ وخامدَ البدعة ، وكاشف الغمة .. إلا نبينا ومولانا
Concerning prophethood, and the meaning of 'al-Bāriqlīṭ' (Paraclete): the Prophet who discloses hidden things. And the meaning of His being the Spirit of Truth and Certainty and the Holy Spirit; i.e.: justice; meaning: that these things which are truth, certainty, and justice are like a dead thing with no movement, rather they are buried, hidden, not relied upon, and the Paraclete, peace and blessings be upon him, when he is sent, he is like the spirit for them, so they return alive, standing on earth. And there is no doubt that the one by whom Allah, exalted, revived truth and certainty and justice, and whose law remains with creation forever after Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, and after truth subsided from the earth and falsehood was revived and spread... he is only the Seal of the Prophets, and he who is a mercy to all the worlds: our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And in the sixteenth chapter of the Gospel: (I tell you now truly and certainly: My departure from you is better for you; for if I do not depart from you to my Father, the Paraclete will not come to you; but if I depart, I will send him to you. When he comes, he will benefit the people of the world, judge them, rebuke them, and make them stand upon sin and righteousness.) Then he said: (When the Spirit of Truth and Certainty comes, he will guide you, teach you, and manage you with all creation; because he does not speak an innovation from himself.) And the meaning of Jesus' departure to his Father—i.e., his Lord, exalted and majestic—is his departure to the place of his honor and elevation, and rest from people by turning the heart to contemplation of the majesty and greatness of Allah, exalted, according to His saying in the Qur'an to him, peace be upon him: {Indeed, I will take you and raise you to} [Al 'Imran: 55]. And his sending the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, means: that he causes it by desiring from Allah, or because he knew, peace be upon him, that the mission of our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would only occur after his raising and his disappearance from people... so his raising was one of the signs of his mission, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so he attributed sending him to himself in this sense. And as for the Psalms: in it is the saying of Allah, exalted, addressing our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: (Gird your sword, O mighty one; for your law and ordinances are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall under you.) And the meaning of (they fall under you) is: they are humbled to you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya (tribute) with humiliation. And in the Psalms also: Allah, exalted, says to David, peace be upon him: (A son will be born to you; I will be called a father to him, and he will be called a son to me. Then David, peace be upon him, said: O Allah, send the establisher of the Sunnah so that he may teach the people that he is a human.) And this son who was born to David, peace be upon him, with that described attribute is Jesus, peace be upon him. And Allah did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, extinguisher of innovation, and remover of distress except our Prophet and master.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural evidence from the Gospel and Psalms for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins by explaining the meaning of 'al-Bāriqlīṭ' (Paraclete) as the Prophet who uncovers hidden things. The author then clarifies that the Paraclete is described as the Spirit of Truth, Certainty, and Holiness (justice). He uses a metaphor: truth, certainty, and justice are like dead, buried things; the Paraclete is like a spirit that revives them, making them alive and operative on earth. The author asserts that the one who revived these values through Allah and whose law remains forever after Jesus—after truth faded and falsehood spread—is none other than Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets and mercy to all worlds.

Next, he quotes the Gospel of John (chapter 16) where Jesus speaks of the Paraclete who will come after his departure. He interprets Jesus's departure 'to the Father' as his ascension to honor and his turning to contemplation of Allah's majesty, citing Qur'an 3:55. The sending of the Paraclete is linked to Jesus's raising, as Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent after his own removal; thus Jesus attributed the sending to himself in a causal sense.

Finally, the author turns to the Psalms (Zabur). He quotes a verse addressed to Muhammad (peace be upon him) about girding the sword, his laws being accompanied by awe, etc., interpreting 'nations fall under you' as their submission to Islam or payment of jizya. Then he cites another Psalm where Allah tells David that a son will be born to him (Solomon? but the text says this son is Jesus) and David prays for the 'establisher of the Sunnah' to teach people that he is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus, and states that after Jesus, the only one who established the Sunnah, extinguished innovation, and removed distress was our Prophet Muhammad.

روح القدس
الإنجيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Paraclete refers to the Holy Spirit.
Correction: Sanusi explains that the Paraclete is the Prophet Muhammad, who revives truth, certainty, and justice after they become buried.

According to Sanusi, what does the term 'al-Bāriqlīṭ' (Paraclete) refer to?
A) The Holy Spirit

D) An angel

Key Takeaway
Sanusi identifies the Paraclete in the Gospel as a prophecy of Prophet Muhammad, who revives divine truth after it is buried.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson says truth, certainty, and justice can become like a dead thing, buried and not acted upon. In your own life, which truth from the Quran or sunnah have you left buried, and how can you let the prophetic message revive it today?
?
Jesus taught that the Paraclete would guide into all truth and not speak of his own accord. If you truly believe Muhammad is that Paraclete, how does that change the way you read the Quran? Are you reading it as the final and complete guidance that demands your obedience, or as a book of suggestions?
?
Sanusi argues that Muhammad's law remains forever, yet many Muslims ignore or selectively apply it. What is one area of your life where you are not fully submitting to that law? What would it cost you to align it completely with the Prophet's teaching, and are you willing to pay that price?

Prophecies in the Psalms about Muhammad
Sanusi cites two Psalms prophecies fulfilled by Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets two Psalms passages as foretelling the coming of Prophet Muhammad and the establishment of the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Psalms contain prophecies about Muhammad's sword, law, and his role as the establisher of the Sunnah after Jesus.

After the Gospel, Sanusi turns to the Psalms (Zabur) to find further evidence. He quotes two passages: one addressing Muhammad directly about his rule, and another where David prays for the 'establisher of the Sunnah'. This lesson examines these prophecies and their fulfillment in the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Psalm quote
Sanusi quotes a Psalm that addresses a mighty one girding his sword, with laws accompanied by awe, and nations falling under him.
Note the imagery of power and submission.
2
Interpret the submission of nations
Sanusi explains that 'nations fall under you' means they are humbled to enter Islam or pay jizya willingly or unwillingly.
This shows the universal scope of Muhammad's mission.
3
Read the second Psalm quote
Sanusi presents a Psalm about a son born to David, and David's prayer for the 'establisher of the Sunnah' to teach that this son is human.
Identify the son as Jesus, and the establisher as Muhammad.

بالنبوَّةِ ، ومعنى البارقليط : النبيُّ كاشف الخفيَّاتِ
و معنى كونِهِ روحَ الحقِّ واليقين وروح القدس ؛ أي : العدل ؛ يعني : أنَّ هذهِ الأشياء التي هي الحقُّ واليقين والعدل كالميت لا حراك لها ، بل هي مدفونةٌ خفيَّةٌ لا يُعوّل عليها ، والبارقليط عليهِ الصلاة والسلام إذا بُعِثَ هو كالروح لها ، فترجع حيَّةً قائمةً في الأرضِ ولا شك أنَّ الذي أحيا الله تعالى به الحق واليقين
والعدل ، ويبقى شرعُهُ معَ الخلْقِ إلى الأبد بعد عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلامُ ، وبعدما خمدَ الحَقُّ مِنَ الأرضِ ، وأُحيي الباطل وانتشر . . إنَّما هو خاتم النبيينَ ، ومَنْ هو رحمة لجميع العالمينَ ؛ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .
وفي المصحفِ السادس عشرَ مِنَ الإنجيل : ( أقولُ لكمُ الآنَ حقاً يقيناً : إِنَّ انطلاقي عنكم خير لكم ؛ فإن لم أنطلق عنكم إلى أبي لم يأتكم البارقليط ، وإن انطلقتُ أرسلتُ بهِ إليكم ، فإذا ما جاءَ هو يفيدُ أهلَ العالم ويُدينهم ويُوبِّخُهم ويوقفُهم على الخطيئة والبر ) ، ثم قال : ( إذا جاءَ روح الحقِّ واليقين يرشدكم ويُعلِّمُكم ويُدبِّرُكم بجميعِ الخلْقِ ؛ لأنَّهُ ليسَ يتكلَّمُ بدعةٌ مِنْ تلقاءِ نفسِهِ )
ومعنى انطلاقِ عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى أبيه - أي : ربَّهِ تعالى جل وعزّ - : انطلاقه إلى محلّ كرامته ورفعتِهِ ، والاستراحةُ مِنَ الناس بتوجيه القلبِ إِلى الجَوَلانِ في جلالِ اللهِ تعالى وعظمته
على حد قوله تعالى في القرآنِ لهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ﴿ إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرَافِعُكَ إِلَى ﴾ [آل عمران : ٥٥]
وكونه يرسل النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّه يتسبب في برغبة إلى الله تعالى ، أو لما علم عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ أنَّ بعثَ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إِنَّمَا يَكونُ بعدَ رفعِهِ وتغييبِهِ عن الناس .. كانَ رفعُهُ مِنْ أماراتِ بعثِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فأسندَ إرساله إلى نفسه بهذا المعنى
وأما في الزَّبورِ : ففيه قوله تعالى خطاباً لسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( تقلَّد أيُّها الجبَّارُ السيفَ ؛ فإنَّ ناموسَكَ وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتَكَ ) ، ومعنى ( يَخِرُّونَ تحتكَ ) أي : يذلُّون لك حتى يدخلوا في الإسلامِ طَوْعاً أو كَرْهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ . وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ الله تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولد لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى له أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ كي يُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ) وهذا الولد الذي وُلِدَ لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام بتلك الصفة المذكورة هو عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ ، ولم يبعث الله تعالى بعدَهُ جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ وخامدَ البدعة ، وكاشف الغمة .. إلا نبينا ومولانا
Concerning prophethood, and the meaning of 'al-Bāriqlīṭ' (Paraclete): the Prophet who discloses hidden things. And the meaning of His being the Spirit of Truth and Certainty and the Holy Spirit; i.e.: justice; meaning: that these things which are truth, certainty, and justice are like a dead thing with no movement, rather they are buried, hidden, not relied upon, and the Paraclete, peace and blessings be upon him, when he is sent, he is like the spirit for them, so they return alive, standing on earth. And there is no doubt that the one by whom Allah, exalted, revived truth and certainty and justice, and whose law remains with creation forever after Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, and after truth subsided from the earth and falsehood was revived and spread... he is only the Seal of the Prophets, and he who is a mercy to all the worlds: our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And in the sixteenth chapter of the Gospel: (I tell you now truly and certainly: My departure from you is better for you; for if I do not depart from you to my Father, the Paraclete will not come to you; but if I depart, I will send him to you. When he comes, he will benefit the people of the world, judge them, rebuke them, and make them stand upon sin and righteousness.) Then he said: (When the Spirit of Truth and Certainty comes, he will guide you, teach you, and manage you with all creation; because he does not speak an innovation from himself.) And the meaning of Jesus' departure to his Father—i.e., his Lord, exalted and majestic—is his departure to the place of his honor and elevation, and rest from people by turning the heart to contemplation of the majesty and greatness of Allah, exalted, according to His saying in the Qur'an to him, peace be upon him: {Indeed, I will take you and raise you to} [Al 'Imran: 55]. And his sending the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, means: that he causes it by desiring from Allah, or because he knew, peace be upon him, that the mission of our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would only occur after his raising and his disappearance from people... so his raising was one of the signs of his mission, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so he attributed sending him to himself in this sense. And as for the Psalms: in it is the saying of Allah, exalted, addressing our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: (Gird your sword, O mighty one; for your law and ordinances are accompanied by the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall under you.) And the meaning of (they fall under you) is: they are humbled to you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya (tribute) with humiliation. And in the Psalms also: Allah, exalted, says to David, peace be upon him: (A son will be born to you; I will be called a father to him, and he will be called a son to me. Then David, peace be upon him, said: O Allah, send the establisher of the Sunnah so that he may teach the people that he is a human.) And this son who was born to David, peace be upon him, with that described attribute is Jesus, peace be upon him. And Allah did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, extinguisher of innovation, and remover of distress except our Prophet and master.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural evidence from the Gospel and Psalms for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins by explaining the meaning of 'al-Bāriqlīṭ' (Paraclete) as the Prophet who uncovers hidden things. The author then clarifies that the Paraclete is described as the Spirit of Truth, Certainty, and Holiness (justice). He uses a metaphor: truth, certainty, and justice are like dead, buried things; the Paraclete is like a spirit that revives them, making them alive and operative on earth. The author asserts that the one who revived these values through Allah and whose law remains forever after Jesus—after truth faded and falsehood spread—is none other than Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets and mercy to all worlds.

Next, he quotes the Gospel of John (chapter 16) where Jesus speaks of the Paraclete who will come after his departure. He interprets Jesus's departure 'to the Father' as his ascension to honor and his turning to contemplation of Allah's majesty, citing Qur'an 3:55. The sending of the Paraclete is linked to Jesus's raising, as Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent after his own removal; thus Jesus attributed the sending to himself in a causal sense.

Finally, the author turns to the Psalms (Zabur). He quotes a verse addressed to Muhammad (peace be upon him) about girding the sword, his laws being accompanied by awe, etc., interpreting 'nations fall under you' as their submission to Islam or payment of jizya. Then he cites another Psalm where Allah tells David that a son will be born to him (Solomon? but the text says this son is Jesus) and David prays for the 'establisher of the Sunnah' to teach people that he is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus, and states that after Jesus, the only one who established the Sunnah, extinguished innovation, and removed distress was our Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms
الزبور
جاعل السنة
السيف
الجزية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Psalms prophecies refer to David or Jesus, not Muhammad.
Correction: Sanusi argues that the sword-bearing mighty one is Muhammad, and the establisher of the Sunnah prayed for by David is also Muhammad, not Jesus.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the meaning of 'nations fall under you' in the Psalms?
A) They are destroyed
B) They are humbled into Islam or pay jizya
C) They become allies
D) They are forgiven

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses two Psalms passages to show that the coming of Muhammad with authority and as the establisher of the Sunnah was prophesied long before his birth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read how the Psalms foretold that nations would fall under Muhammad, do you truly live with the conviction that his message is universal and binding on every aspect of your life? Or do you compartmentalize your faith? What would change if you took that sovereignty seriously?
?
David prayed for an 'establisher of the Sunnah' to teach people that Jesus is human. Have you ever seriously doubted or neglected any part of the Sunnah? Are you actively learning and practicing the Sunnah, or have you let innovations creep in?
?
The Psalms prophecy points to a divinely ordained plan spanning centuries. Do you see your own life as part of that same plan? If you truly believed that Allah orchestrated history to send Muhammad, how would that reshape your daily priorities and your hope for the future?

Prophethood

The Quranic Sign of Muhammad's Coming
Interpretation of Al Imran 3:55 as a prophecy of Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse about Jesus' raising is interpreted as a sign of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Jesus' raising foreshadowed Muhammad's mission.

Sanusi begins his scriptural evidence with a verse from the Quran that, through careful interpretation, points to the coming of Muhammad. This lesson unpacks that verse and the reasoning that links it to the final prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Start by reading the Quranic verse and its literal translation. Notice that it addresses Jesus, not Muhammad.
The verse is from Surah Al Imran 3:55.
2
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi explains that Jesus knew his raising would precede Muhammad's sending, so the raising becomes a sign. Grasp the logical connection.
3
Identify the doctrinal purpose
See how Sanusi uses this verse to affirm Muhammad's prophethood from within the Quran itself.
This is the first of several scriptural proofs.

الله تعالى ، أو لما علم عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ أنَّ بعثَ سيّدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إِنَّمَا يَكونُ بعدَ رفعِهِ وتغييبِهِ عن الناس .. كانَ رفعُهُ مِنْ أماراتِ بعثِهِ صلَّى اللهُ مقرونة بهيبة يمينك ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتَكَ ) (۱) ، ومعنى ( يَخِرُّونَ تحتكَ ) أي : يذلُّون لك حتى يدخلوا في الإسلامِ طَوْعاً أو كَرْهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ . وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ الله تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولد لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى له أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ كي يُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ((۲) وهذا الولد الذي وُلِدَ لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام بتلك الصفة المذكورة هو عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ ، ولم يبعث الله تعالى بعدَهُ جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ وخامدَ البدعة ، وكاشف الغمة .. إلا نبينا ومولانا محمداً صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ (۱) ، فأعلم الناس أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام عبد الله تعالى ورسوله ، وأنَّه لن يستنكف المسيحُ أنْ يكونَ عبداً الله ولا الملائكةُ المقرَّبونَ ، وأنَّهُ ما كانَ للرحمن أن يتَّخذ ولداً ، إن كُلُّ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إِلَّا وَانِي الرَّحْمَنِ عَبْدًا) [مريم : ٩٣] ، وأن مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ أحدٌ صمدٌ ، لم يلد ولم يُولد ، ولم يكن له كفواً أحد . وقد وقع في الإنجيل التي هي بأيدي الكفرة اليوم نظير ما وقع في الزَّبورِ ، يقول فيه عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( اللهم ؛ ابعث البارقليط ليُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ ابنَ الإنسان بشرٌ ((۲) يوصي القلوبَ الغُلْفَ وقال إشعياء النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهرُ في الأمم عدلي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسْمَعُ صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسمعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمد يحمد الله حمداً ) ثم أشار إلى بلدِهِ مكَّةَ فقالَ : ( تفرح البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها يُهلِّلُونَ اللَّهَ على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبِّرُونَهُ على كلِّ رابيةٍ ، لا يَضْعُفُ ولا يُغْلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسْمَعُ في الأسواق صوتُه ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يقوي الصِّدِّيقين ، وهو (۱)
The statement of God Almighty in the Quran concerning him, peace be upon him: “Indeed I will take you and raise you up to Me” [Al Imran 3:55]. That. And that He sends the Prophet, peace be upon him and grant him peace, meaning that He causes [him] to desire God Almighty, or because he, peace be upon him, knew that the sending of our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace, would only be after his raising and his concealment from the people... so his raising was among the signs of his sending, peace be upon him and grant him peace, so he attributed his sending to Himself in this sense. As for in the Psalms: in it is the statement of God Almighty addressing our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “Gird on the sword, O mighty one; for your law and your statutes are coupled with the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you” (1). And the meaning of “they fall under you” is: they are humbled for you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya out of hand while they are humiliated. And in the Psalms also: God Almighty says to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “A son will be born to you; I will call him a father, and he will call Me a son.” So David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, said: “O God, send the establisher of the Sunnah to make people know that he is a human” (2). And this son who was born to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, with that described attribute is Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace. And God Almighty did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, and quencher of innovation, and remover of calamity, except our prophet and master Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace (1). So he made people know that Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace, is the servant of God Almighty and His messenger, and that the Messiah would not disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels brought near; and that it is not for the Most Merciful to take a son; “There is none in the heavens and the earth but who comes to the Most Merciful as a servant” [Maryam 19:93]; and that our Master, Majestic and High, is One, Self-Sufficient, He does not beget nor is He begotten, and there is none equal to Him. And there has occurred in the Gospel that is in the hands of the disbelievers today similar to what occurred in the Psalms; in it Jesus, peace be upon him, says: “O God, send the Paraclete to make people know that the Son of Man is human” (2). He instructs the uncircumcised hearts. And Isaiah the prophet, peace be upon him, said concerning God Almighty: “My servant with whom I am well pleased, I will send down My revelation upon him, and he will manifest My justice among the nations, the nations with the commandments; he does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets; he opens blind eyes, and makes deaf ears hear, and he gives life, and what I give him I give to no one else; Ahmad praises God with praise.” Then he pointed to his city Mecca and said: “The wilderness shall rejoice, and its inhabitants shall glorify God on every hill, and magnify Him on every mound; he will not be weak nor be defeated, nor will he incline to passion, nor will his voice be heard in the markets; nor will he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but he will strengthen the truthful. And he (1)
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument from previous scriptures—the Quran, Psalms, Gospel, and the book of Isaiah—to prove the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by citing a Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:55) where God addresses Jesus, saying 'I will take you and raise you up to Me.' He explains that this raising of Jesus was a sign of the future sending of Muhammad, because Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent only after his own ascent and concealment. Thus God attributes the sending of Muhammad to Himself in this indirect sense. Next, the author turns to the Psalms. He quotes a passage addressing Muhammad as 'O mighty one' and describes his law and victory over nations, interpreting the 'falling under you' as submission through Islam or payment of jizya. Then he quotes another Psalm where God tells David that a son will be born who will call God 'father' and be called 'son' by God; David then prays for the one who will establish the Sunnah (i.e., Muhammad) to make people know that that son (Jesus) is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus and asserts that after Jesus, only Muhammad came as the establisher of the Sunnah. From this, the author derives a refutation ofChristian divinity claims: Jesus is a servant of God, not a son, and God is above having a son. He quotes Surah Maryam (19:93) and the attribute of God as Ahad, Samad, etc. Finally, he cites the Gospel and the prophecy of Isaiah. In the Gospel (as held by Christians), Jesus prays for the sending of the Paraclete (the Comforter) to teach that the Son of Man is human—again referring to Muhammad. In Isaiah, a description matching Muhammad is given: a servant of God, given revelation, who does not attract attention in markets, heals spiritual blindness and deafness, and is associated with the name 'Ahmad' (a name of Muhammad) and guided to Mecca and its hills. The passage ends mid-sentence at 'and he' (وهو), probably continuing with the rest of the Isaiah quote on the next page. The overall argument is that the scriptures preceding the Quran foretold Muhammad's coming, confirming him as the final prophet for all mankind.

Key Terms
مُتَوَفِّيكَ
رَافِعُكَ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, how does the verse about Jesus' raising serve as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood?
A) It directly states Muhammad's name.
B) Jesus knew Muhammad would come after him, so his raising became a sign.
C) It proves Jesus was not the final prophet.
D) It shows that Muhammad would be raised like Jesus.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse about Jesus' raising is interpreted as a sign foretelling the prophethood of Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you recognize that God often places signs in seemingly unrelated events? How has He done that in your own life?
?
The raising of Jesus was a quiet sign—only understood by those who knew the future. Are you alert to the subtle ways God speaks to you, or do you demand dramatic miracles?
?
Jesus' ascent was not an end but a preparation for Muhammad's mission. How does knowing that every event in your life serves a larger purpose change how you face trials?

Prophethood

Psalms Foretell Muhammad and Refute Jesus' Divinity
Two Psalms prophecies linked to Muhammad and Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two prophecies from the Psalms and how they point to Muhammad while refuting Christian claims about Jesus.

Core Idea
The Psalms predict Muhammad and affirm Jesus' humanity.

Sanusi turns to the Psalms, quoting two distinct prophecies. The first describes a mighty warrior with law and victory, interpreted as Muhammad. The second involves David's son and a request for the 'establisher of the Sunnah' to clarify Jesus' human nature, which Sanusi uses to refute Christian doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Psalm prophecy
Read the Arabic and translation of the first Psalm quote. Notice it addresses a 'mighty one' with sword and law.
Sanusi interprets this as addressing Muhammad.
2
Understand the second Psalm prophecy
Read the second Psalm about David's son and the prayer for the 'establisher of the Sunnah'.
The son is Jesus; the establisher is Muhammad.
3
See the theological conclusion
Sanusi argues that Muhammad came to teach that Jesus is a servant, not divine. This refutes Christological errors.
This is a key interfaith argument.

حد قوله تعالى في القرآنِ لهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ﴿ إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرَافِعُكَ إِلَيَّ ﴾ [آل عمران : ٥٥] ذلك • وكونه يرسل النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّه يتسبب في برغبة إلى الله تعالى ، أو لما علم عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ أنَّ بعثَ سيّدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إِنَّمَا يَكونُ بعدَ رفعِهِ وتغييبِهِ عن الناس .. كانَ رفعُهُ مِنْ أماراتِ بعثِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فأسندَ إرساله إلى نفسه بهذا المعنى وأما في الزَّبورِ : ففيه قوله تعالى خطاباً لسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( تقلَّد أيُّها الجبَّارُ السيفَ ؛ فإنَّ ناموسَكَ وشرائعك مقرونة بهيبة يمينك ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتَكَ ) (۱) ، ومعنى ( يَخِرُّونَ تحتكَ ) أي : يذلُّون لك حتى يدخلوا في الإسلامِ طَوْعاً أو كَرْهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ . وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ الله تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولد لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى له أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ كي يُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ((۲) وهذا الولد الذي وُلِدَ لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام بتلك الصفة المذكورة هو عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ ، ولم يبعث الله تعالى بعدَهُ جاعلَ السُّنَّةِ وخامدَ البدعة ، وكاشف الغمة .. إلا نبينا ومولانا محمداً صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ (۱) ، فأعلم الناس أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام عبد الله تعالى ورسوله ، وأنَّه لن يستنكف المسيحُ أنْ يكونَ عبداً الله ولا الملائكةُ المقرَّبونَ ، وأنَّهُ ما كانَ للرحمن أن يتَّخذ ولداً ، إن كُلُّ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إِلَّا وَانِي الرَّحْمَنِ عَبْدًا) [مريم : ٩٣] ، وأن مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ أحدٌ صمدٌ ، لم يلد ولم يُولد ، ولم يكن له كفواً أحد . وقد وقع في الإنجيل التي هي بأيدي الكفرة اليوم نظير ما وقع في الزَّبورِ ، يقول فيه عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( اللهم ؛ ابعث البارقليط ليُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ ابنَ الإنسان بشرٌ ((۲) يوصي القلوبَ الغُلْفَ وقال إشعياء النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهرُ في الأمم عدلي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسْمَعُ صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسمعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمد يحمد الله حمداً ) ثم أشار إلى بلدِهِ مكَّةَ فقالَ : ( تفرح البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها يُهلِّلُونَ اللَّهَ على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبِّرُونَهُ على كلِّ رابيةٍ ، لا يَضْعُفُ ولا يُغْلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسْمَعُ في الأسواق صوتُه ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يقوي الصِّدِّيقين ، وهو (۱)
The statement of God Almighty in the Quran concerning him, peace be upon him: “Indeed I will take you and raise you up to Me” [Al Imran 3:55]. That. And that He sends the Prophet, peace be upon him and grant him peace, meaning that He causes [him] to desire God Almighty, or because he, peace be upon him, knew that the sending of our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace, would only be after his raising and his concealment from the people... so his raising was among the signs of his sending, peace be upon him and grant him peace, so he attributed his sending to Himself in this sense. As for in the Psalms: in it is the statement of God Almighty addressing our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “Gird on the sword, O mighty one; for your law and your statutes are coupled with the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you” (1). And the meaning of “they fall under you” is: they are humbled for you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya out of hand while they are humiliated. And in the Psalms also: God Almighty says to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “A son will be born to you; I will call him a father, and he will call Me a son.” So David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, said: “O God, send the establisher of the Sunnah to make people know that he is a human” (2). And this son who was born to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, with that described attribute is Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace. And God Almighty did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, and quencher of innovation, and remover of calamity, except our prophet and master Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace (1). So he made people know that Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace, is the servant of God Almighty and His messenger, and that the Messiah would not disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels brought near; and that it is not for the Most Merciful to take a son; “There is none in the heavens and the earth but who comes to the Most Merciful as a servant” [Maryam 19:93]; and that our Master, Majestic and High, is One, Self-Sufficient, He does not beget nor is He begotten, and there is none equal to Him. And there has occurred in the Gospel that is in the hands of the disbelievers today similar to what occurred in the Psalms; in it Jesus, peace be upon him, says: “O God, send the Paraclete to make people know that the Son of Man is human” (2). He instructs the uncircumcised hearts. And Isaiah the prophet, peace be upon him, said concerning God Almighty: “My servant with whom I am well pleased, I will send down My revelation upon him, and he will manifest My justice among the nations, the nations with the commandments; he does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets; he opens blind eyes, and makes deaf ears hear, and he gives life, and what I give him I give to no one else; Ahmad praises God with praise.” Then he pointed to his city Mecca and said: “The wilderness shall rejoice, and its inhabitants shall glorify God on every hill, and magnify Him on every mound; he will not be weak nor be defeated, nor will he incline to passion, nor will his voice be heard in the markets; nor will he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but he will strengthen the truthful. And he (1)
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument from previous scriptures—the Quran, Psalms, Gospel, and the book of Isaiah—to prove the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by citing a Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:55) where God addresses Jesus, saying 'I will take you and raise you up to Me.' He explains that this raising of Jesus was a sign of the future sending of Muhammad, because Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent only after his own ascent and concealment. Thus God attributes the sending of Muhammad to Himself in this indirect sense. Next, the author turns to the Psalms. He quotes a passage addressing Muhammad as 'O mighty one' and describes his law and victory over nations, interpreting the 'falling under you' as submission through Islam or payment of jizya. Then he quotes another Psalm where God tells David that a son will be born who will call God 'father' and be called 'son' by God; David then prays for the one who will establish the Sunnah (i.e., Muhammad) to make people know that that son (Jesus) is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus and asserts that after Jesus, only Muhammad came as the establisher of the Sunnah. From this, the author derives a refutation ofChristian divinity claims: Jesus is a servant of God, not a son, and God is above having a son. He quotes Surah Maryam (19:93) and the attribute of God as Ahad, Samad, etc. Finally, he cites the Gospel and the prophecy of Isaiah. In the Gospel (as held by Christians), Jesus prays for the sending of the Paraclete (the Comforter) to teach that the Son of Man is human—again referring to Muhammad. In Isaiah, a description matching Muhammad is given: a servant of God, given revelation, who does not attract attention in markets, heals spiritual blindness and deafness, and is associated with the name 'Ahmad' (a name of Muhammad) and guided to Mecca and its hills. The passage ends mid-sentence at 'and he' (وهو), probably continuing with the rest of the Isaiah quote on the next page. The overall argument is that the scriptures preceding the Quran foretold Muhammad's coming, confirming him as the final prophet for all mankind.

Key Terms
الزَّبورِ
جبَّارُ
السُّنَّةِ
عبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Psalms contain no prophecies about Muhammad.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the Psalms contain explicit prophecies about a mighty prophet and the 'establisher of the Sunnah,' identified as Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did David pray for the 'establisher of the Sunnah'?
A) To teach people that David's son was divine.
B) To make people know that the son (Jesus) is human.
C) To establish a new law.
D) To defeat the enemies of Israel.

Key Takeaway
The Psalms foretell Muhammad's mission and affirm Jesus' servanthood, refuting the idea of his divinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Psalms address Muhammad as 'O mighty one' and promise the submission of nations, does it deepen your conviction in his prophethood? How does this affect your daily trust in Allah's plan for Islam's victory?
?
David prayed for someone to teach the people that Jesus is human. Have you ever felt uncertain about who Jesus truly is? How does this lesson clarify your response when others claim he is divine?
?
The passage ends with the truth that all in heavens and earth are servants of the Most Merciful. Do you live as a true servant, or do you sometimes act independently? What one concrete action can you take today to embody complete servitude to Allah?

Prophethood

The Gospel's Paraclete Prophecy Points to Muhammad
Gospel prophecy of Paraclete linked to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Gospel prophecy about the Paraclete is interpreted as a reference to Muhammad.

Core Idea
The promised Paraclete is Muhammad, clarifying Jesus' humanity.

Sanusi continues his scriptural evidence by citing the Gospel. He notes that the Gospel contains a prophecy similar to the Psalms: Jesus prays for the sending of the Paraclete (the Comforter) to teach people that the Son of Man is human. For Sanusi, this Paraclete is none other than Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Gospel quote
Read the short Arabic and English passage. Note that Jesus prays for the 'Paraclete'.
Paraclete is a Greek term meaning advocate or comforter.
2
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi identifies the Paraclete as Muhammad, who would clarify Jesus' human nature.
This is a key Islamic argument from the Bible.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'uncircumcised hearts'
The passage ends with 'He instructs the uncircumcised hearts,' indicating the Paraclete's role in guiding those with hardened hearts.

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument from previous scriptures—the Quran, Psalms, Gospel, and the book of Isaiah—to prove the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by citing a Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:55) where God addresses Jesus, saying 'I will take you and raise you up to Me.' He explains that this raising of Jesus was a sign of the future sending of Muhammad, because Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent only after his own ascent and concealment. Thus God attributes the sending of Muhammad to Himself in this indirect sense. Next, the author turns to the Psalms. He quotes a passage addressing Muhammad as 'O mighty one' and describes his law and victory over nations, interpreting the 'falling under you' as submission through Islam or payment of jizya. Then he quotes another Psalm where God tells David that a son will be born who will call God 'father' and be called 'son' by God; David then prays for the one who will establish the Sunnah (i.e., Muhammad) to make people know that that son (Jesus) is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus and asserts that after Jesus, only Muhammad came as the establisher of the Sunnah. From this, the author derives a refutation ofChristian divinity claims: Jesus is a servant of God, not a son, and God is above having a son. He quotes Surah Maryam (19:93) and the attribute of God as Ahad, Samad, etc. Finally, he cites the Gospel and the prophecy of Isaiah. In the Gospel (as held by Christians), Jesus prays for the sending of the Paraclete (the Comforter) to teach that the Son of Man is human—again referring to Muhammad. In Isaiah, a description matching Muhammad is given: a servant of God, given revelation, who does not attract attention in markets, heals spiritual blindness and deafness, and is associated with the name 'Ahmad' (a name of Muhammad) and guided to Mecca and its hills. The passage ends mid-sentence at 'and he' (وهو), probably continuing with the rest of the Isaiah quote on the next page. The overall argument is that the scriptures preceding the Quran foretold Muhammad's coming, confirming him as the final prophet for all mankind.

What is the main purpose of the Paraclete according to Sanusi's citation?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Jesus himself prayed for a prophet to come after him to clarify his humanity, does your heart truly accept Jesus as a human servant of Allah, or do you still hold any hidden reverence for him that borders on worship? What specific action can you take today to purify your belief?
?
The Paraclete is sent to instruct uncircumcised hearts—hearts hardened against truth. Which area of your life are you still 'uncircumcised' in faith, resisting the full submission that Islam demands? What step will you take this week to soften that heart?
?
Christians have this very prophecy in their scripture but reject its fulfillment in Muhammad. How does that make you feel about the power of truth to guide some and blind others? Will you let this lesson increase your gratitude for being guided, and spur you to share this truth with someone who is searching?

Isaiah's Prophecy Describes Muhammad and His Mission
Isaiah prophecy describing Muhammad's attributes and mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecy of Isaiah foretells the coming of Muhammad and his characteristics.

Core Idea
Isaiah's servant prophecy matches Muhammad's description and mission.

Sanusi concludes his scriptural evidence with a lengthy prophecy from Isaiah. The passage describes a servant of God who receives revelation, is gentle yet powerful, opens blind eyes, and is associated with the name 'Ahmad' and the city of Mecca. This is clearly identified as Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Isaiah prophecy
Read the full Arabic and translation. Notice the detailed description of the servant.
This is the longest quote in the lesson.
2
Identify key characteristics
Look for traits: does not laugh, voice not heard in markets, opens blind eyes, etc. These match Muhammad's conduct and miracles.
The prophecy also mentions 'Ahmad', a name of Muhammad.
3
Understand the geography
Isaiah points to Mecca ('the wilderness') and describes praise on hills and mounds, referencing Islamic practices.
This reinforces the identification of Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the incomplete ending
The passage ends abruptly with 'and he'. The rest of the prophecy likely continues in the original source.
This shows the original text was longer.
