الغُلْفَ وقال إشعياء النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهرُ في الأمم عدلي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسْمَعُ صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسمعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمد يحمد الله حمداً ) ثم أشار إلى بلدِهِ مكَّةَ فقالَ : ( تفرح البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها يُهلِّلُونَ اللَّهَ على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبِّرُونَهُ على كلِّ رابيةٍ ، لا يَضْعُفُ ولا يُغْلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسْمَعُ في الأسواق صوتُه ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يقوي الصِّدِّيقين ، وهو (۱)
The statement of God Almighty in the Quran concerning him, peace be upon him: “Indeed I will take you and raise you up to Me” [Al Imran 3:55]. That. And that He sends the Prophet, peace be upon him and grant him peace, meaning that He causes [him] to desire God Almighty, or because he, peace be upon him, knew that the sending of our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace, would only be after his raising and his concealment from the people... so his raising was among the signs of his sending, peace be upon him and grant him peace, so he attributed his sending to Himself in this sense. As for in the Psalms: in it is the statement of God Almighty addressing our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “Gird on the sword, O mighty one; for your law and your statutes are coupled with the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you” (1). And the meaning of “they fall under you” is: they are humbled for you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya out of hand while they are humiliated. And in the Psalms also: God Almighty says to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace: “A son will be born to you; I will call him a father, and he will call Me a son.” So David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, said: “O God, send the establisher of the Sunnah to make people know that he is a human” (2). And this son who was born to David, peace be upon him and grant him peace, with that described attribute is Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace. And God Almighty did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, and quencher of innovation, and remover of calamity, except our prophet and master Muhammad, peace be upon him and grant him peace (1). So he made people know that Jesus, peace be upon him and grant him peace, is the servant of God Almighty and His messenger, and that the Messiah would not disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels brought near; and that it is not for the Most Merciful to take a son; “There is none in the heavens and the earth but who comes to the Most Merciful as a servant” [Maryam 19:93]; and that our Master, Majestic and High, is One, Self-Sufficient, He does not beget nor is He begotten, and there is none equal to Him. And there has occurred in the Gospel that is in the hands of the disbelievers today similar to what occurred in the Psalms; in it Jesus, peace be upon him, says: “O God, send the Paraclete to make people know that the Son of Man is human” (2). He instructs the uncircumcised hearts. And Isaiah the prophet, peace be upon him, said concerning God Almighty: “My servant with whom I am well pleased, I will send down My revelation upon him, and he will manifest My justice among the nations, the nations with the commandments; he does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets; he opens blind eyes, and makes deaf ears hear, and he gives life, and what I give him I give to no one else; Ahmad praises God with praise.” Then he pointed to his city Mecca and said: “The wilderness shall rejoice, and its inhabitants shall glorify God on every hill, and magnify Him on every mound; he will not be weak nor be defeated, nor will he incline to passion, nor will his voice be heard in the markets; nor will he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but he will strengthen the truthful. And he (1)
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument from previous scriptures—the Quran, Psalms, Gospel, and the book of Isaiah—to prove the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by citing a Quranic verse (Al Imran 3:55) where God addresses Jesus, saying 'I will take you and raise you up to Me.' He explains that this raising of Jesus was a sign of the future sending of Muhammad, because Jesus knew that Muhammad would be sent only after his own ascent and concealment. Thus God attributes the sending of Muhammad to Himself in this indirect sense. Next, the author turns to the Psalms. He quotes a passage addressing Muhammad as 'O mighty one' and describes his law and victory over nations, interpreting the 'falling under you' as submission through Islam or payment of jizya. Then he quotes another Psalm where God tells David that a son will be born who will call God 'father' and be called 'son' by God; David then prays for the one who will establish the Sunnah (i.e., Muhammad) to make people know that that son (Jesus) is human. The author identifies that son as Jesus and asserts that after Jesus, only Muhammad came as the establisher of the Sunnah. From this, the author derives a refutation ofChristian divinity claims: Jesus is a servant of God, not a son, and God is above having a son. He quotes Surah Maryam (19:93) and the attribute of God as Ahad, Samad, etc. Finally, he cites the Gospel and the prophecy of Isaiah. In the Gospel (as held by Christians), Jesus prays for the sending of the Paraclete (the Comforter) to teach that the Son of Man is human—again referring to Muhammad. In Isaiah, a description matching Muhammad is given: a servant of God, given revelation, who does not attract attention in markets, heals spiritual blindness and deafness, and is associated with the name 'Ahmad' (a name of Muhammad) and guided to Mecca and its hills. The passage ends mid-sentence at 'and he' (وهو), probably continuing with the rest of the Isaiah quote on the next page. The overall argument is that the scriptures preceding the Quran foretold Muhammad's coming, confirming him as the final prophet for all mankind.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Isaiah's prophecy refers to Jesus or another figure.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates that the details—especially the name Ahmad and the mention of Mecca—point uniquely to Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to the Isaiah prophecy, where will the promised servant's city be?
A) Jerusalem
B) Mecca
C) Medina
D) Damascus

Key Takeaway
Isaiah's prophecy describes Muhammad by name, character, and location, providing strong scriptural evidence for his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophecy describes Muhammad as one who 'does not laugh' and 'his voice is not heard in the markets'. Think about your own behavior in public: do you guard your speech and actions, or do you seek attention and laughter? What would you need to change in your daily interactions to better reflect this prophetic example?
?
Muhammad strengthened the truthful; he did not humiliate the weak. Who in your life is like a 'weak reed' that needs support? Are you strengthening them or inadvertently ignoring them? Commit to one concrete action this week to support someone who speaks truth in the face of difficulty.
?
The prophecy says the wilderness of Mecca rejoiced when its inhabitants glorified God. Do you feel joy when Allah is mentioned and when His religion is proclaimed? Or does your heart feel heavy or indifferent? Be honest: what is the condition of your heart towards the spread of Islam, and what can you do to increase your love for it?

The Paraclete and Isaiah's Prophecies
Sanusi presents the Paraclete and Isaiah prophecies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two key biblical prophecies that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad: the Paraclete in the Gospel and the servant in Isaiah.

Core Idea
The Bible contains explicit prophecies about Ahmad, the praised one.

Sanusi begins by establishing the correct Islamic belief about Jesus and God's oneness, then presents two prophecies from the Gospel and Isaiah that he argues clearly refer to Muhammad. These prophecies set the stage for a detailed analysis of their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening context
Read the opening sentences about Jesus being a servant of God and God's oneness to understand the theological foundation.
This context shows that these prophecies are not about Jesus but about another prophet.
2
Identify the Paraclete prophecy
Find the words of Jesus in the Gospel where he prays for the Paraclete to inform people that the son of man is human.
The Paraclete is interpreted as Muhammad.
3
Read the Isaiah prophecy
Read the long prophecy from Isaiah about God's servant: he will receive revelation, manifest justice, open blind eyes, etc.
Notice the phrase 'Ahmad praises God'.
4
Note the description of Makka
Observe how the prophecy describes a land where people praise God on hills and mounds, which Sanusi identifies as Makka.

الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمد يحمد الله حمداً ) ثم أشار إلى بلدِهِ مكَّةَ فقالَ : ( تفرح البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها يُهلِّلُونَ اللَّهَ على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبِّرُونَهُ على كلِّ رابيةٍ ، لا يَضْعُفُ ولا يُغْلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسْمَعُ في الأسواق صوتُه ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يقوي الصِّدِّيقين ، وهو ركن المتواضعين ، وهو نورُ اللهِ الذي لا يُطفأُ ولا يُخصَمُ حتى تثبتَ بالأرضِ حُجَّتي ، وينقطع به العذرُ ، وإلى توراته ينقاد الحق )) انظر رحمَكَ الله إلى هذا التصريح العظيم بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ غيرِ ما وجه : منها قوله : ( يوصي الأمم ) ، فإنَّ هذا يقتضي أنَّهُ بُعِثَ لجميعِ الأممِ ، ولم يثبت ذلك إلا لسيدنا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وفي الإنجيل : أنَّ المسيح عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : ( إني لم أبعَثْ إلى الأجناس ، وإِنَّما بُعِثْتُ إلى الغنم الرابضة مِنْ نسل بني إسرائيل ) ومنها قوله : ( أحمد يحمد الله ) ، وهذا تصريح باسمه . ومنها قوله : ( تفرحُ البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها ... ) إلى آخرِ ما ذكرَهُ مِنْ أوصافها ، ولا خفاءَ أنَّها أوصافُ مكَّةَ التي بُعِثَ فيها نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على القطع ، إلى غير ذلك ممَّا ذُكِرَ مِنْ أوصافه التي اشتهر بها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بلا منازع . وفي صحف إشعياء عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ، ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان ، وكمثل حُسْنِ الدساكر والرياض )
Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. So inform the people that Jesus, peace be upon him, is the servant of God Almighty and His messenger, and that the Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels who are near [to Him]. And that it is not for the Most Merciful to take a son. There is none in the heavens and the earth but comes to the Most Merciful as a servant (Qur'an 19:93). And that our Master, Majestic and Exalted, is One, Eternal, He has not begotten nor was He begotten, and there is none comparable to Him. And there has occurred in the Gospel which is in the hands of the disbelievers today similar to what occurred in the Psalms: Jesus, peace be upon him, says in it: 'O God, send the Paraclete to inform the people that the son of man is human.' He will guide the blind hearts. And Isaiah the prophet, peace be upon him, said about God Almighty: 'My servant in whom my soul delights, I will send down my revelation upon him, and he will manifest my justice among the nations with the commandments. He does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets. He opens the blind eyes, and makes the deaf ears hear, and gives life. And what I give him I give to none other. Aḥmad praises God with praise.' Then he pointed to his city Makka and said: 'The wilderness and its inhabitants shall rejoice, they shall praise God on every hill, and magnify Him on every mound. He does not weaken nor is he overcome, nor does he incline to desire, nor is his voice heard in the markets, nor does he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but he strengthens the truthful, and he is the support of the humble, and he is the light of God that is not extinguished nor defeated until my proof is established on earth, and the excuse is cut off, and to his Torah the truth submits.' Look, may God have mercy on you, at this great declaration concerning our Prophet and Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: among them his saying 'He will instruct the nations,' for this necessitates that he was sent to all nations, and that is not established except for our Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. And in the Gospel: the Messiah, peace be upon him, said: 'I was not sent to the Gentiles, but rather I was sent to the sheep that lie down from the descendants of the children of Israel.' And among them is his saying 'Aḥmad praises God,' and this is a clear mention of his name. And among them is his saying 'The wilderness and its inhabitants shall rejoice...' to the end of what he mentioned of its descriptions, and there is no doubt that they are descriptions of Makka in which our Prophet and Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent definitively, besides other things mentioned of his descriptions with which he, may God bless him and grant him peace, is famously known without dispute. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the deserts and the plains delight, for they shall be given by Aḥmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of villages and gardens.'
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures (Tawrat, Zabur, Injil) for the prophethood of Muhammad. The author first establishes the correct Islamic belief about Jesus (servant of God, not son) and God's oneness. Then he notes that the Gospels contain a prophecy similar to that in the Psalms: Jesus prays for the Paraclete to inform people that the son of man is human. Then he quotes Isaiah at length: God speaks of His servant, on whom He will send revelation, who will manifest justice, open blind eyes, etc. The servant is described as one who does not laugh or raise his voice, and he is called 'Ahmad' who praises God. Isaiah then points to Makka and describes its inhabitants praising God on hills and mounds. The servant is gentle but firm, a light not extinguished. The author then analyzes multiple indicators: (1) 'He will instruct the nations' implies universal mission, which is unique to Muhammad; (2) the name 'Ahmad' is explicitly mentioned; (3) the description of the land matches Makka where Muhammad was sent. He concludes that these prophecies are unmistakably about Muhammad. He adds another Isaiah citation specifically mentioning 'Ahmad' and the beauties of Lebanon.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that Jesus prayed for the Paraclete to inform people that he is merely a human servant. Do you truly believe this, or do you sometimes harbor doubts about Jesus's human nature? What specific steps will you take to ensure your heart and mind fully accept this truth?
?
Isaiah described the servant as one who does not laugh or raise his voice in markets, and who does not incline to desire. How does your own behavior compare to this model? Will you commit to adopting one of these traits this week, even if it makes you seem strange to those around you?
?
The prophecy points to Makka as the city of the servant. Yet many Muslims do not actively seek to verify these biblical prophecies. Why have you not personally studied the Bible to find these verses? What would it take for you to begin?

Analyzing the Prophecies: Indicators and Additional Citation
Sanusi analyzes the prophecies and adds another citation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi analyzes the biblical prophecies to confirm that they refer specifically to Prophet Muhammad, and you will see an additional prophecy from Isaiah mentioning Ahmad.

Core Idea
The prophecies point to Muhammad through universal mission, explicit name, and geographic description.

Sanusi now provides a detailed commentary on the prophecies, highlighting three key indicators: the universal instruction of nations, the name Ahmad, and the description of Makka. He then adds another Isaiah citation that specifically names Ahmad.

Guided Path
1
Read Sanusi's analysis introduction
Read the sentence 'Look, may God have mercy on you, at this great declaration...' to understand that he is now explaining the prophecies.
2
Identify the three indicators
Find the three indicators he lists: 1) 'He will instruct the nations' (universal mission), 2) 'Ahmad praises God' (name), 3) description of the land (Makka).
He also notes that Jesus was sent only to the children of Israel.
3
Understand the argument for universal mission
Notice that Sanusi argues that only Muhammad was sent to all nations, not Jesus.
This is a key point of distinction.
4
Read the additional Isaiah citation
Read the final lines where Sanusi quotes another prophecy: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice... for they shall be given by Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon.'
This further confirms the name Ahmad and the blessings.

محمداً صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فأعلم الناس أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام عبد الله تعالى ورسوله ، وأنَّه لن يستنكف المسيحُ أنْ يكونَ عبداً الله ولا الملائكةُ المقرَّبونَ ، وأنَّهُ ما كانَ للرحمن أن يتَّخذ ولداً ، إن كُلُّ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ إِلَّا وَانِي الرَّحْمَنِ عَبْدًا) [مريم : ٩٣) ، وأن مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ أحدٌ صمدٌ ، لم يلد ولم يُولد ، ولم يكن له كفواً أحد . وقد وقع في الإنجيل التي هي بأيدي الكفرة اليوم نظير ما وقع في الزَّبورِ ، يقول فيه عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( اللهم ؛ ابعث البارقليط ليُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ ابنَ الإنسان بشرٌ ) يوصي القلوبَ الغُلْفَ وقال إشعياء النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهرُ في الأمم عدلي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسْمَعُ صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسمعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمد يحمد الله حمداً ) ثم أشار إلى بلدِهِ مكَّةَ فقالَ : ( تفرح البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها يُهلِّلُونَ اللَّهَ على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبِّرُونَهُ على كلِّ رابيةٍ ، لا يَضْعُفُ ولا يُغْلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسْمَعُ في الأسواق صوتُه ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يقوي الصِّدِّيقين ، وهو ركن المتواضعين ، وهو نورُ اللهِ الذي لا يُطفأُ ولا يُخصَمُ حتى تثبتَ بالأرضِ حُجَّتي ، وينقطع به العذرُ ، وإلى توراته ينقاد الحق )) انظر رحمَكَ الله إلى هذا التصريح العظيم بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ غيرِ ما وجه : منها قوله : ( يوصي الأمم ) ، فإنَّ هذا يقتضي أنَّهُ بُعِثَ لجميعِ الأممِ ، ولم يثبت ذلك إلا لسيدنا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وفي الإنجيل : أنَّ المسيح عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : ( إني لم أبعَثْ إلى الأجناس ، وإِنَّما بُعِثْتُ إلى الغنم الرابضة مِنْ نسل بني إسرائيل ) ومنها قوله : ( أحمد يحمد الله ) ، وهذا تصريح باسمه . ومنها قوله : ( تفرحُ البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها ... ) إلى آخرِ ما ذكرَهُ مِنْ أوصافها ، ولا خفاءَ أنَّها أوصافُ مكَّةَ التي بُعِثَ فيها نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على القطع ، إلى غير ذلك ممَّا ذُكِرَ مِنْ أوصافه التي اشتهر بها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بلا منازع . وفي صحف إشعياء عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ، ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان ، وكمثل حُسْنِ الدساكر والرياض )
Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. So inform the people that Jesus, peace be upon him, is the servant of God Almighty and His messenger, and that the Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels who are near [to Him]. And that it is not for the Most Merciful to take a son. There is none in the heavens and the earth but comes to the Most Merciful as a servant (Qur'an 19:93). And that our Master, Majestic and Exalted, is One, Eternal, He has not begotten nor was He begotten, and there is none comparable to Him. And there has occurred in the Gospel which is in the hands of the disbelievers today similar to what occurred in the Psalms: Jesus, peace be upon him, says in it: 'O God, send the Paraclete to inform the people that the son of man is human.' He will guide the blind hearts. And Isaiah the prophet, peace be upon him, said about God Almighty: 'My servant in whom my soul delights, I will send down my revelation upon him, and he will manifest my justice among the nations with the commandments. He does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets. He opens the blind eyes, and makes the deaf ears hear, and gives life. And what I give him I give to none other. Aḥmad praises God with praise.' Then he pointed to his city Makka and said: 'The wilderness and its inhabitants shall rejoice, they shall praise God on every hill, and magnify Him on every mound. He does not weaken nor is he overcome, nor does he incline to desire, nor is his voice heard in the markets, nor does he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but he strengthens the truthful, and he is the support of the humble, and he is the light of God that is not extinguished nor defeated until my proof is established on earth, and the excuse is cut off, and to his Torah the truth submits.' Look, may God have mercy on you, at this great declaration concerning our Prophet and Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: among them his saying 'He will instruct the nations,' for this necessitates that he was sent to all nations, and that is not established except for our Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. And in the Gospel: the Messiah, peace be upon him, said: 'I was not sent to the Gentiles, but rather I was sent to the sheep that lie down from the descendants of the children of Israel.' And among them is his saying 'Aḥmad praises God,' and this is a clear mention of his name. And among them is his saying 'The wilderness and its inhabitants shall rejoice...' to the end of what he mentioned of its descriptions, and there is no doubt that they are descriptions of Makka in which our Prophet and Master Muḥammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent definitively, besides other things mentioned of his descriptions with which he, may God bless him and grant him peace, is famously known without dispute. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the deserts and the plains delight, for they shall be given by Aḥmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of villages and gardens.'
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures (Tawrat, Zabur, Injil) for the prophethood of Muhammad. The author first establishes the correct Islamic belief about Jesus (servant of God, not son) and God's oneness. Then he notes that the Gospels contain a prophecy similar to that in the Psalms: Jesus prays for the Paraclete to inform people that the son of man is human. Then he quotes Isaiah at length: God speaks of His servant, on whom He will send revelation, who will manifest justice, open blind eyes, etc. The servant is described as one who does not laugh or raise his voice, and he is called 'Ahmad' who praises God. Isaiah then points to Makka and describes its inhabitants praising God on hills and mounds. The servant is gentle but firm, a light not extinguished. The author then analyzes multiple indicators: (1) 'He will instruct the nations' implies universal mission, which is unique to Muhammad; (2) the name 'Ahmad' is explicitly mentioned; (3) the description of the land matches Makka where Muhammad was sent. He concludes that these prophecies are unmistakably about Muhammad. He adds another Isaiah citation specifically mentioning 'Ahmad' and the beauties of Lebanon.

Key Terms
يوصي الأمم
أحمد
مكة
إشعياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That biblical prophecies about Muhammad are vague or require forced interpretation.
Correction: Sanusi argues the prophecies are explicit and contain clear indicators: universal mission, name Ahmad, and description of Makka.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the significance of the phrase 'He will instruct the nations' in the prophecy?
A) It shows he will teach the Jewish law
B) It shows he was sent to all nations, which is unique to Muhammad
C) It shows he will instruct angels
D) It shows he will be a teacher in synagogues

Key Takeaway
Sanusi identifies three clear indicators in the prophecies—universal mission, the name Ahmad, and the location Makka—plus an additional prophecy confirming Ahmad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophecies clearly mention the name 'Ahmad' and describe Makka. Have you ever considered that the clarity of these prophecies demands a personal response? In what way is your heart still hesitant to fully embrace the truth of Muhammad's prophethood, despite the overwhelming evidence? What step will you take today to remove that hesitation?
?
Jesus said he was sent only to the children of Israel, but Muhammad was sent to all nations. Does your concern for others reflect that universal mission, or are you still exclusive in your care? Think of one person you have ignored; what will you do to show them the mercy of this Prophet?
?
The prophecy says the desert dwellers rejoice. Do you genuinely rejoice in the message of Muhammad, or has familiarity dulled your gratitude? Ask yourself: when was the last time your heart felt real joy upon hearing his name or his teachings? Commit to renewing that joy today.

Prophethood

Universal Mission and Name Ahmad in Torah and Gospel
Sanusi presents three proofs from Torah and Gospel foretelling Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses biblical prophecies to prove Muhammad's universal mission, his name Ahmad, and the description of Mecca.

Core Idea
Earlier scriptures point to Muhammad by name, mission, and homeland.

Sanusi begins his argument from previous scriptures by pointing to explicit prophecies. He highlights a declaration about a prophet sent to all nations, the name 'Ahmad,' and a barren land that will rejoice — unmistakably Mecca. This lesson examines these three proofs from the Torah and Gospel.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening declaration
Start by reading the initial lines about the unextinguishable light and the call to look at the great declaration. Understand that this sets the stage for the proofs.
2
Identify the first proof: universal mission
Find the phrase 'He commands the nations' and note that Sanusi says this implies a prophet sent to all nations, unique to Muhammad.
Contrast with Jesus's limited mission stated in the Gospel.
3
Identify the second proof: name 'Ahmad'
Locate where the text says 'Ahmad praises God' and recognize this as a clear mention of Muhammad's name.
4
Identify the third proof: description of Mecca
Find the description of the barren land that rejoices and note that Sanusi identifies it as Mecca without doubt.
Consider how this matches the state of Mecca before prophethood.
5
Reflect on the cumulative argument
Think about how these three distinct proofs from Torah and Gospel together form a strong case for Muhammad's prophethood.

حُسْنِ الدساكر والرياض ((٣) فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمِهِ ، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجودِهِ ونشأته فيها ، وبعثه منها ومعنى كونها عطشى ؛ أي: مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ لأنَّ بلدهم معظم الشام ، ومكَّةُ كَانَتْ مهملةً مِنَ النبوَّةِ مِنْ عهد إسماعيل عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ، فأعطى الله سبحانه لمكَّةَ ببعثِ أشرفِ الخَلْقِ منها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ محاسن لبنان ؛ أي : الشامِ ؛ لأن لبنانَ مِنْ جباله وفي صحفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( أَتَتْ أيامُ الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثم قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلينَ : أَنَّ مَنْ تسمُّونَهُ ضالاً .. هو صاحبُ النبوَّةِ ، تفترونَ ذلكَ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((١) وفي صحفِ حِزْقِيالَ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : يقولُ اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بعد ما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمَةِ ؛ وهي شجرة العنب ، وقال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكرمةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسخطة ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض ، وأحرقَتِ السمائمُ ثمارها (٢) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غَرْسٌ في البدْهِ ، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نارٌ أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمَةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَدْ فيها غصن قوي ولا قضيب )(٣) .
The pillar of the humble, and it is the light of God that is not extinguished and is not refuted until my proof is established on the earth, and by it the excuse is cut off, and to His Torah the truth submits. (1) Look, may God have mercy on you, at this great declaration concerning our Prophet and our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: among them is His saying: 'He commands the nations' – for this implies that he was sent to all nations, and that is not established except for our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. And in the Gospel: that the Messiah, peace be upon him, said: 'I was not sent to the Gentiles, but only to the lost sheep of the offspring of the Children of Israel.' (2) And among them is His saying: 'Ahmad praises God' – and this is a clear mention of his name. And among them is His saying: 'The desert and its inhabitants will rejoice...' to the end of what he mentioned of its descriptions, and there is no doubt that they are the descriptions of Mecca, in which our Prophet and our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent, with certainty, besides other descriptions of him that he became famous for, may God bless him and grant him peace, without dispute. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the deserts and wastelands be glad; for they will be given by Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of villages and gardens.' (3) Then also look at this clear declaration of his name, and at what God Almighty honored his city Mecca with, due to the blessing of his existence and his upbringing in it, and his being sent from it, and the meaning of its being 'thirsty' – that is, devoid of messengers and prophets, peace be upon them – because their land is mostly Syria, and Mecca was neglected from prophethood since the time of Ishmael, peace be upon him. So God, glorified is He, gave to Mecca, by sending the most noble of creation from it, may God bless him and grant him peace, the beauties of Lebanon – that is, Syria – because Lebanon is from its mountains. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, also peace be upon him: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come,' then he said: 'Let it be known to you, O ignorant Children of Israel, that he whom you call a stray... is the owner of prophethood; you fabricate that because of the abundance of your sins and the greatness of your wickedness.' (1) And in the scriptures of the prophet Ezekiel, peace be upon him: God Almighty says, after mentioning the sins of the Children of Israel and comparing them to a vine – that is, the grape tree – and He said: 'That vine did not last but was plucked up in anger, and thrown upon the earth, and the hot winds burned its fruits. (2) Then, at that time, a planting was planted in the desert, in the neglected thirsty land, and out of its excellent branches came a fire that consumed that vine, until no strong branch or staff was found in it.' (3)
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is an argument from previous scriptures (tahrif notwithstanding) proving the prophethood of Muhammad. The author begins with an introductory phrase describing the prophetic light as unextinguishable. He then calls the reader to notice the explicit prophecy in the Torah (or a book) about Muhammad: 'He commands the nations' – which implies universal mission, unique to Muhammad. He contrasts this with Jesus's statement in the Gospel that he was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel. Next, the author points to the name 'Ahmad' appearing in prophecy, and then to descriptions of a place that match Mecca – a barren land that rejoices. He then quotes Isaiah explicitly mentioning 'Ahmad' and the beauties of Lebanon, interpreting Lebanon as Syria. He explains that Mecca was 'thirsty' for prophets since Ishmael, and God gave it the beauties of Syria through Muhammad. Another Isaiah prophecy speaks of 'days of visitation' and declares that the one called a stray is actually the prophet. Finally, from Ezekiel, the parable of the vine (Israel) being uprooted and a new planting in the desert (Mecca) that sends out fire to consume the vine – symbolizing the succession of prophethood from Israel to Muhammad. The author uses these texts to show that the earlier scriptures foretold Muhammad by name, description, and mission.

الأمم
أحمد
مكّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muslims reject all previous scriptures as corrupted and useless.
Correction: Sanusi actively uses earlier scriptures as evidence, showing that despite alterations, they still contain clear prophecies confirming Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the statement 'He commands the nations' in the earlier scripture imply about Muhammad?
A) He was sent only to the Arabs.
B) He was sent to all nations.
C) He was sent only to the Jews.
D) He was sent to the Israelites first.

Key Takeaway
The Torah and Gospel contain clear prophecies about Muhammad's universal mission, his name, and his homeland, confirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Torah and Gospel announced Muhammad’s name and mission centuries before his birth. If you truly believe this, why do you still hesitate to fully embody the message of Islam in your daily life? What concrete step will you take today to honour this foretold prophethood?
?
Jesus was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel, but you have been sent to every nation through Muhammad's universal message. Are you actively sharing this message with those around you, or do you keep it to yourself? When will you start?
?
Sanusi calls this 'the light of God that is not extinguished.' Has that light illuminated your heart to the point that your actions reflect certainty? If not, what darkness are you still holding onto that dims it?

Isaiah and Ezekiel's Prophecies of Muhammad and the New Planting
Sanusi interprets Isaiah and Ezekiel prophecies as foretelling Muhammad and the rise of Islam in Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the prophecies of Isaiah and Ezekiel to point to Muhammad and the rise of Islam in Mecca.

Core Idea
Isaiah explicitly names 'Ahmad' and describes Mecca's transformation; Ezekiel's vine parable foretells the shift of prophethood from Israel to Arabia.

Sanusi continues his argument from earlier scriptures, now turning to Isaiah and Ezekiel. In Isaiah, he finds another explicit mention of 'Ahmad' and a description of a barren land receiving the beauties of Lebanon. In Ezekiel, a parable of a vine being replaced by a new planting in the desert symbolizes the transfer of prophethood from the Children of Israel to the Arabs. This lesson explores these prophecies and their interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the first Isaiah prophecy
Read the Isaiah quote about the thirsty desert rejoicing and receiving beauties of Lebanon by Ahmad. Note the explicit name and the description of the land.
2
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Recognize that 'thirsty' means lacking prophets from Ishmael's time and 'beauties of Lebanon' refers to Syria, which Mecca was given through Muhammad.
3
Read the second Isaiah prophecy
Find the portion about 'days of visitation' and the rebuke to those who call the prophet a stray. Understand it as a warning to the Children of Israel.
4
Study the Ezekiel parable
Read the parable of the vine (Israel) that is uprooted and burned, and a new planting in the desert that sends out fire to consume it.
5
Reflect on the symbolism
Consider how the vine represents Israel's prophethood and the new planting represents Muhammad's mission from Mecca, symbolizing a transfer of divine favor.

اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ غيرِ ما وجه : منها قوله : ( يوصي الأمم ) ، فإنَّ هذا يقتضي أنَّهُ بُعِثَ لجميعِ الأممِ ، ولم يثبت ذلك إلا لسيدنا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وفي الإنجيل : أنَّ المسيح عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : ( إني لم أبعَثْ إلى الأجناس ، وإِنَّما بُعِثْتُ إلى الغنم الرابضة مِنْ نسل بني إسرائيل )(٢) ومنها قوله : ( أحمد يحمد الله ) ، وهذا تصريح باسمه . ومنها قوله : ( تفرحُ البريَّةُ ، وسُكَانُها ... ) إلى آخرِ ما ذكرَهُ مِنْ أوصافها ، ولا خفاءَ أنَّها أوصافُ مكَّةَ التي بُعِثَ فيها نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على القطع ، إلى غير ذلك ممَّا ذُكِرَ مِنْ أوصافه التي اشتهر بها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بلا منازع . وفي صحف إشعياء عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ، ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان ، وكمثل حُسْنِ الدساكر والرياض ((٣) فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمِهِ ، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجودِهِ ونشأته فيها ، وبعثه منها ومعنى كونها عطشى ؛ أي: مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ لأنَّ بلدهم معظم الشام ، ومكَّةُ كَانَتْ مهملةً مِنَ النبوَّةِ مِنْ عهد إسماعيل عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ، فأعطى الله سبحانه لمكَّةَ ببعثِ أشرفِ الخَلْقِ منها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ محاسن لبنان ؛ أي : الشامِ ؛ لأن لبنانَ مِنْ جباله وفي صحفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( أَتَتْ أيامُ الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثم قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلينَ : أَنَّ مَنْ تسمُّونَهُ ضالاً .. هو صاحبُ النبوَّةِ ، تفترونَ ذلكَ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((١) وفي صحفِ حِزْقِيالَ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : يقولُ اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بعد ما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمَةِ ؛ وهي شجرة العنب ، وقال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكرمةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسخطة ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض ، وأحرقَتِ السمائمُ ثمارها (٢) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غَرْسٌ في البدْهِ ، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نارٌ أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمَةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَدْ فيها غصن قوي ولا قضيب )(٣) .
The pillar of the humble, and it is the light of God that is not extinguished and is not refuted until my proof is established on the earth, and by it the excuse is cut off, and to His Torah the truth submits. (1) Look, may God have mercy on you, at this great declaration concerning our Prophet and our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: among them is His saying: 'He commands the nations' – for this implies that he was sent to all nations, and that is not established except for our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. And in the Gospel: that the Messiah, peace be upon him, said: 'I was not sent to the Gentiles, but only to the lost sheep of the offspring of the Children of Israel.' (2) And among them is His saying: 'Ahmad praises God' – and this is a clear mention of his name. And among them is His saying: 'The desert and its inhabitants will rejoice...' to the end of what he mentioned of its descriptions, and there is no doubt that they are the descriptions of Mecca, in which our Prophet and our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent, with certainty, besides other descriptions of him that he became famous for, may God bless him and grant him peace, without dispute. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the deserts and wastelands be glad; for they will be given by Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of villages and gardens.' (3) Then also look at this clear declaration of his name, and at what God Almighty honored his city Mecca with, due to the blessing of his existence and his upbringing in it, and his being sent from it, and the meaning of its being 'thirsty' – that is, devoid of messengers and prophets, peace be upon them – because their land is mostly Syria, and Mecca was neglected from prophethood since the time of Ishmael, peace be upon him. So God, glorified is He, gave to Mecca, by sending the most noble of creation from it, may God bless him and grant him peace, the beauties of Lebanon – that is, Syria – because Lebanon is from its mountains. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, also peace be upon him: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come,' then he said: 'Let it be known to you, O ignorant Children of Israel, that he whom you call a stray... is the owner of prophethood; you fabricate that because of the abundance of your sins and the greatness of your wickedness.' (1) And in the scriptures of the prophet Ezekiel, peace be upon him: God Almighty says, after mentioning the sins of the Children of Israel and comparing them to a vine – that is, the grape tree – and He said: 'That vine did not last but was plucked up in anger, and thrown upon the earth, and the hot winds burned its fruits. (2) Then, at that time, a planting was planted in the desert, in the neglected thirsty land, and out of its excellent branches came a fire that consumed that vine, until no strong branch or staff was found in it.' (3)
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is an argument from previous scriptures (tahrif notwithstanding) proving the prophethood of Muhammad. The author begins with an introductory phrase describing the prophetic light as unextinguishable. He then calls the reader to notice the explicit prophecy in the Torah (or a book) about Muhammad: 'He commands the nations' – which implies universal mission, unique to Muhammad. He contrasts this with Jesus's statement in the Gospel that he was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel. Next, the author points to the name 'Ahmad' appearing in prophecy, and then to descriptions of a place that match Mecca – a barren land that rejoices. He then quotes Isaiah explicitly mentioning 'Ahmad' and the beauties of Lebanon, interpreting Lebanon as Syria. He explains that Mecca was 'thirsty' for prophets since Ishmael, and God gave it the beauties of Syria through Muhammad. Another Isaiah prophecy speaks of 'days of visitation' and declares that the one called a stray is actually the prophet. Finally, from Ezekiel, the parable of the vine (Israel) being uprooted and a new planting in the desert (Mecca) that sends out fire to consume the vine – symbolizing the succession of prophethood from Israel to Muhammad. The author uses these texts to show that the earlier scriptures foretold Muhammad by name, description, and mission.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muslims believe that all previous scriptures are completely corrupted and contain no truth.
Correction: Sanusi uses these scriptures as evidence, showing that they still contain prophecies that confirm Muhammad, despite later alterations.

Checkpoint
According to the Ezekiel prophecy in the passage, what happened to the vine (Israel) after it was uprooted?
A) It was replanted.
B) It was consumed by fire from a new planting.
C) It was given to another nation.
D) It remained barren.

Key Takeaway
Isaiah and Ezekiel's prophecies foretell Muhammad by name and depict the transfer of prophethood from Israel to the Arabian desert.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophecy says the desert dwellers would rejoice. Is your heart rejoicing in the blessing of Muhammad's prophethood, or have you grown complacent? What specific action can you take today to revive that joy?
?
Isaiah rebukes the Israelites for calling the prophet a 'stray.' Are there ways you, despite being Muslim, dismiss or undervalue the Messenger through neglect of his sunnah? Name one sunnah you will commit to reviving this week.
?
Ezekiel's parable shows that the old vine was consumed because of its sins. Seeing that prophethood was transferred from Israel to Arabia, do you truly appreciate the privilege of being from the ummah of the final prophet? How does that awareness change the way you approach your faith today?

6 min
Prophecies of Isaiah and Ezekiel on Muhammad and Mecca
Sanusi cites Isaiah and Ezekiel as clear testimonies to Muhammad's prophethood and Mecca's dignity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the prophecies of Isaiah and Ezekiel as clear testimonies to the prophethood of Muhammad and the honor of Mecca, and how he interprets them in light of Islamic history.

Core Idea
The scriptures of Isaiah and Ezekiel foretell Muhammad and Mecca with startling clarity.

Sanusi invites us to 'look at this clear declaration' from earlier scriptures. He presents two specific passages from the prophets Isaiah and Ezekiel, interpreting them as direct references to Muhammad and the rise of Islam in Mecca. This lesson explores these testimonies and shows how Sanusi reads the Old Testament as confirming Islamic beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage from Sanusi, then the English translation. Notice the flow: introduction, Isaiah citation, Ezekiel citation, and conclusion.
The passage is dense; take your time to see the structure.
2
Identify the two prophecies and their interpretations
The first is from Isaiah: 'The days of visitation have come...' Sanusi interprets this as referring to Muhammad. The second is from Ezekiel: a vine parable replaced by a new planting, which Sanusi reads as the rise of Islam after the rejection of Israel.
Both prophecies are taken from the Jewish scriptures and given new meaning.
3
Understand the meaning of 'thirsty'
Sanusi explains that 'thirsty' means devoid of prophets. Mecca had no prophet since Ishmael, but then received Muhammad, the most honored creation.
This emphasizes the special status of Mecca and the Prophet.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi concludes by connecting the prophecies to the historical defeat and humiliation of the Jews at the hands of Muslims. This shows how the prophecies were fulfilled.
Consider how this argument strengthens belief in Muhammad's prophethood.

فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمِهِ ، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجودِهِ ونشأته فيها ، وبعثه منها ومعنى كونها عطشى ؛ أي: مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ لأنَّ بلدهم معظم الشام ، ومكَّةُ كَانَتْ مهملةً مِنَ النبوَّةِ مِنْ عهد إسماعيل عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ، فأعطى الله سبحانه لمكَّةَ ببعثِ أشرفِ الخَلْقِ منها صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ محاسن لبنان ؛ أي : الشامِ ؛ لأن لبنانَ مِنْ جباله
وفي صحفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( أَتَتْ أيامُ الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثم قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلينَ : أَنَّ مَنْ تسمُّونَهُ ضالاً .. هو صاحبُ النبوَّةِ ، تفترونَ ذلكَ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم )
وفي صحفِ حِزْقِيالَ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام : يقولُ اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بعد ما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمَةِ ؛ وهي شجرة العنب ، وقال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكرمةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسخطة ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض ، وأحرقَتِ السمائمُ ثمارها ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غَرْسٌ في البدْهِ ، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نارٌ أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمَةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَدْ فيها غصن قوي ولا قضيب )
فاعتبر رحمَكَ اللهُ تعالى بهذا التصريح العظيم به وبصفة بلدِهِ مكَّةَ ، والتصريح بما وقع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مع اليهود بني إسرائيلَ مِنْ تمكينه تعالى لهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ منهم بالقتل الذريع
والسبي ، والإذلالِ لهم بضَرْبِ الجزية في جميع بلادِ المسلمين .
So look also at this clear declaration concerning his name, and how Allah Almighty honored his city Mecca due to the blessing of his existence and his upbringing in it, and his being sent from it, and the meaning of it being 'thirsty': i.e., devoid of messengers and prophets (peace and blessings be upon them); because their land is mostly Syria, and Mecca was neglected with respect to prophethood since the time of Ishmael (peace and blessings be upon him). So Allah the Exalted gave to Mecca, by sending the most honorable of creation from it (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), the beauties of Lebanon, i.e., Syria; because Lebanon is one of its mountains.
And also in the scriptures of Isaiah (peace and blessings be upon him): 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come.' Then he said: 'That you may know, O ignorant children of Israel, that the one you call a strayer... he is the possessor of prophethood. You fabricate that because of your many sins and great wickedness.'
And in the scriptures of Ezekiel the prophet (peace and blessings be upon him): Allah Almighty says after mentioning the sins of the Children of Israel and comparing them to a vine, which is the grape tree, and He said: 'That vine did not remain but was uprooted in wrath, and cast upon the ground, and the hot winds burned its fruit. Then a planting was planted in the desert, in the neglected thirsty land, and from its excellent branches a fire came out that consumed that vine, until there was found in it no strong branch nor rod.'
So take heed, may Allah Almighty have mercy on you, of this great declaration concerning him and the description of his city Mecca, and the declaration of what happened to him (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) with the Jewish Children of Israel, of His Almighty giving him power over them through devastating killing, captivity, and humiliating them by imposing the jizya in all the lands of the Muslims.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures (samiyyat) for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by drawing attention to a clear declaration that names the Prophet and honors Mecca. He explains that Mecca is called 'thirsty' (ʿaṭshā) meaning it was deprived of prophets, while most prophets came from Syria. Then he cites Isaiah: 'The days of visitation have come' – interpreted as the time of Muhammad. Isaiah says that those who call him a strayer are wrong. Then Ezekiel compares Israel to a vine uprooted in wrath, and then a new planting is placed in a neglected thirsty land – interpreted as Mecca. From that planting's branches comes a fire that consumes the old vine – referring to the Prophet's victory over the Jews. The author then urges the reader to consider how this prophecy matches the conquest and humiliation of Jews in Islamic lands. The entire argument follows a pattern: citation, interpretation, and application to Muhammad and his community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Mecca was once 'thirsty'—spiritually barren—then became the most honored city. Think of one area of your life that feels spiritually dry or neglected. Will you let the same Lord who sent the Prophet from Mecca turn that desert into a garden? What is the first step?
?
Ezekiel's prophecy describes a vine (the Jews) consumed by fire from the new planting's branches. That fire—the Prophet's community—continues to spread. Are you a flame that draws others to the truth, or are you content to watch from a distance? Name one person you will invite to learn about Islam this week.

Daniel's Prophecy on False Claimants
Sanusi cites Daniel's prophecy to prove Muhammad's truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the prophecy of Daniel to argue for the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Daniel's prophecy proves Muhammad is a true prophet by contrast.

Sanusi now turns to the scriptures of previous prophets to find external confirmation of Muhammad's truthfulness. He cites a prophecy from Daniel about false claimants and applies it directly to the enduring message of Islam. This is a powerful argument from scriptural consistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the Daniel prophecy
Read the Arabic quote from Daniel's scriptures. Notice the key claims: false claimants' calls do not exceed thirty years, and the Lord swears by His arm that falsehood will not appear.
The term 'arm' is symbolic of power.
2
Understand the inference
Sanusi draws the logical conclusion: a false claimant's mission cannot last more than thirty years. This sets a criterion for testing prophethood.
3
Apply to Muhammad
Muhammad's message has already lasted nearly nine hundred years (at Sanusi's time) and continues. Therefore, he cannot be a false claimant; he is a true prophet.
The argument is based on longevity as a sign of truth.
4
Clarify the metaphor
Sanusi explains that 'arm' in the prophecy means 'power', referencing Quran 38:75 to avoid anthropomorphism.
This shows Sanusi's commitment to tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صحف دانيال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام وقد نعت الكذابينَ وقال فيهم : ( لا تمتدُّ دعوتُهم ، ولا يتم قربانُهم ، وأقسم الربُّ بساعده لا يظهرُ الباطل ، ولا تقومُ لمدَّعِ كاذب دعوةٌ أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثينَ سنة )
فاعتبر مِنْ هذا الكلامِ عدمَ طولِ دعوةِ الكاذبِ أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثينَ سنة ، وهذه دعوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قائمةٌ ظاهرة والحمد لله قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنة ، وهي بفضل الله تعالى باقيةٌ إلى يوم القيامة
ومعنى ( أقسم الربُّ بساعدِهِ ( : أَنَّهُ أقسم بقدرتِهِ ؛ على حد قولِهِ : مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى [ص : ٧٥] أي : بقدرتي
And in the scriptures of Daniel the prophet (peace and blessings be upon him), he described the liars and said concerning them: 'Their call does not extend, nor is their offering completed, and the Lord swore by His arm that falsehood will not appear, and no false claimant will have a call more than thirty years.'
So take heed from this statement: the length of the call of a liar does not exceed thirty years. And this call of our Prophet and Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) is established and apparent, praise be to Allah, for nearly nine hundred years, and it will, by the grace of Allah, remain until the Day of Resurrection.
And the meaning of 'the Lord swore by His arm' is that He swore by His power, according to His statement: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My hands?' [Sād:75] i.e., by My power.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is another prophetic proof, from Daniel, specifically about false claimants. The author quotes Daniel saying that the call of liars does not last more than thirty years, and their offering is not accepted. The Lord swears by His arm (interpreted as power) that falsehood will not prevail. The author then applies this: Muhammad's message has already lasted nearly nine hundred years (at the time of writing) and continues, so he cannot be a false claimant. This is a clear external proof that Muhammad is a true prophet. The author also explains the metaphorical meaning of 'arm' as 'power', citing the Qur'anic verse about God's 'hands' meaning His power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'arm' in the prophecy implies God has a physical body.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that 'arm' means 'power', just as 'hands' in Quran 38:75 means power, avoiding anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
According to the Daniel prophecy, how long can a false claimant's call last at most?
A) Thirty years

C) One hundred years
D) Indefinitely

Key Takeaway
Daniel's prophecy provides a clear criterion for distinguishing true prophets from false ones, and Muhammad's message easily surpasses it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The truth of Muhammad's message has endured for over 1400 years. Yet your own faith waxes and wanes with daily trials. When your personal 'call' seems weak or unanswered, do you use the Prophet's lasting success to strengthen your certainty, or do you let temporary doubts outweigh a 900-year proof? What one change can you make today to align your heart with this evidence?
?
Daniel's prophecy exposes false claimants by their short-lived influence. Are there any beliefs or practices in your life that you cling to merely because they are comfortable but that have no lasting spiritual fruit? Will you examine them honestly in light of what you know about truth's permanence?
?
God swore by His power that falsehood will not prevail. Yet you often fear that your personal efforts for Islam—teaching your children, calling others to good—will be wasted or undone. Does this passage shift your perspective? How can you entrust the outcome to God's promise and act with courage today?

Proof from Daniel: False Prophets Limited to 30 Years
The author cites a prophecy that false prophets' call lasts at most 30 years and contrasts it with Muhammad's enduring call.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecy from Daniel's scriptures that false prophets last at most 30 years serves as evidence for the truth of Muhammad's prophethood, because his call has endured nearly 900 years.

Core Idea
Muhammad's enduring call proves his prophethood.

The author presents a unique proof from the scriptures of Prophet Daniel. In it, false prophets are given a maximum of 30 years for their call to be accepted. The call of Muhammad has lasted nearly 900 years and continues, so it cannot be false. This lesson unpacks that argument and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice how the author first describes the Prophet's victory over the Jews and then quotes Daniel.
The passage starts with an exhortation 'So consider, may Allah have mercy on you...'
2
Understand Daniel's prophecy
Identify the key condition: 'no false claimant will have a call more than thirty years.' This is the premise of the argument.
The phrase 'swore by His arm' is explained as 'by His power'.
3
Apply the logic to Muhammad
Contrast the 30-year limit with the nearly 900 years of Muhammad's call. The conclusion is that Muhammad's call cannot be false, establishing his prophethood.
This is a clear proof from earlier revelation.

فاعتبر رحمَكَ اللهُ تعالى بهذا التصريح العظيم به وبصفة بلدِهِ مكَّةَ ، والتصريح بما وقع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مع اليهود بني إسرائيلَ مِنْ تمكينه تعالى لهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ منهم بالقتل الذريع والسبي ، والإذلالِ لهم بضَرْبِ الجزية في جميع بلادِ المسلمين . وفي صحفِ دانيال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام وقد نعت الكذابينَ وقال فيهم : ( لا تمتدُّ دعوتُهم ، ولا يتم قربانُهم ، وأقسم الربُّ بساعده لا يظهرُ الباطل ، ولا تقومُ لمدَّعِ كاذب دعوةٌ أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثينَ سنة ) فاعتبر مِنْ هذا الكلامِ عدمَ طولِ دعوةِ الكاذبِ أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثينَ سنة ، وهذه دعوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قائمةٌ ظاهرة والحمد لله قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنة ، وهي بفضل الله تعالى باقيةٌ إلى يوم القيامة . ومعنى ( أقسم الربُّ بساعدِهِ ) : أَنَّهُ أقسم بقدرتِهِ ؛ على حد قولِهِ : مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى [ص : ٧٥] أي : بقدرتي
So consider, may Allah have mercy on you, this great declaration concerning him and the description of his city Mecca, and the declaration of what happened to him, peace be upon him, with the Jews of the Children of Israel: that Allah enabled him, peace and blessings be upon him, to destroy them by terrible killing and captivity, and to humiliate them by imposing the jizya in all the lands of the Muslims. And in the scriptures of Daniel the prophet, peace be upon him, he described the liars and said concerning them: (Their call will not extend, nor will their offering be accepted, and the Lord swore by His arm that falsehood will not appear, and no false claimant will have a call more than thirty years.) So consider from this statement that the call of the liar does not last more than thirty years, and this call of our prophet and master Muhammad, peace be upon him, is manifest and apparent, praise be to Allah, for nearly nine hundred years, and it is by the grace of Allah remaining until the Day of Resurrection. And the meaning of 'the Lord swore by His arm' is that He swore by His power; analogous to His saying: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My hands' [Saad:75] meaning: with My power.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is a proof from prophecy, specifically from the scriptures of Daniel (peace be upon him), used to demonstrate the truth of Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins by calling the reader to consider a great declaration concerning the Prophet Muhammad's victory over the Jews in Mecca and his conquests, which included killing, captivity, and the imposition of jizya. Then he cites a text from Daniel's scriptures where Daniel describes false claimants to prophecy, stating that their call will not last more than thirty years. The author then draws the conclusion: since the call of Muhammad has lasted nearly nine hundred years and continues, it cannot be false; therefore it is true. He explains that the phrase 'swore by His arm' means 'by His power,' citing the Qur'anic verse where God says 'with My hands' in a similar sense.

Correction: The author specifies that this is from 'the scriptures of Daniel the prophet,' which are separate prophetic books, not the commonly known revealed books.

?

?
Daniel's prophecy warns that falsehood is short-lived. Look at your own life: are you investing in things that will last beyond thirty years, or are you chasing what will fade? How does this lesson reshape your priorities today?

Daniel's Interpretation of the Stone from Heaven as Prophecy of Muhammad
Daniel's interpretation of the dream identifies the stone as the religion of a prophet in the end times, applied to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream was applied by the author to support the prophethood of Muhammad and the eternal nature of his message.

Core Idea
The stone that crushes all empires is the religion of Muhammad destined to fill the earth.

The author presents a detailed account of Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream, showing how each part of the idol represents successive empires, and the stone represents an everlasting kingdom. He then directly applies this to Prophet Muhammad, highlighting how Muhammad's mission fulfills this prophecy. This passage serves as a proof from scripture for the truth of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read Daniel's description of the idol with its different materials and the stone that smashes it. Notice the vivid imagery and the king's confirmation.
The dream is presented in direct speech.
2
Understand the interpretation
Daniel explains that the idol's parts represent different empires in chronological order. Identify which empire each metal corresponds to.
3
Apply the stone to Muhammad
The stone is interpreted as the religion of a prophet and an everlasting kingdom at the end of time. See how the author explicitly matches this to Muhammad.
The author emphasizes no prophet after Muhammad and no abrogation of his law.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider how this prophecy serves as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood and the universal, eternal nature of Islam.

وقال أيضاً دانيالُ النبي عليه الصلاةُ والسلام وقد سأله الملك بُخْتَنَصَّرُ عن منامة رآها، وطلبَهُ أنْ يخبره بها وبتفسيرها، فقالَ لهُ دانیال عليه الصلاة والسلام : أيُّها الملكُ؛ رأيت صنماً بارع الجمال؛ أعلاهُ مِنْ ذهبٍ، ووسطهُ مِنْ فضةٍ، وأسفلُهُ مِنْ نحاس، وساقاهُ مِنْ حديد، ورجلاه مِنْ فَخَارِ، فبينما أنتَ تنظر إليه قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السماءِ فكسرَهُ، وضرب رأسَ الصنمِ فطحنه ذهبُهُ وفضَّتُهُ ونحاسُهُ وحديده وفَخَارُهُ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الحجرَ رَبَا وعظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرض كلها فقالَ لهُ بُخْتَنصَّرُ : صدقت، فأخبرني بتأويلها فقالَ دانيال عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : أما الصنم فأمم مختلفةٌ؛ في أوَّلِ الزمانِ، وفي وسطه، وفي آخره؛ فالرَّأْسُ مِنَ الذهبِ أَنتَ أيُّها الملكُ، والفضَّةُ ابنُكَ مِنْ بعدِكَ، والنحاس الروم، والحديد الفُرْسُ، والفخَارُ أمَّتانِ ضعيفتانِ تملكهما امرأتان باليمن والشام، والحجر النازلُ مِنَ السماء دين نبي، ومُلْكُ أبدي يكون في آخرِ الزمان، يغلب الأممَ كلّها، ثم يعظُم حتى يملأ الأرض كلها كما ملاها هذا الحجر. فانظر هذا التصريحَ الجليَّ المطابق لسيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ؛ إذْ هو الذي بُعِثَ في آخرِ الزمانِ، وهو الذي نبوَّتُهُ ومُلْكُ أمَّتِهِ أبدي إلى قيام الساعةِ؛ إذ لا نبيَّ بعدَهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، ولا نسْخَ لشرعِهِ الشريف ما بقيَتِ الدنيا، وهو الذي بُعِثَ إلى الأمم، وظهر عليها كلّها، وخلط بين أجناسها، وجعلها على اختلاف أديانها واختلافِ لغاتِها جنساً واحداً، وعلى لغة واحدة، جميع
And also Daniel the prophet, peace be upon him, said when King Nebuchadnezzar asked him about a dream he had seen and requested that he inform him of it and its interpretation. Daniel, peace be upon him, said to him: 'O king, you saw an idol of perfect beauty; its head was of gold, its middle of silver, its lower part of brass, its legs of iron, and its feet of clay. While you were looking at it, amazed by it, suddenly a stone fell from heaven and broke it, struck the head of the idol and ground its gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay into powder. Then the stone grew and became great until it filled the whole earth.' Nebuchadnezzar said to him: 'You have spoken truthfully; tell me its interpretation.' Daniel, peace be upon him, said: 'As for the idol, it is different nations: in the beginning, middle, and end. The head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the brass is the Romans; the iron is the Persians; the clay are two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria. The stone that fell from heaven is the religion of a prophet and an everlasting kingdom which will come at the end of time. It will overcome all nations, then grow until it fills the entire earth, just as this stone filled it.' So look at this clear declaration that corresponds to our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him, for he is the one sent in the end of time, and his prophethood and the kingdom of his community are everlasting until the Hour, for there is no prophet after him, peace be upon him, and no abrogation of his noble law as long as the world remains. He is the one sent to all nations, and he overcame them all, mixing their races and making them, despite their different religions and languages, one race and one language, all [of them].
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is another proof from prophecy, recounting Daniel's interpretation of King Nebuchadnezzar's dream. The author first narrates the dream: a magnificent idol with different materials (gold, silver, brass, iron, clay) is destroyed by a stone from heaven that grows to fill the whole earth. Daniel interprets the idol as successive empires: Nebuchadnezzar (gold), his son (silver), Romans (brass), Persians (iron), and two weak nations ruled by women (clay). The stone is interpreted as the religion of a prophet and an everlasting kingdom that will come in the end times, overcoming all nations. The author then applies this directly to Muhammad: he is the prophet sent at the end of time, his prophethood and community's kingdom are everlasting (since no prophet after him and no abrogation of his law), he was sent to all nations and overcame them, and he united diverse peoples into one community under one language (Arabic) and one religion. The author emphasizes the perfect match between Daniel's prophecy and Muhammad's mission.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Daniel's prophecy refers to a different religion or kingdom.
Correction: The author argues it specifically matches Islam and Muhammad's ummah, as the stone represents an everlasting kingdom at the end of time, which fits Muhammad's prophethood and the eternal nature of his message.

Key Takeaway
Daniel's prophecy of the stone from heaven foretells the coming of Muhammad and the everlasting dominion of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The stone from heaven shattered the idol of earthly empires. What 'idol' in your own life—such as pride in your status, wealth, or lineage—needs to be crushed by the religion of Muhammad? Will you let it be broken today?
?
Daniel described an everlasting kingdom that fills the earth. Are you actively contributing to spreading that kingdom, or are you content to let others carry the burden while you remain passive?
?
The author says Muhammad united diverse nations into one community under one language (Arabic). In your interactions with Muslims of different backgrounds, do you still hold onto ethnic or cultural divisions, or do you truly see them as part of the same ummah? What one step can you take this week to break down that barrier?

Nebuchadnezzar's Dream and Daniel's Interpretation
Sanusi recounts the dream and Daniel's interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream as a scriptural prophecy pointing to an eternal kingdom.

Core Idea
The stone that destroys the statue symbolizes the eternal kingdom of Islam.

Sanusi draws from the Old Testament story of Nebuchadnezzar's dream to provide a prophecy of Muhammad's mission. The dream, interpreted by Daniel, describes a succession of kingdoms culminating in a divine stone that fills the earth. This lesson unpacks the dream and its interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage describing the dream and Daniel's interpretation. Note the structure of the statue and the stone.
The dream is from the Book of Daniel.
2
Identify the symbolism of each metal
List the metals (gold, silver, copper, iron, pottery) and the kingdoms they represent according to Daniel.
The head of gold is Nebuchadnezzar himself.
3
Understand Daniel's interpretation
Focus on Daniel's explanation that the stone is a divine kingdom that will destroy all others and fill the earth.
4
Reflect on the eternal kingdom
Consider how the stone represents an eternal, all-conquering kingdom from heaven, not a human empire.
This sets the stage for Sanusi's application to Muhammad.

Iron, and its legs of pottery. While you were looking at it, admiring it, a stone from heaven came down and broke it, and struck the head of the idol and crushed its gold, silver, copper, iron, and pottery. Then the stone grew and became great until it filled all the earth. Nebuchadnezzar said to him: You have spoken truly, so tell me its interpretation. Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Muhammad's prophethood via scriptural prophecy from the Old Testament, as interpreted by Daniel. It begins by recounting Nebuchadnezzar's dream of a statue with head of gold, chest and arms of silver, belly and thighs of copper, legs of iron, and feet partly iron and partly clay. A stone from heaven smashes the whole statue and grows to fill the earth. Daniel interprets the dream: the metals represent successive kingdoms — the golden head is Nebuchadnezzar, silver his son, copper the Romans, iron the Persians, and the clay two weak kingdoms ruled by women. The stone is a prophet's eternal kingdom at the end of time. Sanusi then explains how this matches Muhammad exactly: he was sent at the end of time, his prophethood and community's dominion are eternal (no prophet after him, no abrogation of his law), he was sent to all nations and unified them under one religion (Islam) and one language (Arabic) for worship. Sanusi concludes that the previous scriptures' testimonies to Muhammad are countless and his status is clearer than the sun.

?

?

?
Nebuchadnezzar's dream showed that human empires rise and fall, but the kingdom of God endures. Sanusi's Application to Muhammad
Sanusi applies Daniel's interpretation to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi identifies the stone in Daniel's vision with the prophethood of Muhammad and his eternal community.

Core Idea
Muhammad's prophethood is the eternal kingdom foretold by Daniel.

After presenting Daniel's interpretation, Sanusi explicitly applies the prophecy to the Prophet Muhammad. He highlights how Muhammad was sent at the end of time, his law is eternal, and he united all nations under Islam. This lesson examines that application and the overwhelming evidence from previous scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read Sanusi's application
Read the Arabic passage where Sanusi explicitly links the stone to Muhammad (peace be upon him).
The phrase 'فانظر هذا التصريح' signals the direct application.
2
Identify the parallels to Muhammad
Notice how Sanusi draws parallels: Muhammad sent at the end of time, eternal prophethood and law, sent to all nations, unifying them.
3
Reflect on the unity of language and religion
Sanusi emphasizes that all Muslims recite the Quran in Arabic and follow one religion, Islam, as a fulfillment of the prophecy.
This shows the universal and unified nature of the Islamic community.
4
Understand the conclusion about previous scriptures
Sanusi states that the previous books contain countless testimonies to Muhammad's prophethood, clearer than the sun.
This reinforces the certainty of the prophecy.

حديد ، ورجلاه مِنْ فَخَارِ ، فبينما أنتَ تنظر إليه قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السماءِ فكسرَهُ ، وضرب رأسَ الصنمِ فطحنه ذهبُهُ وفضَّتُهُ ونحاسُهُ وحديده وفَخَارُهُ ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الحجرَ رَبَا وعظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرض كلها فقالَ لهُ بُخْتَنصَّرُ : صدقت ، فأخبرني بتأويلها • وقالَ دانيال عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : أما الصنم فأمم مختلفةٌ ؛ في أوَّلِ الزمانِ ، وفي وسطه ، وفي آخره ؛ فالرأْسُ مِنَ الذهبِ أَنتَ أَيُّها الملكُ ، والفضَّةُ ابنُكَ مِنْ بعدِكَ ، والنحاس الروم، والحديد الفُرْسُ ، والفخَارُ أمَّتانِ ضعيفتانِ تملكهما امرأتان باليمن والشام ، والحجر النازلُ مِنَ السماء دين نبي ، ومُلْكُ أبدي يكون في آخرِ الزمان ، يغلب الأممَ كلّها ، ثم يعظُم حتى يملأ الأرض كلها كما ملاها هذا الحجر فانظر هذا التصريحَ الجليَّ المطابق لسيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ إذْ هو الذي بُعِثَ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، وهو الذي نبوَّتُهُ ومُلْكُ أمَّتِهِ أبدي إلى قيام الساعةِ ؛ إذ لا نبيَّ بعدَهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، ولا نسْخَ لشرعِهِ الشريف ما بقيَتِ الدنيا ، وهو الذي بُعِثَ إلى الأمم، وظهر عليها كلّها ، وخلط بين أجناسها ، وجعلها على اختلاف أديانها واختلافِ لغاتِها جنساً واحداً، وعلى لغة واحدة، ودين واحدٍ ؛ إذْ كلُّهم يقرؤون القرآن بلغة العرب ، وبها يصلُّونَ ، إلى غير ذلكَ ، وكلُّهم يدينون بدين واحدٍ ، وهو دين الإسلام . وبالجملة : فنصوص الكتب السابقة على ثبوتِ نبوَّة سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وتعظيم شأنه ، وإيصاءات الأنبياء الماضينَ عليه ، وإشادتهم ذكرَهُ ، وتبشيراتُ الأحبار به.. لا تكاد تنحصرُ ، وثبوتُ رسالتِهِ وشرفه على كلّ ما خلق الله تعالى .. أجلى مِنَ الشمس
Iron, and its legs of pottery. While you were looking at it, admiring it, a stone from heaven came down and broke it, and struck the head of the idol and crushed its gold, silver, copper, iron, and pottery. Then the stone grew and became great until it filled all the earth. Nebuchadnezzar said to him: You have spoken truly, so tell me its interpretation. And Daniel, peace be upon him, said: As for the idol, it is different nations: at the beginning of time, its middle, and its end. The head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the copper is Rome; the iron is Persia; and the pottery are two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria. The stone coming down from heaven is the religion of a prophet, and an eternal kingdom at the end of time, which will overcome all nations, then grow until it fills all the earth, just as this stone filled it. So look at this clear declaration matching our Master and Lord Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace; for he was sent at the end of time, and his prophethood and the kingdom of his community are eternal until the Day of Resurrection, since there is no prophet after him, may God bless him and grant him peace, and no abrogation of his noble Law as long as the world endures; and he was sent to all nations, and prevailed over all of them, and mixed their races, and made them, despite their different religions and different languages, one nation and one language and one religion; for all of them recite the Quran in the language of the Arabs, and in it they pray, and so forth, and all of them follow one religion, which is the religion of Islam. In summary, the texts of the previous books regarding the establishment of the prophethood of our Master and Lord Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, his exaltation, the charges of the past prophets concerning him, their praise of him, and the tidings of the rabbis about him are almost countless, and the establishment of his messengerhood and his honor over all that God Almighty created is clearer than the sun.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Muhammad's prophethood via scriptural prophecy from the Old Testament, as interpreted by Daniel. It begins by recounting Nebuchadnezzar's dream of a statue with head of gold, chest and arms of silver, belly and thighs of copper, legs of iron, and feet partly iron and partly clay. A stone from heaven smashes the whole statue and grows to fill the earth. Daniel interprets the dream: the metals represent successive kingdoms — the golden head is Nebuchadnezzar, silver his son, copper the Romans, iron the Persians, and the clay two weak kingdoms ruled by women. The stone is a prophet's eternal kingdom at the end of time. Sanusi then explains how this matches Muhammad exactly: he was sent at the end of time, his prophethood and community's dominion are eternal (no prophet after him, no abrogation of his law), he was sent to all nations and unified them under one religion (Islam) and one language (Arabic) for worship. Sanusi concludes that the previous scriptures' testimonies to Muhammad are countless and his status is clearer than the sun.

Key Terms
نبوة محمد
العبادة
الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the previous scriptures do not mention Muhammad by name, so they are not prophecies.
Correction: Sanusi argues that the descriptions in Daniel's dream (e.g., a prophet at the end of time, eternal kingdom) match Muhammad uniquely, and that the previous books contain numerous clear testimonies.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what makes Muhammad's prophethood eternal?
A) He is the last prophet and his law is never abrogated
B) He conquered many lands
C) He performed many miracles
D) He was a descendant of Abraham

Key Takeaway
Sanusi confirms that Muhammad is the eternal prophet foretold by Daniel, whose law and community will endure until the end of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Muhammad's prophethood and community's rule are eternal until the Day of Resurrection, and you are part of that community, how does that shape your priorities today? Will you live as a citizen of this eternal kingdom or as if this world is all there is?
?
Sanusi says the proofs of Muhammad's prophethood are 'clearer than the sun.' Have you ever struggled with doubt about his prophethood? What will you do this week to strengthen your certainty by studying the evidence?
?
The passage describes how Muhammad united nations of different religions and languages into one community under Islam. In your own life, are you actively building unity among Muslims, or do you contribute to division? What specific step will you take today to unite rather than divide?
