Proof of Muhammad's Superiority Through Consensus and Intercession
Sanusi proves Muhammad's superiority via consensus and the major intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses consensus and the unique great intercession to establish Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation.

Core Idea
Muhammad's unmatched rank is proven by universal consensus and his exclusive role in the great intercession.

Sanusi presents a clear proof for the superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all creatures. He begins with the consensus of the community and then offers a compelling argument from the unique role of the major intercession on the Day of Judgment. This lesson examines this proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim and consensus
Read the passage's opening assertion that consensus exists on Muhammad's superiority. Note that Sanusi says the evidences from Quran and Sunnah are countless.
Consensus (ijma) is a strong evidence in Islamic theology.
2
Examine the major intercession argument
Focus on the description of the Day of Judgment: all creatures, including prophets and angels, are terrified. Only Muhammad is entrusted to intercede for relief.
This exclusive role demonstrates his highest rank.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi implies that the greatest messengers themselves seek intercession from Muhammad, showing his station above them.
The passage cuts off, but the implication is clear.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان كون سيدنا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلَ خَلْقِ اللهِ تعالى ] وقد ثبت الإجماع على أنَّهُ أفضلُ مِنْ جميع المخلوقاتِ مِنْ غيرِ استثناء (۱) ، وشواهد ذلكَ مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّة لا تكاد تنحصر ، ولا يُعتدُّ بمَنِ ابتدعَ وحاولَ غير ذلكَ ، ويكفيك في معرفة شرفِهِ وعلوّ منزلته على كل المخلوقات .. ما أُجمِعَ عليهِ مِنْ ثبوتِ شفاعتِهِ الكبرى في مواطن الآخرةِ لإراحةِ الخَلْقِ مِنْ هول المحشرِ وشدائد أهوالِهِ . وقد عُلِمَ أنَّ ذلك الموقف الهائل جمعَ الأولين والآخرين ، وجميع الأنبياء والمرسلين ، وجميع الملائكة والمقرَّبينَ ، وقد عظَمَ خوفُ الجميع على أنفسهم ، واشتدَّ الهولُ اشتداداً لا يمكن وصفه ، وطالَ أمرُه ، وماجَ الخَلْقُ بعضُهم في بعض ، واهتم البُرَاءُ مِنْ كلٌّ عيبٍ - لشدَّة الهول - بأنفسهم ، حتى قالَتْ أكابرُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام
Statement that our Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is the best of God's creation. Consensus has been established that he is the best of all creatures without exception, and the evidences for that from the Book and the Sunnah are almost countless, and no heed is paid to anyone who innovates and attempts otherwise. It suffices you for knowing his honor and high station over all creatures what has been unanimously agreed upon: the confirmation of his great intercession in the stations of the Hereafter to give relief to creation from the terror of the Gathering and the severe horrors thereof. And it is known that that tremendous situation gathered the first and the last, all the prophets and messengers, and all the angels and those brought near; and the fear of all for themselves became great, and the terror intensified beyond description, and its duration lengthened, and the creatures surged into one another, and the pure ones [the righteous/prophets?] — due to the intensity of the terror — concerned themselves with their own selves, until the greatest of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, said...
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the superiority (afḍaliyya) of Muhammad over all creation. Sanusi begins by stating the consensus (ijmaʿ) that Muhammad is the best of all creatures without exception. He notes that the evidences from Quran and Sunnah are countless, and that innovators who deny this are disregarded. Then he offers a sufficient proof: the unanimously agreed fact that Muhammad alone will perform the major intercession (al-shafāʿa al-kubrā) on the Day of Judgment to relieve all creation from the terrors of the Gathering. Sanusi describes the scene: the first and last, all prophets and messengers, all angels and the close ones are gathered, all terrified for themselves, the horror indescribable, even the prophets worry about themselves. At that point, the greatest messengers themselves say... (the text cuts off, implying they seek intercession from Muhammad). Thus, the fact that only Muhammad is entrusted with this intercession proves his rank above all.

Key Terms
أفضل
الإجماع
الشفاعة الكبرى
الموقف الهائل
المحشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Muhammad's superiority is based on miracles alone, or that intercession is a general concept shared by many prophets.
Correction: Sanusi specifically uses the unique major intercession (al-shafāʿa al-kubrā) as the decisive proof, showing that Muhammad is the only one entrusted with it when all others, including the greatest prophets, are in need.

Checkpoint

C) The large number of his followers
D) His wealth and power

Key Takeaway
The unique role of Prophet Muhammad in the great intercession, as agreed upon by consensus, establishes his superiority over all creation.

?
The description of the terror is intense: even the pure ones are concerned only for themselves. Have you ever felt that kind of desperation about your own salvation? If not, what does that say about your awareness of the Hereafter and your reliance on Muhammad's intercession?

Proof of the Prophet's Superiority over All Creation
Proof of Prophet's superiority via consensus and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how consensus and the intercession narrative demonstrate the Prophet Muhammad's unmatched superiority over all creation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession on the Day of Judgment proves he is the most honored by Allah.

This lesson presents the definitive proof for the Prophet's superiority over all creatures. The author begins by citing the consensus of the Muslim community and then delves into the powerful scene of the Great Intercession, where even the greatest prophets defer to him. Through this narrative, we see that Muhammad is uniquely addressed by Allah and given authority over the fates of all creation. The lesson also includes additional hadiths that reinforce his unparalleled rank.

Guided Path
1
Understand the thesis and consensus
Read the opening statement where the author asserts the Prophet is the best of creation and that consensus supports this. Note the dismissal of innovators.
2
Visualize the terror of the gathering
Pay attention to the description of the Day of Judgment: all creation gathered, intense fear, even prophets are terrified for themselves.
This sets the stage for why intercession is needed.
3
Follow the intercession chain to the Prophet
Trace how each prophet declines intercession until it reaches Muhammad (peace be upon him). He says 'I am for it' and prostrates under the Throne.
Notice the contrast between the prophets' fear and the Prophet's confidence.
4
Reflect on the divine address and additional proofs
Consider the honor of being addressed directly by Allah and commanded to intercede. Then review the hadiths about entering Paradise first and the fire being restrained.
These reinforce his unique rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان كونِ سيّدِنا محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلَ خَلْقِ اللهِ تعالى وقد ثبت الإجماع على أنَّهُ أفضلُ مِنْ جميع المخلوقاتِ مِنْ غيرِ استثناء (۱) ، وشواهد ذلكَ مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّة لا تكاد تنحصر ، ولا يُعتدُّ بمَنِ ابتدعَ وحاولَ غير ذلكَ ، ويكفيك في معرفة شرفِهِ وعلوّ منزلته على كل المخلوقات .. ما أُجمِعَ عليهِ مِنْ ثبوتِ شفاعتِهِ الكبرى في مواطن الآخرةِ لإراحةِ الخَلْقِ مِنْ هول المحشرِ وشدائد أهوالِهِ .
وقد عُلِمَ أنَّ ذلك الموقف الهائل جمعَ الأولين والآخرين ، وجميع الأنبياء والمرسلين ، وجميع الملائكة والمقرَّبينَ ، وقد عظَمَ خوفُ الجميع على أنفسهم ، واشتدَّ الهولُ اشتداداً لا يمكن وصفه ، وطالَ أمرُه ، وماجَ الخَلْقُ بعضُهم في بعض ، واهتم البُرَاءُ مِنْ كلٌّ عيبٍ - لشدَّة الهول - بأنفسهم ، حتى قالَتْ أكابرُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام اعتذاراً عندما طُلِبَتْ منهم الشفاعةُ ، كلُّ واحدٍ منهم يقولُ : إِنَّ رَبِّي غضبَ اليوم غضباً شديداً لم يغضب قبله مثله ، ولن يغضب بعدَهُ مثله ، لا أسألُهُ اليوم إلا نفسي ، اذهبوا إلى غيري ، ويتدافعونَ الشفاعةَ مِنْ واحدٍ إلى آخر ، حتى تنتهي إلى عروس المملكة وسِرّها وإكسيرها ، وسيّدِ كلَّ ما خَلَقَ مولانا جل وعزَّ ، فيقولُ : « أَنَا لَهَا ويذهب حتى يسجد تحت العرش ، فيُقالُ لَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تعالى : أَرْفَعْ رَأْسَكَ ، وَقُلْ يُسْمَعْ لَكَ ، وَاشْفَعْ تُشَفَّعْ ، وَسَلْ تُعْطَهُ (۱) ، فانظُرْ رحمَكَ الله تعالى هذا الخطاب العظيمَ لهُ مِنْ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ذلك اليوم الهائل ؛ كيف هو صريح بالمعنى بلا نزاع ولا ريب أنَّه لا أكرم منه على الله تعالى .
وفي الحديث : أَنَّهُ أَوَّلُ مَنْ يقرعُ باب الجنة ، فيقولُ رضوان خازنها عليه السلام : ( مَنْ أَنْتَ ؟ ( فيقولُ : ( مُحَمَّدٌ »، فيقولُ رضوان عليه السلام : « بِكَ أُمِرْتُ أَلا أَفْتَحَ لِأَحَدٍ قَبْلَكَ » ، أو كما قال(۲) : ورُوِيَ ما معناه : أنَّ النارَ عندما تسوقها الملائكةُ الموكلون بها بالسلاسل لتحيط بالخَلْقِ في المحشرِ ، فإذا قرُبَتْ منهم بنحو خمس مئة سنة تشهقُ شهيقاً عظيماً ، ويتفلَّتُ منها عنق طوله خمس مئة سنة ، فم ولسان ، فيصل إلى أهل المحشرِ ويزفر عليهم ويشهقُ شهيقاً له
Statement that our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is the best of Allah's creation. And consensus has been established that he is the best of all creatures without exception (1), and evidences of that from the Book and the Sunnah are almost innumerable, and no regard is given to whoever innovates and attempts otherwise. And sufficient for you in knowing his honor and high station over all creatures is what has been agreed upon from the establishment of his great intercession in the stations of the hereafter to give relief to creation from the terror of the gathering and the severities of its horrors. And it is known that that tremendous situation gathered the first and the last, and all the prophets and messengers, and all the angels and those brought near, and the fear of all for themselves became great, and the terror intensified intensely beyond description, and its matter lengthened, and the creation surged into one another, and the innocent of every defect became concerned - due to the intensity of the terror - about themselves, until the greatest of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, said apologetically when intercession was requested from them, each one of them saying: 'Indeed my Lord is angry today with an anger the like of which He has never been angry before, and He will never be angry the like of it afterwards; I do not ask Him today except for myself; go to someone else.' And they push the intercession away from one to another until it reaches the bride of the kingdom and its secret and its elixir, and the master of everything that our Master, Mighty and Majestic, created, and he says: 'I am for it.' And he goes until he prostrates under the Throne, and it is said to him from Allah Almighty: 'Raise your head, speak and you will be heard, intercede and your intercession will be accepted, ask and you will be given' (1). Then look, may Allah have mercy on you, at this great address to him from our Master, Mighty and Majestic, on that tremendous day; how it is explicit in meaning without dispute or doubt that there is none more honored than him with Allah Almighty. And in the hadith: That he is the first to knock at the door of Paradise, and Ridwan, its keeper, peace be upon him, says: 'Who are you?' He says: 'Muhammad.' And Ridwan, peace be upon him, says: 'I have been commanded not to open for anyone before you,' or as he said (2). And it has been reported, meaning: That when the angels appointed over it drive the fire with chains to surround the creation in the gathering, and when it approaches them to about five hundred years, it sighs a great sigh, and a neck comes out from it, its length five hundred years, with a mouth and a tongue, and it reaches the people of the gathering and blows on them and sighs a sigh.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a proof passage demonstrating the superiority of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) over all creation. The author begins by stating the thesis that the Prophet is the best of Allah's creation, supported by consensus (ijmaʿ) of the Muslim community. He notes that the evidences from Qur'an and Sunnah are innumerable and that innovators who claim otherwise are not considered. He then presents the greatest evidence: the established fact of the Prophet's great intercession (al-shafaʿah al-kubra) in the hereafter, which will relieve creation from the terror of the gathering (al-mahshar). The author describes the scene: all previous and later generations, prophets, messengers, angels are gathered. The terror is so intense that even the greatest prophets each decline intercession, saying 'Go to someone else,' until the intercession reaches the Prophet. He says 'I am for it' (ana laha) and prostrates under the Throne. Then he receives the command: raise his head, speak, intercede, ask. The author reflects that this address shows clearly that none is more honored by Allah than the Prophet. Two additional supporting hadiths are cited: that the Prophet will be the first to enter Paradise, and a hadith describing the fire being brought with a neck that terrifies the people. These reinforce his unique rank and authority.

Key Terms
أفضل الخلق
الشفاعة الكبرى
الإجماع
المحشر
العرش
رضوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the intercession is only for his community, but the passage shows it is for all creation to relieve the terror.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the intercession is for the relief of all creation from the horror of the gathering, not just his followers.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet say when the intercession ultimately reaches him?
A) أنا لها (I am for it)
B) اذهبوا إلى غيري (Go to someone else)
C) لا أسأله اليوم إلا نفسي (I ask only for myself today)
D) ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة (Our Lord, give us good in this world)

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unique role in intercession, confirmed by consensus and the Qur'an, establishes his supremacy over all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage describes how even the greatest prophets trembled in fear on that day. If they were so terrified, how would you fare? What have you done today to prepare for that moment when you will stand alone before your Lord?
?
The Prophet said 'أنا لها' (I am for it) and prostrated under the Throne. His humility and readiness to intercede reflect his perfect character. In what area of your life are you holding back from prostrating in submission? Will you, like the Prophet, step forward when others retreat?
?
Allah honored the Prophet with a direct address and granted him the great intercession. If you knew that you could be among those who receive his intercession, what would you change in your daily life to ensure you are worthy of his love and concern?

Prophethood
beginner

The Prophet's Supreme Intercession on the Day of Judgment
Sanusi narrates the hadith of intercession culminating in the Prophet's unique role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's unique intercession on the Day of Judgment demonstrates his supreme rank with Allah.

Core Idea
The Prophet is the most honored creation, as shown by his exclusive role in intercession.

The Day of Judgment is a day of immense fear and awe. Even the greatest prophets and angels are overwhelmed by Allah's wrath, directing the people away from themselves. But the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is singled out to intercede, receiving a direct command from Allah that leaves no doubt about his unparalleled status. This passage from Sanusi's work narrates this powerful hadith to establish the Prophet's unique honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete hadith narrative
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Let the story unfold without immediate analysis.
Notice the sequence: prophets and angels pass the request until it reaches the Prophet.
2
Observe the contrast in responses
Compare the response of the other prophets and angels ('I only ask for myself') with the Prophet's response ('I am for it'). The contrast highlights his unique bravery and station.
The other figures are overwhelmed by Allah's anger, while the Prophet steps forward.
3
Reflect on the honorific language and divine address
Consider the metaphors ('bride of the kingdom', 'secret', 'elixir') and the direct command from Allah. How do these prove the Prophet's unmatched honor?
The author invites you to 'look' and see the evidence.

اعتذاراً عندما طُلِبَتْ منهم الشفاعةُ ، كلُّ واحدٍ منهم يقولُ : إِنَّ رَبِّي غضبَ اليوم غضباً شديداً لم يغضب قبله مثله ، ولن يغضب بعدَهُ مثله ، لا أسألُهُ اليوم إلا نفسي ، اذهبوا إلى غيري ، ويتدافعونَ الشفاعةَ مِنْ واحدٍ إلى آخر ، حتى تنتهي إلى عروس المملكة وسِرّها وإكسيرها ، وسيّدِ كلَّ ما خَلَقَ مولانا جل وعزَّ ، فيقولُ : « أَنَا لَهَا ويذهب حتى يسجد تحت العرش ، فيُقالُ لَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تعالى : أَرْفَعْ رَأْسَكَ ، وَقُلْ يُسْمَعْ لَكَ ، وَاشْفَعْ تُشَفَّعْ ، وَسَلْ تُعْطَهُ (۱) ، فانظُرْ رحمَكَ الله تعالى هذا الخطاب العظيمَ لهُ مِنْ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ذلك اليوم الهائل ؛ كيف هو صريح بالمعنى بلا نزاع ولا ريب أنَّه لا أكرم منه على الله تعالى .
As an excuse when intercession is asked of them, each one of them says: 'Indeed my Lord is angry today with a severe anger that He has not been angry with before, and He will not be angry after it with the like; I do not ask Him today except for myself; go to other than me.' And they pass the intercession from one to another until it reaches the bride of the kingdom, its secret and its elixir, and the master of all that our Lord, Glorious and Mighty, has created. He says: 'I am for it' and goes until he prostrates under the Throne. Then it is said to him from Almighty Allah: 'Raise your head, speak and you will be heard, intercede and your intercession will be accepted, ask and you will be given (1).' So look, may Allah have mercy on you, at this great address to him from our Lord, Glorious and Mighty, on that tremendous day; how it is explicit in meaning without dispute or doubt that there is none more honored than him with Allah.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a narrative from hadith describing the events of intercession on the Day of Judgment. The author presents how each of the great prophets and angels, when asked to intercede, declines due to the overwhelming fear of Allah's anger that day, each saying they are only concerned for themselves and directing the people to others. This continues until the people reach the 'bride of the kingdom, its secret and its elixir' — a metaphor for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as the most beloved and honored creation. He then takes the matter upon himself, goes and prostrates under the Throne, and is honored by Allah with a command to raise his head, speak, intercede, and ask; his intercession is accepted and his request granted. The author draws attention to this as evidence of the Prophet's unmatched rank with Allah on that day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the prophets and angels refuse intercession out of unwillingness or lack of care.
Correction: The hadith shows they are overwhelmed by fear of Allah's anger that day, saying 'I only ask for myself,' which indicates their awe, not unwillingness.

Checkpoint

A) They do not want to help the people.
B) They are not able to intercede.
C) They are overwhelmed by fear of Allah's anger that day.
D) They are saving intercession for later.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's intercession on the Day of Judgment is the clearest proof of his supreme honor with Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Does your heart ever tremble at the thought of standing before Allah, or have you become numb to His greatness? What would it take today for you to truly feel that fear and turn it into hope in the Prophet's intercession?
?
The Prophet said 'I am for it' while every other prophet retreated. Is there a difficult duty in your life—forgiving someone, giving up a sin, or speaking the truth—that you keep passing to others? How can the Prophet's courageous step inspire you to stop passing the responsibility and say 'I am for it'?
?
Allah commanded the Prophet: 'Raise your head, speak, intercede, ask, and you will be given.' Do you live as if you believe that the Prophet is the most honored with Allah? When you sin, do you truly trust that his intercession can reach you, or do you despair of Allah's mercy? What one habit can you change today to show that you rely on the Prophet's intercession?

The Prophet Commands the Fire on the Day of Judgment
Narrative of the Prophet's intercession with Paradise and the Fire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the immense rank of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as demonstrated by his authority over the Fire on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The Prophet commands even the Fire, showing his unparalleled status.

This lesson narrates two powerful scenes from the Hereafter: the Prophet being the first to enter Paradise, and his commanding the Fire to obey him. These events illustrate his supreme intercession and authority granted by Allah. Through these descriptions, we glimpse the honor bestowed upon our Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the sequence of events.
2
Identify the two scenes
Note the first scene about entering Paradise and the second about the Fire's approach.
3
Reflect on the Prophet's role
Consider why the Prophet is able to command the Fire and what this signifies.
4

وفي الحديث : أَنَّهُ أَوَّلُ مَنْ يقرعُ باب الجنة ، فيقولُ رضوان خازنها عليه السلام : ( مَنْ أَنْتَ ؟ ( فيقولُ : ( مُحَمَّدٌ »، فيقولُ رضوان عليه السلام : « بِكَ أُمِرْتُ أَلا أَفْتَحَ لِأَحَدٍ قَبْلَكَ » ، أو كما قالَ(۲) : ورُوِيَ ما معناه : أنَّ النارَ عندما تسوقها الملائكةُ الموكلون بها بالسلاسل لتحيط بالخَلْقِ في المحشرِ ، فإذا قرُبَتْ منهم بنحو خمس مئة سنة تشهقُ شهيقاً عظيماً ، ويتفلَّتُ منها عنق طوله خمس مئة سنة ، فم ولسان ، فيصل إلى أهل المحشرِ ويزفر عليهم ويشهقُ شهيقاً لهُ منكراً لا يُستطاع سماعه ، ويملأُ عليهم الجو ظلمة وناراً زيادةً على ما هم فيهِ مِنَ الأهوالِ الجسيمةِ ، ويلتقط الناسَ مِنَ الموقفِ ويبتلعُهم في ذلك العنق الطويل إلى جوفه ! وحينئذ تجثو الملائكة المقربون والأنبياء والرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام على الرُّكَبِ خوفاً مِنَ اللهِ تعالى ، فحينئذٍ ينهض إلى النارِ سيّد الخَلْقِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فتسمعُ النارُ حينئذ نداءً مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تعالى : اسمعي له وأطيعي
And in the hadith: That he is the first to knock at the door of Paradise. The gatekeeper Ridwan (peace be upon him) says: 'Who are you?' He says: 'Muhammad.' Ridwan says: 'I have been commanded not to open for anyone before you,' or as he said (2). And it is narrated with the meaning: When the Fire is driven by the angels appointed over it with chains to surround the creation in the gathering place, when it comes near them by about five hundred years, it gives a great gasp, and a neck of five hundred years length, with a mouth and a tongue, breaks loose from it. It reaches the people of the gathering, blasts upon them, and gasps with a terrible gasp that cannot be tolerated hearing. It fills the air with darkness and fire in addition to what they are already in of great terrors. It snatches people from the station and swallows them into its depth. At that moment, the angels brought near, the prophets, and the messengers (peace be upon them) fall on their knees in fear of Almighty Allah. Then the master of creation, our Prophet and master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) rises up towards the Fire, and the Fire then hears a call from Almighty Allah: 'Hear and obey him.'
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a narrative combining two hadiths. First, the Prophet will be the first to knock at the gate of Paradise, and Ridwan the gatekeeper will open for him before anyone else. Second, a description of the Fire on the Day of Judgment: it is driven by angels, comes close to the people, and a monstrous neck emerges with a mouth and tongue that seizes people. The terror is such that even the nearest angels and prophets fall on their knees in fear of Allah. But then the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) rises and approaches the Fire, and Almighty Allah commands the Fire to hear and obey him. This demonstrates the Prophet's immense rank and authority, as even the Fire is made subservient to his command.

Correction: They fall in fear of Allah, not the Fire. Their prostration is out of awe and reverence for Him alone.

Disagreement on who is best after the Prophet
Taftazani lists five opinions on who is best after the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five opinions held by scholars about which prophet is best after Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), and why these differences exist based on different virtues.

Core Idea
Scholars disagree on who is best after Muhammad, but each opinion honors a unique virtue of a prophet.

This passage from Taftazani's Sharh al-Maqasid presents a scholarly disagreement about the ranking of prophets after Muhammad. After affirming the consensus that Muhammad is the best of all prophets, Taftazani lists five opinions, each supported by a specific virtue. This lesson explores these opinions and encourages reflection on how different virtues can lead to different assessments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Taftazani first states the consensus on Muhammad's superiority before listing the five opinions.
The passage is a direct quotation from Taftazani's work.
2
Identify each opinion and its virtue
Go through each of the five opinions. For each prophet, note the specific virtue mentioned as the reason for considering them best after Muhammad.
Write down the prophet and their attributed virtue.
3
Reflect on the differences
Consider why different scholars might emphasize different virtues. What does this tell us about how we evaluate greatness?
This shows that ranking depends on which virtue is prioritized.
4
Understand the broader context
Remember that this disagreement occurs after the consensus that Muhammad is the best of all prophets. The disagreement is about second place, not first.
The passage begins by reaffirming Muhammad's absolute superiority.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیهات الأول في اختلافهم في الأفضل بعدَهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قال التفتازاني في شرح المقاصد الدينية له بعد ما ذكر الإجماع على أنَّه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلُ الأنبياء والرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام : ( اختلفوا في الأفضل بعده : فقيل : آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لكونه أبا البشر وقيل : نوح عليه الصلاة والسلام ، لطول عبادته ومجاهدته . وقيل : إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لزيادة توكله واطمئنانه وقيل : موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لكونه كليم الله تعالى ونجيه . وقيل : عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لكونه روح الله وصفيه )
Admonitions. First: On their disagreement concerning who is best after him (peace be upon him). Al-Taftazani said in Sharh al-Maqasid al-Diniyyah, after he mentioned the consensus that he (peace be upon him) is the best of prophets and messengers (peace be upon them): 'They differed concerning who is best after him. It was said: Adam (peace be upon him) because he is the father of mankind. It was said: Noah (peace be upon him) due to the length of his worship and struggle. It was said: Abraham (peace be upon him) due to his greater trust and tranquility. It was said: Moses (peace be upon him) because he is the interlocutor of Allah Almighty and His intimate. It was said: Jesus (peace be upon him) because he is the spirit of Allah and His chosen.'
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Taftazani's Sharh al-Maqasid that reports a disagreement among scholars about who is the best prophet after Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). After affirming the consensus that Muhammad is the best of all prophets and messengers, Taftazani lists five opinions: some say Adam, because he is the father of humanity; some say Noah, because of his long worship and struggle; some say Abraham, because of his greater trust and tranquility; some say Moses, because he is the one whom Allah spoke to directly and His intimate; some say Jesus, because he is the spirit of Allah and His chosen one. Each opinion is based on a specific virtue of that prophet. The passage simply presents these views without adjudicating between them.

Types of Extraordinary Events and the Ruling on Karamat
Sanusi defines irhas, istidraj, ibtila and states the position on karamat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of pre-prophetic and non-prophetic extraordinary events and the ruling on the miracles of saints (karamat).

Core Idea
Extraordinary events reveal divine purpose—preparation, trial, or honor—distinguished by context.

This lesson introduces three types of extraordinary events that occur outside the context of prophetic miracles: irhas (preparatory signs before prophethood), istidraj (gradual delusion of the unrighteous), and ibtila (trials like those of the Dajjal). It then explains the position of the majority of Muslims that the karamat of saints are real and distinct from prophetic miracles by the absence of a claim to prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of definitions.
2
Identify the three types
Find the definitions of irhas, istidraj, and ibtila. Note how each is characterized by its timing or the state of the person.
Irhas precedes prophethood; istidraj accompanies unrighteousness; ibtila is a trial like the Dajjal.
3
Understand the ruling on karamat
Read the second part of the passage on karamat. Note the majority view and the dissenting view of the Mu'tazila and Abu Ishaq.
Key distinction: karamat lack a claim to prophethood.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself: What makes a miracle a mu'jiza versus a karama? The answer is the claim of prophethood, not the event itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرهاصُ : وهو ما يظهرُ مِنَ الخوارقِ قبل دعوى النبوَّةِ تأسيساً لها . والاستدراج : كالخوارق التي تظهرُ ممَّنْ لم يستقم دينه والابتلاء : كالخوارق التي تظهر على يد الدجال وذهب جمهور المسلمين إلى جواز كرامات الأولياء ، وأنَّ الخوارق يجوزُ ظهورها على أيديهم جملةً مِنْ غيرِ تفصيل ، وإنَّما تمتاز عن المعجزة بخلوها عن دعوى النبوَّة ومنعها أكثرُ المعتزلة ، والأستاذ أبو إسحاق يميل إلى قريبٍ مِنْ مذهبهم ، كذا قال إمام الحرمين .
Al-Irhās: It is that which appears of extraordinary events before the claim of prophethood, as a foundation for it. Al-Istidrāj: Like the extraordinary events that appear from one whose religion is not upright. Al-Ibtilā': Like the extraordinary events that appear at the hand of the Dajjāl. The majority of Muslims hold the permissibility of the karamāt of the awliyā', and that extraordinary events are permissible to appear at their hands in general without specification, and they are distinguished from a mu‘jiza by their lack of a claim of prophethood. The majority of the Mu‘tazila forbade it, and al-Ustādh Abū Isḥāq inclines close to their doctrine; thus said Imām al-Ḥaramayn.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage defines three types of extraordinary events: irhās (preparatory miracle before prophethood), istidrāj (gradual leading astray of the non-righteous), and ibtilā' (trial, as from the Dajjāl). It then states the position of the majority of Muslims that karamāt of saints are permissible and that they are distinguished from prophetic miracles solely by the absence of a claim to prophethood. The Mu‘tazila and Abū Isḥāq oppose this view, as cited from Imām al-Ḥaramayn.

Key Terms
الإرهاص
الاستدراج
الابتلاء
الكرامات
المعجزة
الأولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That karamat are identical to mu'jizat.
Correction: The passage clarifies that karamat are distinguished from mu'jizat solely by the absence of a claim to prophethood.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Extraordinary events are categorized by their timing and purpose; karamat of saints are real but carry no claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Have you ever been impressed by a person's outward religiosity only to later discover their heart was not upright? How does the concept of istidraj in this passage serve as a warning for you to examine your own sincerity and not rely on outward wonders?

First Proof from the Quran: Stories and Objection Answer
Sanusi presents first proof from Quran and answers objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic stories of Maryam, the Companions of the Cave, and Asaf serve as evidence for the permissibility of karamat, and how the objection that these events are prophetic is answered.

Core Idea
Extraordinary events can occur through saints, not just prophets.

Sanusi, through Al-Taftazani, presents the first scriptural proof for karamat by citing three well-known Quranic narratives. An objection is raised that these are actually prophetic signs, but the answer shows that the context does not require them to be linked to a claim of prophethood. This lesson walks through the proof, the objection, and the persuasive response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three stories and the flow from evidence to objection to answer.
This passage is a complete argument in three parts.
2
Identify the three Quranic proofs
Find the three stories: Maryam's provision, the Cave sleepers, and Asaf bringing the throne. Understand each as an example of a karamah.
These are events that happened through righteous people, not prophets.
3
Understand the objection
The objection claims each event is actually an irhas (preparatory miracle) for a prophet: Jesus, a prophet in the cave, or Solomon.
This is a common counter-argument.
4
Analyze the answer
The answer argues that the context shows these events were not to confirm prophethood; Zechariah's lack of knowledge proves it. The goal is only to show the possibility of karamat.
The answer also turns the objection back on itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال التفتازاني : ( ويدلُّ على الوقوع وجهان : الأَوَّلُ : ما ثبت بالنصّ : مِنْ قصَّةِ مريمَ عند ولادة عيسى عليهِ الصلاة والسلام ، وأنَّهُ : ﴿ كُلَّمَا دَخَلَ عَلَيْهَا زَكَرِيَّا الْمِحْرَابَ وَجَدَ عِندَهَا رِزْقًا قَالَ يَمريم أَنَّى لَكِ هَذَا قَالَت هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ٣٧] . وقصَّةِ أصحاب الكهف ، ولُبتهم في كهفهم سنين بلا طعام ولا شراب . وقصَّةِ آصَفَ وإتيانِهِ بعرش بلقيس قبل ارتداد الطرفِ فإنْ قيلَ : كانَ الأوَّلُ إرهاصاً لنبوَّةِ عيسى ، والثاني : لمَنْ كانَ نبيّاً في زمن أهل الكهف ، والثالثُ : لسليمان عليه الصلاة والسلام . قلنا : سياقُ القصص يدلُّ على أنَّ ذلك لم يكن لقصدِ تصديقهم في دعوى النبوَّةِ ، بل لم يكن لزكريا علم بذلك ، ولذلك سألَ ونحن لا ندعي إلا جواز ظهورِ الخوارقِ مِنْ بعض الصالحين غيرَ مقرونة بدعوى النبوَّةِ ، ولا مسوقة لقَصْدِ تصديقِ نبي ، ولا يضرنا تسميته إرهاصاً أو معجزةً لنبيَّ هو مِنْ أمَّتِهِ ، على أنَّ ما ذكرتُم يردُّ على كثير من معجزاتِ الأنبياء ؛ لجواز أن تكون معجزة لنبي آخر
Al-Taftāzānī said: (Two proofs indicate permissibility: The first: What is confirmed by textual evidence: from the story of Maryam at the birth of Jesus, peace be upon him, and that [God says]: 'Whenever Zechariah entered upon her in the sanctuary, he found with her provision. He said, 'O Mary, whence this?' She said, 'It is from Allah.' (Surah Al 'Imran: 37). And the story of the Companions of the Cave, and their staying in their cave for years without food or drink. And the story of Āṣaf and his bringing the throne of Bilqis before the twinkling of an eye. If it is said: The first was an irhāṣ for the prophethood of Jesus, the second for someone who was a prophet in the time of the people of the cave, and the third for Solomon, peace be upon him. We say: The context of the stories indicates that they were not for the purpose of affirming them in their claim of prophethood; rather, Zechariah had no knowledge of that, and therefore he asked. And we do not claim except the permissibility of the appearance of extraordinary events from some righteous people, not associated with a claim of prophethood, nor directed to the purpose of affirming a prophet. And it does not harm us to call it an irhāṣ or a miracle for a prophet who is from his community, except that what you have mentioned also refutes many of the miracles of the prophets, because it is possible that it is a miracle for another prophet.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the permissibility of karamat from the Quran, citing three stories: Maryam's provision, the Companions of the Cave, and Asaf's transport of the throne. An objection is raised that these events are actually irhas or miracles for prophets (Jesus, a prophet in the cave, Solomon). The answer explains that the context shows they were not intended to confirm a claim of prophethood; Zechariah's lack of knowledge indicates it was not a sign for him. The proponents merely claim the possibility of karamat from righteous people without a linkage to prophethood. Even if one calls them irhas or a miracle for a prophet of that community, it does not harm the argument, and the objection would actually refute many accepted prophetic miracles.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quranic stories of Maryam, the Cave, and Asaf are exclusively prophetic miracles and cannot be considered karamat for saints.
Correction: The context shows they were not used to confirm a claim of prophethood, so they can be examples of karamat occurring through righteous people.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The first proof from the Quran shows that extraordinary events can occur through righteous people without being tied to a prophetic claim, thus supporting the permissibility of karamat.

The Second Proof for Karamat: Tawatur al-Ma'na and Conclusion
Sanusi presents the second proof from tawatur of karamat and concludes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the concept of tawatur in meaning to establish the occurrence of karamat among the Companions and later saints, and why denial of karamat is a mark of innovation.

Core Idea
Karamat are massively attested through recurrent meaning, even if individual reports are isolated.

Sanusi now presents a second, powerful proof for the reality of karamat: the sheer multitude of reports that, while each may be solitary in detail, collectively convey a common meaning of extraordinary acts occurring through saints. He provides vivid examples from the Companions and concludes that denying such wonders is a sign of following one's own desires rather than the way of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the concept of tawatur in meaning
Understand that while individual narratives may be ahad, the underlying meaning is mutawatir due to the sheer number and variety of reports.
This is a key tool in kalam for establishing events that are widely reported in substance.
2
Examine the specific examples
Consider the cases of 'Umar, Khalid, and 'Ali, which Sanusi cites as well-known instances of karamat. Reflect on how each demonstrates an extraordinary event beyond normal human capacity.
3
Reflect on the concluding claim
Sanusi states that karamat nearly equal prophetic miracles in occurrence, and that denial comes from innovators. Why would he make this strong claim? Consider the broader theological context of defending sainthood.
This connects the proof to the larger Aqeedah framework against deviant sects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : ما تواتر معناهُ وإنْ كانَتِ التفاصيل آحاداً : مِنْ كراماتِ الصحابة رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم والتابعينَ ، ومَنْ بعدهم مِنَ الصالحين ؛ كرؤيةِ عمر رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه على المنبر جيشَهُ بنهاوند ، حتى قال : ( يا ساريةُ ؛ الجبل ) وسمع سارية ذلك ، وكشرب خالد رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه السمَّ مِنْ غيرِ أَنْ يُضَرَّهُ ، وأمَّا علي رضي الله تعالى عنه فعجائبه وكراماته أكثرُ مِنْ أنْ تُحصى . وبالجملة : فكرامات الأولياء باعتبار ظهورها تكاد تلحق بمعجزاتِ الأنبياء ، وإنكارها ليس بعجيبٍ مِنْ أهل البدع والأهواء .
The second: What is recurrent in meaning (mutawātir ma‘nāh), even if the details are isolated (āḥād): from the karamāt of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and the Followers, and those who came after them from the righteous; such as the vision of ‘Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, on the pulpit of his army at Nahāwand, until he said, 'O Sāriya, the mountain!' and Sāriya heard that. And such as the drinking of poison by Khālid, may Allah be pleased with him, without being harmed. As for ‘Alī, may Allah be pleased with him, his wonders and karamāt are too numerous to count. In short, the karamāt of the awliyā', in terms of their appearance, nearly resemble the mu‘jizāt of the prophets. And its denial is not strange from the people of innovation and desires.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for karamat: the tawatur (recurrence) in meaning of reports about the companions and later saints, even if individual details are ahad (solitary). Examples include 'Umar's clairvoyant call to Sariya, Khalid's immunity to poison, and 'Ali's numerous wonders. The passage concludes that karamat are nearly equivalent to prophetic miracles in occurrence, and that denial of karamat is characteristic of the people of innovation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That karamat are not reliably transmitted because individual reports are ahad.
Correction: The passage clarifies that while details may be ahad, the overall meaning is mutawatir due to the widespread occurrence of such reports across many chains and contexts.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi establishes karamat through tawatur of meaning, demonstrating that the collective report of many events confirms the reality of saints' miracles, and brands their denial as innovation.

First Objection: Distinguishing Prophet from Saint
Sanusi presents the first objection to karamat and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against karamat and its refutation based on the distinction between miracles and karamat.

Core Idea
Karamat do not confuse prophets with saints because miracles are uniquely linked to prophethood.

This lesson presents a key objection to the doctrine of saintly miracles (karamat) and its simple yet powerful refutation. The objector fears that if saints can perform extraordinary acts, then prophets become indistinguishable. Sanusi responds by referring to the established difference between miracles and karamat, which rests on the claim to prophethood and challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the concise style of argument and response.
The passage is only two sentences, so pay attention to each part.
2
Identify the objection
The objector argues that if saints (awliya) can perform extraordinary events (khawariq al-'adat), then prophets cannot be distinguished from saints. Identify the logical premise: the only distinguishing factor is the miracle (mu'jiza).
Think about why this objection might seem plausible.
3
Understand the refutation
Sanusi refutes by referring to an earlier distinction already made. This distinction is that miracles are accompanied by a claim to prophethood and a challenge (tahaddi), while karamat are not. Thus, the confusion is avoided.
Recall that the sign of a true prophet is the miracle with a challenge, which no saint can replicate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج مَنْ أنكر الكراماتِ : بأنَّ خوارق العاداتِ لو ظهرَتْ على يدِ الولي لالتبس النبيُّ بغيره ؛ إذ الفارقُ هو المعجزة . ورُدَّ بِما مَرَّ مِنَ الفَرْقِ بينَهما
And he who denied karamat (miracles of saints) argued: if extraordinary events appear at the hand of the wali (saint), the prophet would be confused with others, because the distinguishing factor is the mu'jiza (miracle). And it was refuted by what has already been mentioned of the difference between them.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection against the doctrine of karamat (miracles performed by saints) and its refutation. The objector argues that if saints can perform extraordinary events, then prophets cannot be distinguished from saints, because the only distinguishing factor is the miracle (mu'jiza) itself. The refutation is brief: it refers to an earlier distinction already made between miracles and karamat. The reader is expected to recall that miracles are accompanied by a claim to prophethood and a challenge (tahaddi), while karamat are not. Thus, the confusion is avoided.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that karamat undermine the uniqueness of prophethood because they are also extraordinary events.
Correction: Karamat do not undermine prophethood because miracles (mu'jizat) are distinguished by the claim to prophethood and a challenge, which saints do not make.

Checkpoint

C) The saint's piety
D) The prophet's sinlessness

Key Takeaway
The uniqueness of prophethood is preserved because miracles (mu'jizat) are tied to a prophetic claim and challenge, while saintly wonders (karamat) are not.

?

Second Objection: Karamat Without Purpose Blocks Proof of Prophethood
Sanusi presents the second objection and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection to karamat and how the context of a claim transforms an extraordinary event into a definitive miracle.

Core Idea
Context matters: an extraordinary event accompanied by a claim becomes a decisive proof.

Sanusi now addresses a second objection: if karamat can occur without the purpose of attesting truth, then how can we be sure that any miracle is truly attesting to prophethood? The answer lies in the pairing of the event with a claim. This lesson explains that objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic and translation of the objection carefully. The objector argues that if karamat can appear without the purpose of attestation, then any miracle could be dismissed as a karamat, blocking the proof of prophethood.
Notice that the objector's worry is about the uncertainty of the event's purpose.
2
Examine the refutation
The refutation points to a crucial principle: when an extraordinary event accompanies a claim (da'wa), it definitively produces attestation. The claim contextualizes the event, making it a miracle.
This principle was established earlier in the text.
3
Reflect on the difference
Ask yourself: why does the presence of a claim change the evidentiary value of the event? Consider how the context of a claimant transforms a merely extraordinary occurrence into a sign of truth.
This connects to the broader methodology of verifying prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : لو ظهرَتْ لا لغرض التصديقِ لانسدَّ بابُ إثباتِ النبوَّةِ بالمعجزة ؛ لجواز أنْ يكونَ لغيرِ غرض التصديقِ . ورُدَّ بما مرَّ مِنْ أنَّها عند مقارنتها للدعوى تفيد التصديق قطعاً
Second: If they appear not for the purpose of attestation (tasdiq), the door of establishing prophethood by miracle would be closed, because it would be possible that it appears for other than attestation. And it was refuted by what has already been mentioned: that when they [the extraordinary events] accompany the claim (da'wa), they definitively produce attestation.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is the second objection and its refutation. The objector argues that if karamat can happen without being intended to attest to truth (tasdiq), then miracles for prophethood could also be dismissed as mere karamat, blocking proof of prophethood. The refutation says that when the extraordinary event accompanies a claim to prophethood, it is taken as definitive attestation, because the context of the claim makes it a miracle (mu'jiza), not a karamat. The key is the pairing of event and claim.

Key Terms
تصديق
دعوى
معجزة
كرامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karamat can undermine the evidentiary value of miracles because both are extraordinary events.
Correction: The refutation shows that the context of a claim (da'wa) differentiates a miracle from karamat. When an extraordinary event accompanies a claim to prophethood, it becomes a definitive proof, regardless of whether other events occur without such context.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, what makes an extraordinary event a definitive proof of prophethood?
A) Its rarity
B) Its accompaniment of a claim
C) Its performer being a saint
D) Its visibility

Key Takeaway
An extraordinary event only becomes a decisive miracle when it accompanies a claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one specific change you can make today so that your life becomes a 'miracle' that confirms your faith?
?
This lesson shows that a claim accompanied by a context gives decisive proof. Think of a time you dismissed a truth because you focused on the possibility of 'karamat'—of something being without purpose. Are there truths in your life you are avoiding because you are looking for perfect context? What claim from Allah in the Qur'an have you been ignoring because you wanted a sign on your terms? Commit today to respond to that claim with action.

Third Objection: Karamat Diminish the Prophet's Status
Sanusi presents the third objection to karamat and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection to karamat and its refutation, and how karamat actually enhance the status of prophets.

Core Idea
Karamat of saints magnify, not diminish, the prophet's status.

This passage presents the third objection raised against the possibility of karamat for saints: that sharing miracles with prophets would reduce the prophets' standing. Sanusi refutes this by showing how the karamat of saints actually increase the prophets' majesty and attract people to their message.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the objector's claim: that sharing extraordinary events (karamat) with prophets diminishes the prophets' greatness and standing.
Notice that the objector focuses on the psychological effect in people's hearts.
2
Study the refutation
Sanusi denies the objection and provides two reasons: (1) karamat increase the prophets' status and desire to follow them, and (2) many converts embraced Islam upon witnessing karamat of saints.
The refutation uses the concept of 'blessing of following' to argue that karamat reflect well on the prophets.
3
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider how this argument defends the Islamic doctrine of karamat and reinforces the uniqueness of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثُ : أنَّ مشاركة الأولياء للأنبياء في ظهورِ الخوارقِ يخلُّ بِعِظَمِ قَدْرِ الأنبياء ، ووقعهم في النفوس . ورُدَّ بالمنع ، بل تزيد في جلالةِ أقدارهم ، والرغبة في اتباعهم ؛ حيثُ نالَتْ أَممُهم وأتباعُهم مثل هذهِ الدرجة ؛ ببركة الاقتداء بشريعتهم ، والاستقامة على طريقتهم ، وقد أسلم بمشاهدة أولياء الله تعالى ومشاهدة كراماتِهم خَلْقٌ كثيرٌ مِنَ الكفرة .
Third: That the participation of saints (awliya) with prophets in the appearance of extraordinary events diminishes the greatness of the prophets and their standing in souls. And it was refuted by denial; rather, it increases the majesty of their status and the desire to follow them, because their nations and followers attained such a degree through the blessing of following their law and uprightness on their path, and many disbelievers embraced Islam by witnessing the saints of Allah and their karamat.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is the third objection and its refutation. The objector claims that if saints also perform extraordinary events, the status of prophets is lessened in people's hearts. The refutation denies this and argues the opposite: seeing the followers of prophets achieve such high stations through following the prophets increases the prophets' status and people's desire to follow them. Moreover, many people have converted to Islam by witnessing the karamat of saints, which in turn validates the truth of the prophets' message.

Key Takeaway
The participation of saints in extraordinary events does not reduce the prophets' status; rather, it enhances it because it shows the fruits of following them.

Fourth Objection: Knowledge of the Unseen Refuted
Sanusi presents the fourth objection based on Q.72:26 and its detailed refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that Q.72:26 denies saints knowledge of the unseen by offering multiple interpretations of the verse.

Core Idea
Quranic verses about the unseen do not exclude saints from receiving partial knowledge through divine disclosure.

This lesson addresses a common objection raised against the possibility of karamat involving foreknowledge. The opponent cites Q.72:26, which seems to restrict knowledge of the unseen to messengers alone. Sanusi provides a detailed refutation, showing that the verse can be interpreted in several ways that do not preclude saints from receiving such knowledge. By examining the context, grammar, and alternative readings, he demonstrates that the objection is not decisive.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
Start by reading the objection which quotes Q.72:26. Understand why the opponent thinks this verse excludes saints from knowledge of the unseen.
Notice the specific wording of the verse 'لا يظهر على غيبه أحدا'.
2
Examine the refutation's first interpretation
Sanusi first argues that the word 'unseen' in the verse is not generic but refers specifically to the time of the Day of Judgment, as indicated by the context. This interpretation preserves the possibility of saints knowing other unseen matters.
3
Consider the second interpretation: the exception is valid
Even if 'unseen' is general, the exception ('messengers') is valid. However, this does not deny that saints might still receive knowledge through means other than direct divine disclosure, such as through the messengers themselves.
4
Understand the grammatical argument: negation of all vs. negation of some
Sanusi explains that the verse could be read as a negation of 'all' unseen (i.e., no one knows all of it), which does not preclude knowing some aspects. He also offers the possibility that the disclosure is limited to the path of revelation.
This is a sophisticated grammatical analysis.
5
Conclude why the objection fails
The argument rests on assuming that the verse is a universal negation, but Sanusi shows that this is not necessary. Therefore, the objection does not invalidate karamat involving knowledge of the unseen.

الرابع ـ وهو حال خاص بالإخبار عن المغيبات - : قوله تعالى : عَلِمُ الْغَيْبِ فَلَا يُظْهِرُ عَلَى غَيْبِهِ أَحَدًا ﴾ [الجن : ٢٦] خص سبحانه وتعالى الرُّسُلَ مِنْ بين المرتضينَ بالاطلاع على الغيب ، فلا يُطلع عليه أحداً غيرهم ، وإن كانوا مرتضَينَ أولياء ، فما يُشاهَدُ مِنَ الكهنة وأصحاب التعبير والنجوم ظنون واستدلالات ، ربَّما تطابق وربَّما لا تطابق ، وليسَ مِن إطلاع الله تعالى على الغيبِ بدونِ واسطة عادية في شيء . والجواب : أنَّ الغيب هنا ليسَ عاماً ، بل مطلقاً ، أو معينا ; هو وقت وقوع القيامة بقرينة السياقِ ، ولا يبعدُ أنْ يُطلِعَ عليهِ بعضَ الرُّسُلِ مِنَ الملائكة أو مِنَ البشرِ ، فيصحُ الاستثناءُ ، وإِنْ جُعِلَ منقطعاً فلا خفاء ، بل لا امتناعَ حينَئِذٍ في جَعْلِ الغيبِ للعموم ، لكون اسم الجنس المضاف بمنزلة المعرَّفِ باللام ، سيّما وقد كان في الأصل مصدراً ، ويكون الكلام لسلب العموم ؛ أي : لا يطلعُ على كل غيبه أحدٌ ، وهو لا ينافي اطلاعَ البعض على البعض ، وهكذا لا إشكالَ إِنْ خُصَّ الاطلاع بطريق الوحي . وبالجملة : فالاستدلال مبني على أنَّ الكلام لعموم السلبِ ، وهو ليس بلازم
Fourth – and it is a special case concerning informing about unseen things – His statement, exalted: 'He is the Knower of the Unseen, and He does not disclose His Unseen to anyone' (Q.72:26); He, glorified and exalted, specified the messengers from among those He approves for knowledge of the unseen, so He does not disclose it to anyone other than them, even if they are approved saints. What is observed from soothsayers, interpreters of dreams, and astrologers are conjectures and inferences, which may correspond and may not correspond, and are not from Allah's disclosure of the unseen without an ordinary means. The answer: That the unseen here is not general, but either absolute or specific; it is the time of the occurrence of the Hour by the context of the passage, and it is not unlikely that He discloses it to some messengers from among angels or humans, so the exception is valid. And if it is considered disconnected, there is no obscurity; rather, there is no impossibility then in making the unseen general, because the noun of genus in the construct state is like the definite with 'al', especially since it was originally a verbal noun, and the statement is for negation of generality; i.e., He does not disclose all His unseen to anyone, and that does not negate the disclosure of some to some. Likewise, there is no problem if the disclosure is specified to the path of revelation. In summary: The argument is based on the statement being for universal negation, and that is not necessary.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection and its detailed refutation. The objector quotes Q.72:26, which says Allah does not disclose the unseen to anyone except to a messenger He approves. The objector argues that this verse excludes saints from knowledge of the unseen, contradicting the possibility of karamat involving foreknowledge. The refutation offers multiple interpretations: (1) The 'unseen' here is not general but specific to the Day of Judgment, as indicated by context. (2) Even if it is general, the exception for messengers is valid, and saints are not messengers, so they are excluded. (3) The verse can be read as a negation of all unseen (i.e., no one knows all of it), which does not preclude partial knowledge granted to saints. The refutation concludes that the argument rests on assuming universal negation, which is not necessary. The passage demonstrates careful Quranic exegesis (tafsir) applied to a kalam issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Q.72:26 proves that no one except prophets can have knowledge of the unseen.
Correction: The verse can be interpreted in multiple ways: it may refer specifically to the time of the Hour, or it may negate all unseen but not partial, or it may restrict direct disclosure but not indirect knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is one interpretation given in the refutation for the word 'unseen' in Q.72:26?
A) It refers to all unseen
B) It refers to the time of the Day of Judgment
C) It refers to saints' knowledge
D) It refers to dreams

Key Takeaway
The objection based on Q.72:26 is refuted by showing that the verse is not a blanket denial of all unseen knowledge to saints, allowing for the possibility of karamat involving foreknowledge.

Will you take one hour this week to re-examine a belief you hold about religion or life that you have never questioned rigorously?

Interpreting the Unseen: The Exception for Messengers in Quran 72:26
Sanusi explains the interpretation of the verse about the unseen and responds to an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the exception in Quran 72:26 to affirm that only messengers receive direct knowledge of the unseen, and that the verse does not contradict the general rule that no one knows the unseen independently.

Core Idea
The unseen in the verse is specific to the Day of Judgment, so the exception for messengers is clear.

Sanusi tackles a potential objection to the doctrine that only prophets receive revelation of the unseen. The verse 'He knows the unseen and does not disclose it to anyone' seems absolute, but then excludes messengers. How can saints, who are also 'those pleased with', be excluded? Sanusi explains that the 'unseen' here refers to the time of the Hour, not all unseen matters, and that the exception is consistent with Allah's prerogative to inform whom He wills.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the apparent contradiction: the verse says God does not disclose the unseen to anyone, then excepts messengers. The objector argues that saints are also 'those pleased with' and should be included.
The objection relies on a literal reading of the verse as a general negation.
2
Follow Sanusi's first answer
Sanusi argues that 'the unseen' here is not general but specific to the time of the Hour, based on context. Thus, the exception for messengers is only about that specific matter, and saints are not denied knowledge of other unseen things through other means.
This interpretation preserves the verse's specificity.
3
Consider the alternative interpretation
Sanusi also presents an alternative: if the exception is considered discontinuous, then the verse negates knowledge of all unseen, but the exception for messengers is a separate matter. This does not contradict the verse's apparent generality.
The phrase 'general negation' means no one knows every unseen, but some may know some.
4
Summarize the conclusion
The objection fails because the verse does not deny all unseen knowledge to saints; it only asserts that no one knows the unseen independently. Messengers receive revelation, which is a special case.
The argument depends on assuming the verse is a general negation, which is not necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَلِمُ الْغَيْبِ فَلَا يُظْهِرُ عَلَى غَيْبِهِ أَحَدًا ﴾ [الجن: ٢٦] خص سبحانه وتعالى الرُّسُلَ مِنْ بين المرتضينَ بالاطلاع على الغيب، فلا يُطلع عليه أحداً غيرهم، وإن كانوا مرتضَينَ أولياء، فما يُشاهَدُ مِنَ الكهنة وأصحاب التعبير والنجوم ظنون واستدلالات، ربَّما تطابق وربَّما لا تطابق، وليسَ مِن إطلاع الله تعالى على الغيبِ بدونِ واسطة عادية في شيء.
والجواب: أنَّ الغيب هنا ليسَ عاماً، بل مطلقاً، أو معينا؛ هو وقت وقوع القيامة بقرينة السياقِ، ولا يبعدُ أنْ يُطلِعَ عليهِ بعضَ الرُّسُلِ مِنَ الملائكة أو مِنَ البشرِ، فيصحُ الاستثناءُ، وإِنْ جُعِلَ منقطعاً فلا خفاء، بل لا امتناعَ حينَئِذٍ في جَعْلِ الغيبِ للعموم، لكون اسم الجنس المضاف بمنزلة المعرَّفِ باللام، سيّما وقد كان في الأصل مصدراً، ويكون الكلام لسلب العموم؛ أي: لا يطلعُ على كل غيبه أحدٌ، وهو لا ينافي اطلاعَ البعض على البعض، وهكذا لا إشكالَ إِنْ خُصَّ الاطلاع بطريق الوحي.
وبالجملة: فالاستدلال مبني على أنَّ الكلام لعموم السلبِ، وهو ليس بلازم
He is the Knower of the unseen, and He does not disclose His unseen to anyone, [Quran 72:26]. He, glorified and exalted, singled out the messengers from among those whom He is pleased with for being informed of the unseen, so He does not inform anyone other than them of it, even if they are those whom He is pleased with as saints. So what is seen of soothsayers, interpreters of dreams, and astrologers are conjectures and inferences, which may match and may not match, and are not from Allah's informing of the unseen without an ordinary means.
And the answer: That the unseen here is not general, but rather absolute or specific; it is the time of the occurrence of the Hour due to the context of the passage. And it is not far-fetched that He should inform some of the messengers, whether angels or humans, of it, so the exception is valid. And if it is considered a discontinuous exception, then it is not hidden; rather, there is no impossibility then in making the unseen general, because the common noun in the construct state is like the definite with the lam, especially since it was originally a verbal noun. And the speech is for the negation of generality; i.e., He does not inform anyone of all His unseen, and this does not contradict informing some of some. And thus there is no problem if the informing is specified through the way of revelation.
In summary: The argument is based on the speech being for the generality of negation, and that is not necessary.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. The objector points to the apparent general statement 'He does not disclose His unseen to anyone' and then the exception 'except to a messenger whom He is pleased with.' He argues that if saints are also 'those whom He is pleased with,' then they too should be informed of the unseen, contradicting the exception limited to messengers. The answer clarifies that 'the unseen' here is not general—it refers specifically to the time of the Hour, due to the context. Thus, the exception is valid for messengers regarding that specific unseen. Additionally, if one interprets the exception as discontinuous, then the general negation 'no one knows any of His unseen' can be maintained, and the exception for messengers is only for that specific matter. The final summary states that the objector's argument relies on assuming the verse implies a negation of all unseen knowledge for everyone, but this is not necessarily the case.

Misconception: The verse 72:26 proves that no one except messengers can know anything about the unseen, so saints cannot know even through inspiration or revelation.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the verse refers to the specific unseen of the Hour, and the exception for messengers is about that particular matter. Moreover, the exception can be interpreted as discontinuous, meaning the verse negates general knowledge of all unseen, but revelation to messengers is a different matter.

Key Takeaway
The objection based on Quran 72:26 is resolved by recognizing that 'the unseen' in the verse is specific to the Day of Judgment, not all unseen matters, leaving room for messengers to receive revelation of other hidden things.

Two Consensuses on Prophethood vs. Sainthood
Sanusi states two consensuses on the superiority of prophethood over sainthood and refutes deviant views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two consensuses regarding the superiority of prophets over saints and the deviant views they refute.

Core Idea
Prophets are superior to saints because they combine sainthood with prophethood, and no saint can reach that rank.

This lesson presents two key consensuses (ijmā‘) that establish the orthodox Sunni hierarchy between prophets and saints. Sanusi states these consensuses clearly, and then refutes the claims of two deviant sects. By understanding these consensuses, you will guard against common misconceptions about the relationship between prophethood and sainthood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the two consensuses.
The passage uses the phrase 'واعلم' to draw attention.
2
Identify the two consensuses
The passage states two unanimous agreements: first, that a saint cannot reach prophethood; second, that a prophet is superior to a saint. Write them down.
3
Examine the distinctive qualities of prophets
In the first consensus, Sanusi lists several special qualities of prophets that set them apart. List these qualities.
These include being protected from sin, safe from evil end, etc.
4
Understand the refutations
Note that the passage explicitly dismisses the views of the Karramiyya and Batiniyya. Why are these views considered heretical?
The Karramiyya claim a saint can reach prophethood, the Batiniyya claim sainthood is superior.
5
Reflect on the importance
Think about why these consensuses are foundational for understanding the hierarchy in Islam.
This safeguards against deviant beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنَّ المسلمين أجمعوا على أنَّ الوليَّ لا يصل إلى درجةِ النبي ؛ إذْ مِنْ خاصَّةِ النبيَّ معَ ما حازَهُ مِنْ شرفِ الولايةِ أَنَّهُ معصوم عنِ المعاصي ، مأمونٌ مِنْ سوء العاقبة بحكم النصوص القاطعة ، مُشرَّفٌ بالوحي ومشاهدة المَلَكِ ، مبعوث لإصلاح حال العالم ونظام أمر المعاش والمعادِ ، إلى غير ذلكَ مِنَ الكمالاتِ ، ولا يُعتَدُّ بقول بعض الكراميَّةِ المبتدعةِ أنَّ الوليَّ قد يبلغ درجة النبي

وكذا أجمع المسلمون على أنَّ النبيَّ أفضلُ مِنَ الولي ؛ لأنَّ النبيَّ جمع بين مرتبة الولاية ومرتبة النبوَّةِ ، ولا يُعتَدُّ بقول بعض الباطنيَّةِ : إنَّ الولاية أفضلُ مِنَ النبوَّةِ
And know that the Muslims have unanimously agreed that the saint does not reach the degree of the prophet; indeed, from the specific qualities of the prophet, along with what he has attained of the honor of sainthood, is that he is protected from sins, safe from evil consequence by virtue of decisive texts, honored with revelation and vision of the angel, sent to reform the state of the world and the order of livelihood and the afterlife, and other perfections. And no regard is given to the saying of some of the heretical Karramiyya that the saint may reach the degree of the prophet.

Likewise, the Muslims have unanimously agreed that the prophet is superior to the saint, because the prophet combines the rank of sainthood and the rank of prophethood. And no regard is given to the saying of some of the Batiniyya that sainthood is superior to prophethood.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage establishes two consensuses (ijmā‘) on the relationship between prophets and saints. First, the Muslims agree that no saint can attain the rank of prophethood. The author lists several distinctive features of prophets that set them apart: they are protected from sin, safe from evil end, honored with revelation and seeing angels, and sent for the reform of the world. He then rejects the claim of the Karramiyya sect that a saint could reach prophethood. Second, the Muslims agree that prophets are superior to saints because prophets combine both sainthood and prophethood. The author rejects the Batiniyya claim that sainthood is superior. The passage thus clarifies the orthodox Sunni position on the hierarchy between prophets and saints.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A saint can attain the degree of prophethood (Karramiyya) or sainthood is superior to prophethood (Batiniyya).
Correction: The consensus of the Muslims is that no saint can reach the degree of a prophet, and prophets are superior because they combine sainthood and prophethood.

Checkpoint

A) Prophets are not subject to sin.
B) Prophets combine sainthood and prophethood.
C) Prophets see angels.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are superior to saints because they combine the rank of sainthood with the rank of prophethood, a rank no saint can attain.

Prophethood vs. Sainthood: Which Is Superior?
Al-Taftazani presents two opinions on whether a prophet's prophethood or sainthood is superior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two opinions presented by al-Taftazani on whether a prophet's prophethood or sainthood is superior, and the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Prophethood involves mediation, sainthood closeness—both are perfect in the prophet.

Al-Taftazani raises a subtle question: within the same prophet, is his prophethood superior to his sainthood, or vice versa? He reports two scholarly opinions, each with a compelling reason. This passage invites you to reflect on the distinct excellences of prophethood and sainthood, and how they come together in the prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text of al-Taftazani once, noticing the structure: a question, then two answers introduced by 'فَمِنْ قَائِلٍ'.
Focus on the contrast between 'وساطة' and 'قرب+اختصاص'.
2
Identify the two opinions
The first opinion favors prophethood for its role as mediator between God and creation. The second favors sainthood for its closeness and special distinction. Note the key terms used.
3
Understand the reasoning
For the first opinion: prophethood involves mediation (وساطة) and managing the interests of both worlds, plus the honor of seeing angels. For the second: sainthood involves closeness (قرب) and special distinction (اختصاص), which in a prophet is at its ultimate level.
Compare the two: one emphasizes function, the other emphasizes rank.
4
Reflect on the implication
Al-Taftazani does not choose a side; he presents the hesitation as valid. Think about why both perspectives can be maintained within Sunni theology.
This shows the depth of kalam discussions beyond mere dogma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال التفتازاني : ( نعم ؛ قد يقعُ تردُّد في أنَّ نبوَّةَ النبيِّ أفضلُ أم ولایته ؟
فمِنْ قائل بالأَوَّلِ ؛ لما في النبوَّةِ مِنْ معنى الوساطة مِنَ الجانبين ، والقيام بمصالح الخلْقِ في الدارين ، مع شرفِ مشاهدة الملكِ ومن قائل بالثاني ؛ لما في الولايةِ مِنْ معنى القرب والاختصاص الذي يكونُ في النبي في غاية الكمال ، بخلافِ ولايةِ غيرِ النبي
Al-Taftazani said: 'Yes, there may be hesitation as to whether the prophethood of the prophet is superior or his sainthood? So there is one who says the first, because in prophethood there is the meaning of mediation between the two sides, and undertaking the interests of creation in both worlds, along with the honor of seeing the angel. And one who says the second, because in sainthood there is the meaning of closeness and special distinction which is in the prophet in the utmost perfection, unlike the sainthood of other than the prophet.'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage quotes al-Taftazani discussing a nuanced point: whether within a prophet, his prophethood or his sainthood is superior. Two opinions are presented. The first favors prophethood because it involves mediation between God and creation and managing worldly and religious affairs, along with seeing angels. The second favors sainthood because it involves closeness and special distinction, which in a prophet is at its peak. Taftazani does not resolve the disagreement but presents it as a valid point of consideration.

وساطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is definitively known that a prophet's sainthood is superior to his prophethood.
Correction: Al-Taftazani presents both opinions without resolution, showing that this is a legitimate point of discussion, not settled doctrine.

Checkpoint

C) Because prophets are protected from sin.
D) Because sainthood can be attained by others.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani presents two valid opinions on whether a prophet's prophethood or sainthood is superior, showing that both dimensions have compelling merits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Sainthood Does Not Nullify Religious Obligations
Sanusi asserts the consensus and refutes the libertine view as kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic consensus that sainthood, no matter how advanced, does not exempt a person from religious obligations, and that the contrary belief is kufr.

Core Idea
Even the greatest saint must follow the Sharia fully.

Sanusi now addresses a dangerous misconception held by some extremist groups: that perfect sainthood lifts the burden of religious duties. He begins by stating the unanimous agreement of Muslims that sainthood never nullifies the commands and prohibitions of the Law. Then he identifies and refutes the opposing view, declaring it to be clear disbelief. This lesson will help you see why Islamic orthodoxy insists that the Sharia applies to all, regardless of spiritual rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice the strong language used against the opposing view.
The passage begins with 'Likewise' — this follows a previous consensus.
2
Identify the consensus claim
The Muslims agree that sainthood, even at its peak, does not remove the obligations of Sharia. Underline the key phrase 'لا يسقط معها تكاليف الشرع'.
3
Examine the opposing view
The Batiniyya and heretics claim that when a saint reaches ultimate love and sincerity, commands and prohibitions fall away, sin does not harm, and major sins do not lead to Hell. Note how Sanusi describes this view.
This is a form of antinomianism.
4
Understand the refutation
Sanusi declares this belief to be kufr. Ask yourself: why is it so severe? Because it undermines the universal applicability of divine law and opens the door to moral chaos.
The consensus of the ummah is used as evidence.

وكذا أجمعَ المسلمون على أنَّ الولاية ولو تناهَتْ لا يسقط معها تكاليف الشرع ، وعن أهل الإباحةِ مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ والإلحادِ - أذلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى ، وأخلى منهم الأرضَ - : أنَّ الولي إذا بلغ الغاية في المحبة وصفاء القلب وكمال الإخلاص .. سقط عنه الأمر والنهي ، ولم يضرُّهُ حينَئِذٍ الذنبُ ، ولا يدخلُ النارَ بارتكاب الكبائر ، وهذا كفر
Likewise, the Muslims have unanimously agreed that sainthood, even if it reaches its utmost, does not nullify the obligations of the Law. And from the people of permission among the Batiniyya and the heretics - may Allah disgrace them and clear the earth of them - is that the saint, when he reaches the ultimate in love, purity of heart, and perfection of sincerity, the command and prohibition fall away from him, and then sin does not harm him, and he does not enter the Fire for committing major sins. And this is disbelief.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage states another consensus: sainthood, no matter how advanced, does not abrogate the religious obligations. Then it refutes the view of the Batiniyya and heretics who claim that a perfect saint is free from commands and prohibitions and is not harmed by sin, even major sins. The author declares this belief to be kufr. This defends the consistent application of Sharī‘a to all believers.
