Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that advanced sainthood exempts a person from religious obligations and that major sins are harmless for a saint.
Correction: The passage states that such a belief is kufr; sainthood never nullifies the obligations of the Law.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the belief that a saint is exempt from religious obligations after reaching perfection?
A) It is permissible.
B) It is kufr.
C) It is a minor sin.
D) It is acceptable if the saint is sincere.

Key Takeaway
Sainthood does not nullify religious obligations; the contrary belief is kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought that because you pray, fast, or engage in dhikr, you are somehow above certain rules of Sharia—like ignoring a minor prohibition? What does this passage do to that excuse?
?
The heretics believed that sin does not harm the saint. Is there a part of you that thinks your good deeds outweigh your sins, so you can afford to be careless? How will you uproot that thought from your heart starting today?
?
If sainthood does not nullify a single obligation, then what specific command of Allah have you been neglecting that you will recommit to this week, knowing that no spiritual status exempts you?

The Superiority of the Prophet Over the Saint: Consensus and Refutation
The author states the consensus that a prophet is superior to a saint.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic consensus that a prophet is superior to any saint, the reasoning behind it, and the rejection of the Batiniyya view.

Core Idea
A prophet combines sainthood and prophethood, making him categorically superior to a saint.

This short passage from Sanusi's creedal work establishes a foundational point of Sunni theology: the prophet is superior to the saint. The author appeals to the consensus of Muslims and provides a clear rationale. He also dismisses a deviant sectarian opinion that claimed sainthood is higher. Let's read and unpack the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice how the author states the consensus, gives the reason, and then rejects a contrary view.
2
Identify the two groups mentioned
The passage mentions two sects: the Karamiyya and the Batiniyya. What does each claim? How does the author respond?
3
Analyze the reasoning
Focus on the conjunction 'because' (li-anna). Why does the combination of prophethood and sainthood make the prophet superior?
4
Reflect on the consensus
The author asserts ijmaʿ (consensus). Why is consensus important in Islamic theology? How does this argument strengthen the position?
Consensus is a primary source of authority in Sunni Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) الكراميَّةِ المبتدعةِ أنَّ الوليَّ قد يبلغ درجة النبي وكذا أجمع المسلمون على أنَّ النبيَّ أفضلُ مِنَ الولي ؛ لأنَّ النبيَّ جمع بين مرتبة الولاية ومرتبة النبوَّةِ ، ولا يُعتَدُّ بقول بعض الباطنيَّةِ : إنَّ الولاية أفضلُ مِنَ النبوَّةِ (٢) (۱) كذا في « شرح المقاصد » ( ٢/ ٢٠٥ ) . (۲) انظر ( شرح المقاصد » ( ٢/ ٢٠٥ )
(1) Among the heretical Karamiyya is that the saint (al-walī) may reach the level of a prophet. Likewise, the Muslims are unanimously agreed that the prophet is superior to the saint, because the prophet combines the rank of sainthood (wilāya) and the rank of prophethood (nubuwwa). No heed is paid to the saying of some Batiniyya that sainthood is superior to prophethood (2). (1) Thus in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid (2/205). (2) See Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid (2/205).
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage presents a doctrinal consensus: Muslims agree that a prophet is superior to any saint. The reason given is that a prophet unites both sainthood and prophethood, while a saint only has sainthood. The author then dismisses the deviant opinion of some Batiniyya who claim sainthood is superior. The footnotes cite al-Taftazani's Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid as the source for this consensus.

Key Terms

نبوة
إجماع
باطنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think a saint can equal or surpass a prophet.
Correction: Consensus of Muslims holds a prophet is superior because he combines prophethood and sainthood.

Checkpoint
According to the consensus mentioned in the passage, why is a prophet superior to a saint?
A) Because the prophet has a greater number of miracles.
B) Because the prophet combines the ranks of prophethood and sainthood.
C) Because the saint cannot perform miracles.
D) Because the prophet is sinless.

Key Takeaway
The prophet is superior to the saint because he combines the rank of sainthood with the special rank of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself more drawn to the stories of saints and their miracles than to the life of the Prophet ﷺ? How does this lesson challenge you to reorder your spiritual priorities? Will you commit to learning more about the Prophet's ﷺ seerah this week as an act of honoring his rank?
?
When you seek closeness to Allah, do you secretly wish for a 'shortcut' through sainthood without fully following the prophetic path? This lesson declares that the prophet combines both ranks and is superior. In what practical ways will you submit your spiritual ambitions to the prophetic example, even when it is difficult?
?
The passage dismisses the opinion of those who elevate sainthood above prophethood as not even worth considering. Have you ever unconsciously favored the teachings of a contemporary scholar or spiritual guide over the Sunnah? How will you guard your heart so that the Prophet ﷺ remains your ultimate leader and role model?

Prophethood vs. Sainthood: Which is Superior?
Taftazani discusses the relative merit of prophethood and sainthood within a prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions on whether a prophet's prophethood or his sainthood is superior, along with the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
A prophet's prophethood and sainthood are complementary, not competing, aspects of his station.

Al-Taftazani presents a subtle question: within the same prophet, is his prophethood more excellent or his sainthood? Two opinions exist, each grounded in different aspects of the prophetic reality. This lesson unpacks the arguments and shows how they ultimately point to the prophet's unique role as both mediator and intimate servant of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the two opinions and al-Sa'd's final note.
Pay attention to the key terms: نبوة, ولاية, وساطة, قرب.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents two views: one holding prophethood superior, the other holding sainthood superior. Note the reasoning for each.
The first opinion emphasizes mediation (وساطة) and management of creation; the second emphasizes closeness (قرب) and exclusivity.
3
Understand al-Sa'd's clarification
Al-Sa'd explains that the prophet's ongoing influence over his community is through his sainthood, and the saints are mere manifestations of that influence.
This shows that prophethood and sainthood are not in conflict but serve different functions.
4
Reflect on the complementarity
Consider how both opinions highlight different facets of the prophet's station: prophethood involves outward guidance, sainthood inward closeness. Together they form a complete picture.
The common misunderstanding is to see them as rivals; the passage shows they are complementary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال التفتازاني : ( نعم ؛ قد يقعُ تردُّد في أنَّ نبوَّةَ النبيِّ أفضلُ أم ولايته ؟ فمِنْ قائل بالأَوَّلِ ؛ لما في النبوَّةِ مِنْ معنى الوساطة مِنَ الجانبين ، والقيام بمصالح الخلْقِ في الدارين ، مع شرفِ مشاهدة الملكِ (۳) ومن قائل بالثاني ؛ لما في الولايةِ مِنْ معنى القرب والاختصاص الذي يكونُ في النبي في غاية الكمال ، بخلافِ ولايةِ غيرِ النبي (۳) ويكون تصرُّف النبي في أمَّته إلى قيام الساعة .. بولايته ، والأولياء من أمته هم حمله هذا التصرف ، قال العلامة السعد في ( شرح المقاصد » ( ٢٠٦/٢ ) : ) إذ ليس الولي إلا مظهر تصرُّف النبي )
Al-Taftazani said: (Yes, there may be hesitation as to whether the prophethood of a prophet is more excellent or his sainthood? Some say the former, because in prophethood there is the meaning of mediation between the two sides, and the management of the interests of creation in both worlds, along with the honor of beholding the angel (3). And some say the latter, because in sainthood there is the meaning of closeness and exclusivity which in the prophet is in utmost perfection, unlike the sainthood of other than the prophet. (3) And the prophet's influence over his community until the Resurrection is through his sainthood, and the saints of his community are the carriers of this influence. Al-Sa'd said in Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid (2/206): 'For the saint is only a manifestation of the prophet's influence.')
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage presents a subtle question within the topic: Is a prophet's prophethood superior to his own sainthood, or is his sainthood superior? Al-Taftazani notes two opinions. The first argues that prophethood is superior because it involves mediation between God and creation, managing affairs of both worlds, and the honor of seeing the angel. The second argues that sainthood is superior because it involves closeness and exclusivity with God, which in the prophet is perfect. A footnote from al-Sa'd clarifies that the prophet's ongoing influence over his community is through his sainthood, and the saints are merely vehicles of that influence.

Key Terms
نبوة
ولاية
وساطة
قرب
مشاهدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think prophethood and sainthood are competing or that a prophet's prophethood and sainthood are separate and one is clearly superior to the other.
Correction: The passage shows they are complementary: prophethood involves outward mediation, while sainthood involves inward closeness and is the channel for the prophet's ongoing influence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one reason given by those who say a prophet's prophethood is superior to his sainthood?
A) Because prophethood involves closeness and exclusivity with God.
B) Because prophethood involves mediation between God and creation.
C) Because sainthood is only for non-prophets.
D) Because prophethood includes the ability to perform miracles.

Key Takeaway
A prophet's prophethood and sainthood are complementary: prophethood emphasizes outward mediation and leadership, while sainthood emphasizes inward closeness and is the vehicle for his lasting influence on his community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek to influence others for good, do you rely more on your own efforts or on the prophetic influence channeled through the saints? How will you actively connect to that source after reading that 'the saint is only a manifestation of the prophet's influence'?
?
The prophet's sainthood is described as 'closeness and exclusivity in utmost perfection.' Do you pursue closeness to Allah as an end in itself, or do you see it merely as a means to other goals? What would it mean for you to make closeness your ultimate aim today?
?
If the prophet's ongoing influence on his community is through his sainthood, what does that imply about your connection to him? Are you seeking to be a 'carrier' of that influence, or are you content with passive affiliation? What concrete step will you take to embody that influence this week?

Consensus: Sainthood Does Not Abrogate Obligations
Sanusi states the consensus and refutes the Batiniyya heresy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus of Muslims that sainthood does not exempt one from religious obligations and why the heretical claim otherwise is considered unbelief.

Core Idea
No level of sainthood lifts the obligations of the Sharia.

Sanusi begins by affirming the unanimous agreement of Muslims that even the highest sainthood does not remove the duty to follow the Law. He then mentions the heretical view of the Batiniyya and decisively labels it as kufr. This passage establishes the foundational principle that spiritual excellence does not nullify divine commands.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Pay attention to the strong language used against the heretical view.
Notice the phrase 'kufr la mahala' – it is emphatic.
2
Identify the three components
The passage contains: 1) the consensus statement, 2) the heretical claim, 3) the judgment that it is kufr and the reason. Find each part.
3
Understand the reasoning
Why does the author say the heretical view is kufr? The reason is that a saint is merely a manifestation of the prophet's influence – not a source of new law. Reflect on this logic.
This refutes the idea that sainthood grants authority over the Sharia.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا أجمعَ المسلمون على أنَّ الولاية ولو تناهَتْ لا يسقط معها تكاليف الشرع ، وعن أهل الإباحةِ مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ والإلحادِ - أذلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى ، وأخلى منهم الأرضَ - : أنَّ الولي إذا بلغ الغاية في المحبة وصفاء القلب وكمال الإخلاص .. سقط عنه الأمر والنهي ، ولم يضرُّهُ حينَئِذٍ الذنبُ ، ولا يدخلُ النارَ بارتكاب الكبائر ، وهذا كفر (٤) لا محالة(۱) ؛ إذ لا معنى للولي إلا مُظهِرُ تصرُّفِ النبي في الخلْقِ بالحق . قال التفتازاني بعد أن ردَّ عليهم بإجماع المسلمين وعمـومِ الخطابات : ( ولأنَّ أكمل الناس في المحبة والإخلاص هم الأنبياء الصلاة والسلام ، سيَّما حبيب الله تعالى سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، مَعَ أَنَّ التكاليف في حقهم أتم وأكمل (۲) ، حتى إنَّهم يُعاتبونَ بأدنى زلَّةٍ ، بل بتركِ الأفضل عليهم نعم ؛ حُكِيَ عن بعض الأولياء أنَّه استعفى الله تعالى عن التكاليف ، وسألَهُ الإعتاق عن ظواهر العباداتِ ، فأجابَهُ إلى ذلك ؛ بأن سلبه العقل الذي هو مناط التكليف ، ومع ذلكَ كَانَ مِنْ علوّ المرتبة على ما كانَ وأنتَ خبير بأنَّ العارف لا يسأمُ مِنَ العبادة ، ولا يفتر في الطاعة ، ولا يسألُ الهبوط مِنْ أوج الكمال إلى حضيض النقصانِ ، والنزولَ مِنْ (۱) أما إن ظنَّ جاهل ممن ينتسب للسادة الصوفية أنه وصل إلى حالة بينه وبين الله تعالى سقط فيها عنه التكليف ، وحلَّ له بعض المحرمات .. فتكفيره في محلّ الاجتهاد والنظر عند حجة الإسلام الغزالي ، ومع هذا قال في « فيصل التفرقة » ( ص ٨٦ ) : ( هذا مما لا أشكُ قتله في وجوب ، وإن كان في الحكم بخلوده في النار نظر ، وقتل هذا أفضل من قتل مئة كافر ؛ إذ ضرره في الدين أعظم ) (۲) إذ قال سبحانه وتعالى في حكاية كلام سيدنا عيسى على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام : ﴿ وَجَعَلَنِي مُبَارَكًا أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُ وَأَوْصَنِي بِالصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيَّا [مريم : ٣١] .
And likewise, Muslims are unanimously agreed that sainthood, even if it reaches its utmost, does not cause the obligations of the Law to fall from one. And from the people of licentiousness among the Batiniyya and the heretics—may God Most High humiliate them and empty the earth of them—is that the saint, when he reaches the extreme in love, purity of heart, and perfection of sincerity, the command and prohibition fall from him, and sin does not harm him then, and he does not enter the Fire for committing major sins. This is unbelief (4) without doubt (1); for there is no meaning to 'saint' except a manifestation of the prophet's influence over creation with truth. Al-Taftazani said, after refuting them by the consensus of Muslims and the generality of the addresses: (And because the most complete people in love and sincerity are the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, especially the Beloved of God Most High, our master and lord Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, while the obligations in their regard are most complete and perfect (2), so much so that they are reproached for the slightest slip, indeed for leaving the better. Yes, it is related of some saint that he asked God Most High for exemption from obligations, and asked Him to free him from the outward forms of worship, and He granted him that by removing his intellect, which is the basis of obligation, and despite that he was of high rank as he was. And you are aware that the gnostic does not tire of worship, nor slacken in obedience, nor ask to descend from the peak of perfection to the abyss of deficiency, nor to descend from... (1) But if an ignorant person who claims affiliation with the Sufi masters thinks that he has reached a state between him and God Most High in which obligation has fallen from him, and some forbidden things have become permissible for him—then his excommunication is a matter of ijtihad and consideration according to Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, and despite this he said in Fayṣal al-Tafriqa (p. 86): 'This is something whose killing is obligatory, in which I have no doubt, although there is consideration regarding the judgment of his eternal abiding in the Fire. And killing this person is better than killing a hundred disbelievers, because his harm to the religion is greater.') (2) For He, glorified and exalted, said in the narration of the speech of our master Jesus, peace be upon our Prophet and upon him: 'And He has made me blessed wherever I am, and has enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I live' [Maryam 31].
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage refutes the heretical view that a saint, upon reaching a high spiritual station, is freed from religious obligations. The author begins by stating the consensus of Muslims that even the highest sainthood does not abrogate the obligations of sharia. Then he condemns the Batiniyya and heretics who claim that such a saint is no longer bound by commands and prohibitions, and that sin does not harm him. This, he says, is clear unbelief, because a saint is merely a manifestation of the prophet's influence. Al-Taftazani reinforces this with the example of the prophets, who are the most perfect in love and sincerity yet are held to the strictest obligations, even being reproached for minor slips. He then relates an anecdote about a saint who asked God for exemption and was granted it by having his intellect removed—the basis of obligation—showing that exemption comes only through loss of reason, not through spiritual rank. The author concludes that the true gnostic never tires of worship and never seeks to descend from perfection. The footnote adds that anyone who claims to be freed from obligations and makes forbidden things permissible is to be killed, according to al-Ghazali.

Key Terms
ولاية
تكليف
إباحة
باطنية
إلحاد
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that reaching a high spiritual station (sainthood) frees a person from religious duties and protects them from sin.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the highest level of sainthood does not invalidate obligations, as even the prophets were under full obligation. The claim that it does is kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consensus of Muslims regarding sainthood and religious obligations?
A) Sainthood can sometimes abrogate obligations for the most advanced saints.
B) Sainthood does not cause obligations to fall, even if it reaches its utmost.
C) Only minor sins are forgiven for saints, but major obligations remain.
D) The obligation is lifted only if the saint asks God for exemption.

Key Takeaway
Sainthood does not nullify religious obligations, and any claim otherwise is clear unbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your spiritual progress or religious devotion exempts you from some of the commands of Allah, such as prayers or fasting, even if only for a moment? How does this lesson expose that as dangerous?
?
Do you secretly admire those who claim a special status that lifts them above the law, thinking that they have 'arrived'? What would you say to yourself to guard against that illusion?
?
If you were to die today, would you be confident that you have fulfilled the obligations that Allah placed on you, or have you hoped that your devotion might let you off some of them? What one obligation will you commit to upholding more sincerely after this lesson?

Al-Taftazani's Argument: Prophets as the Highest Example
Al-Taftazani argues using the example of prophets and an anecdote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's argument that the prophets, being the most perfect in love and sincerity, are held to the strictest obligations, proving that sainthood cannot exempt one from duties.

Core Idea
The prophets are the most beloved yet the most obligated, refuting exemption.

After the initial refutation, al-Taftazani provides a powerful argument from the example of the prophets. If anyone could be exempted from obligations due to perfect love and sincerity, it would be the prophets, especially Muhammad. Yet they are bound by the strictest duties. This lesson unpacks that argument and an illuminating anecdote about a saint who asked for exemption.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Taftazani's argument
Read the Arabic passage from 'قال التفتازاني' to 'حضيض النقصانِ'. Then read the translation. Notice how he uses the prophets as evidence.
The argument is based on the principle that the more perfect one is, the more obligations they have, not fewer.
2
Understand the anecdote
Al-Taftazani relates a story of a saint who asked God for exemption and was granted it by having his intellect removed. This illustrates that exemption only comes through loss of reason, not through spiritual rank.
3
Reflect on the gnostic's attitude
The passage concludes that the true gnostic never tires of worship and never seeks to descend from perfection. This reinforces that seeking exemption is a sign of deficiency, not sainthood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا أجمعَ المسلمون على أنَّ الولاية ولو تناهَتْ لا يسقط معها تكاليف الشرع ، وعن أهل الإباحةِ مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ والإلحادِ - أذلَّهمُ اللهُ تعالى ، وأخلى منهم الأرضَ - : أنَّ الولي إذا بلغ الغاية في المحبة وصفاء القلب وكمال الإخلاص .. سقط عنه الأمر والنهي ، ولم يضرُّهُ حينَئِذٍ الذنبُ ، ولا يدخلُ النارَ بارتكاب الكبائر ، وهذا كفر (٤) لا محالة(۱) ؛ إذ لا معنى للولي إلا مُظهِرُ تصرُّفِ النبي في الخلْقِ بالحق . قال التفتازاني بعد أن ردَّ عليهم بإجماع المسلمين وعمـومِ الخطابات : ( ولأنَّ أكمل الناس في المحبة والإخلاص هم الأنبياء الصلاة والسلام ، سيَّما حبيب الله تعالى سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، مَعَ أَنَّ التكاليف في حقهم أتم وأكمل (۲) ، حتى إنَّهم يُعاتبونَ بأدنى زلَّةٍ ، بل بتركِ الأفضل عليهم نعم ؛ حُكِيَ عن بعض الأولياء أنَّه استعفى الله تعالى عن التكاليف ، وسألَهُ الإعتاق عن ظواهر العباداتِ ، فأجابَهُ إلى ذلك ؛ بأن سلبه العقل الذي هو مناط التكليف ، ومع ذلكَ كَانَ مِنْ علوّ المرتبة على ما كانَ وأنتَ خبير بأنَّ العارف لا يسأمُ مِنَ العبادة ، ولا يفتر في الطاعة ، ولا يسألُ الهبوط مِنْ أوج الكمال إلى حضيض النقصانِ ، والنزولَ مِنْ (۱) أما إن ظنَّ جاهل ممن ينتسب للسادة الصوفية أنه وصل إلى حالة بينه وبين الله تعالى سقط فيها عنه التكليف ، وحلَّ له بعض المحرمات .. فتكفيره في محلّ الاجتهاد والنظر عند حجة الإسلام الغزالي ، ومع هذا قال في « فيصل التفرقة » ( ص ٨٦ ) : ( هذا مما لا أشكُ قتله في وجوب ، وإن كان في الحكم بخلوده في النار نظر ، وقتل هذا أفضل من قتل مئة كافر ؛ إذ ضرره في الدين أعظم ) (۲) إذ قال سبحانه وتعالى في حكاية كلام سيدنا عيسى على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام : ﴿ وَجَعَلَنِي مُبَارَكًا أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُ وَأَوْصَنِي بِالصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيَّا [مريم : ٣١] .
And likewise, Muslims are unanimously agreed that sainthood, even if it reaches its utmost, does not cause the obligations of the Law to fall from one. And from the people of licentiousness among the Batiniyya and the heretics—may God Most High humiliate them and empty the earth of them—is that the saint, when he reaches the extreme in love, purity of heart, and perfection of sincerity, the command and prohibition fall from him, and sin does not harm him then, and he does not enter the Fire for committing major sins. This is unbelief (4) without doubt (1); for there is no meaning to 'saint' except a manifestation of the prophet's influence over creation with truth. Al-Taftazani said, after refuting them by the consensus of Muslims and the generality of the addresses: (And because the most complete people in love and sincerity are the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, especially the Beloved of God Most High, our master and lord Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, while the obligations in their regard are most complete and perfect (2), so much so that they are reproached for the slightest slip, indeed for leaving the better. Yes, it is related of some saint that he asked God Most High for exemption from obligations, and asked Him to free him from the outward forms of worship, and He granted him that by removing his intellect, which is the basis of obligation, and despite that he was of high rank as he was. And you are aware that the gnostic does not tire of worship, nor slacken in obedience, nor ask to descend from the peak of perfection to the abyss of deficiency, nor to descend from... (1) But if an ignorant person who claims affiliation with the Sufi masters thinks that he has reached a state between him and God Most High in which obligation has fallen from him, and some forbidden things have become permissible for him—then his excommunication is a matter of ijtihad and consideration according to Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, and despite this he said in Fayṣal al-Tafriqa (p. 86): 'This is something whose killing is obligatory, in which I have no doubt, although there is consideration regarding the judgment of his eternal abiding in the Fire. And killing this person is better than killing a hundred disbelievers, because his harm to the religion is greater.') (2) For He, glorified and exalted, said in the narration of the speech of our master Jesus, peace be upon our Prophet and upon him: 'And He has made me blessed wherever I am, and has enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I live' [Maryam 31].
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage refutes the heretical view that a saint, upon reaching a high spiritual station, is freed from religious obligations. The author begins by stating the consensus of Muslims that even the highest sainthood does not abrogate the obligations of sharia. Then he condemns the Batiniyya and heretics who claim that such a saint is no longer bound by commands and prohibitions, and that sin does not harm him. This, he says, is clear unbelief, because a saint is merely a manifestation of the prophet's influence. Al-Taftazani reinforces this with the example of the prophets, who are the most perfect in love and sincerity yet are held to the strictest obligations, even being reproached for minor slips. He then relates an anecdote about a saint who asked God for exemption and was granted it by having his intellect removed—the basis of obligation—showing that exemption comes only through loss of reason, not through spiritual rank. The author concludes that the true gnostic never tires of worship and never seeks to descend from perfection. The footnote adds that anyone who claims to be freed from obligations and makes forbidden things permissible is to be killed, according to al-Ghazali.

Key Terms
تكليف
إخلاص
محبة
أنبياء
عارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that perfect love and sincerity can cause religious obligations to fall away.
Correction: The prophets are the most perfect in love and sincerity, yet they are the most obligated. Thus, obligations are not lifted by spiritual perfection.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani's argument, what happened to the saint who asked God for exemption from obligations?
A) He was granted exemption while keeping his intellect.
B) He was granted exemption by having his intellect removed.
C) He was denied and punished for asking.
D) He was made a prophet.

Key Takeaway
The example of the prophets and the anecdote prove that sainthood does not exempt from obligations; exemption only comes through loss of intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel overburdened by religious duties, do you ever secretly wish for a 'saintly' exemption? How does the example of the prophets—who were the most obligated and yet the most loving—challenge that desire? What commitment can you make today to embrace an obligation you have been avoiding?
?
Consider the saint who asked for exemption and was given ignorance. If you were to ask Allah for a lighter burden, what would that reveal about the sincerity of your love for Him? Are you willing to sit with that discomfort and examine your heart?
?
The true gnostic never tires of worship. Do you tire? And if you do, what does that say about your current spiritual state? Will you take this to Allah in honest supplication, asking Him to increase your love so that service becomes rest?

Ruling on Those Who Claim Exemption from Obligations
Al-Ghazali's ruling on those who claim exemption, with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the serious ruling against anyone who claims that sainthood makes forbidden things permissible, including the obligation to kill such a person according to al-Ghazali.

Core Idea
Those who claim sainthood exempts from duties must be killed, even if their disbelief is debated.

The footnote from the original passage, attributed to al-Ghazali, addresses the practical consequences of the heretical claim. It states that anyone who believes that sainthood has freed him from obligations and made forbidden things lawful is to be killed without doubt, as his harm to the religion is greater than that of a hundred disbelievers. This lesson examines that ruling and its scriptural support.

Guided Path
1
Read the footnote passage
Read the Arabic from 'أما إن ظنَّ جاهل' to the end. Then read the translation. Note the strong language and the Quranic citation.
This is a separate comment but directly related to the main refutation.
2
Understand the ruling
Al-Ghazali says that if an ignorant person claims exemption, his killing is obligatory without doubt, although there is scholarly difference on his eternal fate. Killing him is better than killing a hundred disbelievers because of his greater harm to the religion.
3
See the Quranic support
The passage ends with a verse from Surah Maryam where Jesus says that prayer and zakah were enjoined upon him as long as he lives. This reinforces that even prophets are under lifelong obligation.
The verse directly counters the idea of exemption from obligations.

Misconception: Some think that if a person claims exemption due to sainthood, he should be left alone or considered a true saint.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali's ruling in the passage, what is the obligation regarding a person who thinks sainthood has made forbidden things permissible for him?
A) He should be counseled and educated.
B) He must be killed, and this is better than killing a hundred disbelievers.
C) He is to be excommunicated but not killed.
D) He is considered a true saint and left alone.

Key Takeaway
Claiming that sainthood exempts from obligations and permits the forbidden is such a grave harm that it warrants the death penalty, as per al-Ghazali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed a personal spiritual experience to make you lax in an obligation you know Allah has commanded? Will you commit today to never let that happen again?
?
If you encountered a Muslim who claimed that their closeness to Allah exempted them from the salah or zakah, would you have the courage to confront them with al-Ghazali's ruling, or would you remain silent out of fear of being harsh?
?
Your own soul: is there any forbidden thing you have begun to view as permissible because you feel 'spiritual' or 'sincere'? How does Jesus's example of lifelong prayer and zakah challenge that excuse?

Superiority of Prophets over Awliya and the State of Annihilation
Taftazani argues for prophets' superiority over awliya and explains the state of 'dehool'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets are superior to saints (awliya) even though saints may experience powerful spiritual states, and how the state of 'dehool' (annihilation) relates to this hierarchy.

Core Idea
Prophets are superior because their spiritual absorption never prevents them from fulfilling obligations.

This passage from Taftazani addresses a delicate question: Can any saint ever equal or surpass a prophet? Taftazani argues decisively that prophets are superior, using both rational arguments and a striking example of a saint who was so overwhelmed by divine attraction that he sought exemption from obligations. Understanding this distinction clarifies the unique rank of prophethood and the proper place of mystical states like 'annihilation' (dehool).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation to get the overall flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the shift from definition to argument to anecdote to explanation.
2
Identify Taftazani's main argument
Look for why Taftazani says prophets are 'the most complete in love and sincerity' and why their heavier obligations actually prove their higher rank.
Contrast: heavier accountability yet they fulfill it perfectly.
3
Understand the story of the wali who sought exemption
Note how this wali was relieved of obligations by having his intellect removed. Reflect on why this shows a limitation, not a virtue.
The true 'arif does not ask for such removal.
4
Analyze the state of 'dehool'
Understand that this heedlessness is like sleep and results from inability to balance both worlds. It is a temporary weakness, not a perfection. This leads to the conclusion of prophethood's superiority.
Prophets never experience even a moment of such heedlessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا محالة؛ إذ لا معنى للولي إلا مُظهِرُ تصرُّفِ النبي في الخلْقِ بالحق. قال التفتازاني بعد أن ردَّ عليهم بإجماع المسلمين وعمـومِ الخطابات : ( ولأنَّ أكمل الناس في المحبة والإخلاص هم الأنبياء الصلاة والسلام ، سيَّما حبيب الله تعالى سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، مَعَ أَنَّ التكاليف في حقهم أتم وأكمل ، حتى إنَّهم يُعاتبونَ بأدنى زلَّةٍ ، بل بتركِ الأفضل عليهم ) نعم؛ حُكِيَ عن بعض الأولياء أنَّه استعفى الله تعالى عن التكاليف ، وسألَهُ الإعتاق عن ظواهر العباداتِ ، فأجابَهُ إلى ذلك ؛ بأن سلبه العقل الذي هو مناط التكليف ، ومع ذلكَ كَانَ مِنْ علوّ المرتبة على ما كانَ وأنت خبير بأنَّ العارف لا يسأمُ مِنَ العبادة ، ولا يفتر في الطاعة ، ولا يسألُ الهبوط مِنْ أوج الكمال إلى حضيض النقصانِ ، والنزولَ مِنْ معارج الملكِ إلى منازل الحيوانِ ، بل ربَّما يحصلُ لهُ كمالُ الانجذابِ إلى عالم القدس ، والاستغراق في ملاحظة جانب الحقِّ ، فيَذهَلُ عن هذا العالم ، ويُخِلُّ بالتكاليفِ مِنْ غيرِ تأثُم بذلكَ ؛ لكونه في حُكْمِ كالنائم ؛ وذلك لعجزه عن مراعاة الأمرين ، وملاحظة الجانبين ، فربَّما يسألُ دوام تلكَ الحالة ، وعدم العود إلى عالم ، وهذا الدُّهولُ هو الجنونُ الذي ربَّما يُرجحُ على بعضِ العقولِ [؟]، والمتسمَّونَ بهِ هُمُ المسمَّونَ بمجانين العقلاء وبهذا يظهرُ فضلُ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام على الأولياء ؛ فإنَّهم مع أنَّ استغراقهم أكمل ، وانجذابهم أشمل .. لا يُخِلُّونَ بأدنى طاعةٍ ، ولا يَذْهَلُونَ عن هذا الجانبِ ساعةٌ ؛ لأنَّ قوَّتَهمُ القدسيَّةَ مِنَ الكمال ، بحيثُ لا يشغلها شاغل عن ذلكَ الجناب ، ولهذا يُعاتبونَ على أدنى ذهول عن الأولى مِنْ مراتبِ الصواب
Inevitably; for there is no meaning of wali (saint) except as a manifester of the prophet's disposal in creation with truth. Al-Taftazani said after refuting them by the consensus of Muslims and the generality of addresses: 'And because the most complete people in love and sincerity are the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, especially the beloved of Allah, our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, while the obligations in their regard are more complete and perfect, such that they are rebuked for the slightest slip, even for leaving what is better.' Yes; it is narrated about some awliya that he sought exemption from Allah Almighty from obligations, and asked Him for freedom from outward acts of worship, and He answered him to that by stripping him of intellect which is the basis of obligation, and despite that he was of high rank as he was. And you are aware that the 'arif (gnostic) does not tire of worship, nor slacken in obedience, nor asks to descend from the peak of perfection to the abyss of deficiency, nor descend from the ascents of dominion to the stations of animals. Rather, sometimes he experiences complete attraction to the world of holiness and immersion in contemplating the side of Truth, so he becomes heedless of this world and neglects obligations without thereby sinning, because he is in the status of a sleeper; and that is due to his inability to observe both matters and attend to both sides. So perhaps he asks for the continuation of that state and not returning to a world. This heedlessness (al-duhul) is the insanity (al-junun) that sometimes outweighs some intellects [?], and those so described are called 'the sane madmen' (majaneen al-'uqala). And by this appears the superiority of the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, over the awliya; for indeed, although their immersion is greater and their attraction more comprehensive, they do not neglect the slightest act of obedience, nor are they heedless of this side for an hour, because their holy power is of such perfection that no distraction occupies them from that [divine] presence. For this reason they are rebuked for the slightest heedlessness from what is prior among the ranks of correctness.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument establishing the superiority of prophets over awliya. It begins by stating that a wali (saint) is only a manifestation of the prophet's authority in creation. Then it quotes al-Taftazani, who refutes those who might elevate awliya above prophets. Taftazani argues that prophets are the most perfect in love and sincerity, yet their obligations are heavier; they are even rebuked for minor slips or for not choosing the better option (tark al-afdal). This shows their higher station despite greater accountability. Then the author (likely Sanusi or Taftazani) relates a story of a wali who sought exemption from obligations, and was answered by having his intellect removed (since intellect is the basis of obligation), yet he remained in a high rank. This illustrates that some awliya may be relieved of obligations due to being overwhelmed. The author then explains that the true mystic ('arif) does not seek to abandon worship or descend in rank. However, at times he may experience complete attraction (istighraq) to the divine, leading to heedlessness of worldly obligations without sin, like a sleeper. This state (al-duhul) is a kind of insanity that may outweigh intellect in some people; they are called 'sane madmen' (majaneen al-'uqala). Finally, the passage shows the superiority of prophets: despite their greater spiritual absorption, they never neglect any duty or become heedless even for a moment, because their holy power is so perfect that nothing distracts them. Thus they are rebuked even for the slightest oversight from the optimal choice.

Key Terms
ولي
عارف
استغراق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that awliya can equal or surpass prophets in rank, or that the state of annihilation excuses permanent neglect of obligations.
Correction: This passage clarifies that prophets are superior and that such neglect in awliya is a temporary human weakness, not a virtue. The state of annihiliation is like sleep and does not indicate higher rank.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason for the superiority of prophets over awliya mentioned in this passage?
A) Prophets perform more miracles.
B) Prophets never become heedless of obligations even in the highest states of spiritual absorption.
C) Prophets have more followers.
D) Awliya are not beloved to Allah.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are superior to saints because their complete absorption in the Divine never interferes with their perfect observance of obligations, unlike saints who may temporarily become heedless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a 'spiritual mood' as an excuse to neglect your religious duties—prayer, charity, or helping others? How does the example of the prophets, who never let their complete absorption interfere with even the smallest obedience, expose this as a weakness in your own heart? What one obligation will you recommit to today, regardless of how you feel?
?
The wali sought exemption from obligations and was granted it by losing his intellect. In what areas of your life do you secretly wish to be excused from religious responsibilities because you feel 'too advanced' or 'too busy' with spiritual pursuits? How does this passage confront that desire as a descent from perfection to deficiency?
?
Prophets are rebuked for leaving what is better (tark al-afdal). Consider your own daily choices—when have you settled for 'good enough' instead of the best, thinking it wouldn't matter? If you were held to the standard of prophetic accountability, what 'better' action have you been neglecting that you will now commit to?
